# MASTER_QUEUE.md — Universal Salesforce Skill Build Queue

<!--
PURPOSE:
  Single source of truth for the full Role × Domain × Cloud skill matrix.
  This file drives the expanded vision: every SF role, every cloud, every task.

VISION:
  One public repo. Every Salesforce professional (Admin, BA, Dev, Data, Architect)
  drops it into Claude, Cursor, or any AI and gets role-appropriate, task-accurate
  Salesforce guidance grounded in official docs — not training data guesses.

AGENT INSTRUCTIONS (read before doing anything):
  1. Read CLAUDE.md and AGENT_RULES.md first. This file does not override them.
  2. Find the first row with status RESEARCHED (preferred) or TODO in the queue below.
  3. Change status to IN_PROGRESS and record your agent name + ISO timestamp in the Notes column.
  4. python3 scripts/search_knowledge.py "<skill-name>" --domain <domain>
       → If has_coverage: true, the skill exists. Mark DUPLICATE and move to next.
       → If has_coverage: false, proceed.
  5. Read official sources for this domain from standards/official-salesforce-sources.md BEFORE writing anything.
  6. python3 scripts/new_skill.py <domain> <skill-name>
  7. Fill every TODO marker in every generated file with real, doc-grounded content.
       SKILL.md body must be 300+ words. Include "NOT for ..." in description.
       Triggers must be 3+ natural-language symptom phrases, 10+ chars each.
  8. python3 scripts/skill_sync.py --skill skills/<domain>/<skill-name>
       Fix every ERROR before continuing. Do not use --skip-validation.
  9. Add query fixture to vector_index/query-fixtures.json.
       Run python3 scripts/search_knowledge.py "<query>" and confirm skill appears in top 3.
  10. python3 scripts/validate_repo.py → must exit 0.
  11. Mark row DONE. Commit: skill package + registry/ + vector_index/ + docs/SKILLS.md.
  12. Move to the next TODO row.

STATUS KEY:
  TODO        → Not started. Needs research before building.
  RESEARCHED  → Deep research done, notes in Notes column. Ready to build next session.
  IN_PROGRESS → Being built or researched. Do not touch — another agent is working on it.
  DONE        → Complete. validate_repo.py passes. Committed.
  DUPLICATE   → Skill already exists. Skipped.
  BLOCKED     → Stopped. Read Notes before continuing.
-->

---

## Execution Order

Build phases sequentially. Within each phase, build roles in this order:
**Admin → BA → Dev → Data → Architect**

Reason: Admin defines the data model and configuration that Dev and Architect skills
reference. BA skills assume Admin config exists. Data skills assume Dev patterns exist.
Architect skills synthesize all of the above.

Phase 0 (domain sweeps) builds before all cloud phases because cross-cloud skills
are prerequisites for cloud-specific skills.

---

## Phase 0 — Domain Sweeps (Cross-Cloud)

These skills apply across all clouds. Build before cloud-specific phases.

Key: 3 manifest variants — Pre.xml (deletions before additions), plain destructiveChanges.xml (same), Post.xml (after additions — required when deleted component still referenced); sf CLI --pre-destructive-changes/--post-destructive-changes flags; undeletable via API: Record Types, Picklist values, active Flow versions. |
| DONE | continuous-integration-testing | Running Apex tests in CI: code coverage gates, parallel test execution, test result parsing, selective test runs. NOT for writing test classes (use test-class-standards). | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [SF CLI Command Ref apex commands; Apex Dev Guide code coverage, testing best practices; Metadata API deploy subset tests]. Key: RunLocalTests=75% org-wide, RunSpecifiedTests=75% per-class/trigger in package (stricter); --code-coverage collects but does not enforce threshold; --result-format junit for CI report ingestion; known bug: --code-coverage+--wait returns 0% (poll with sf apex get test instead); @isTest(isParallel=true) opts class into parallel. |

Key: `orgPreferences` deprecated since Winter '20 — use `settings` instead; Org Shape (Enterprise+ Dev Hub only) excludes some features (MultiCurrency, PersonAccounts) that must still be declared explicitly; `--release` flag pins preview vs. current release; distinct from scratch-org-management which covers lifecycle/CI — this skill covers schema depth of the def file itself. |
| DONE | git-branching-for-salesforce | Branching models for SF projects: feature branches, release branches, org-based vs artifact-based development alignment. NOT for Git basics. | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-04. |
| DONE | post-deployment-validation | Post-deploy smoke tests, validation deploy vs quick deploy, monitoring after deployment, rollback triggers. NOT for pre-deployment planning. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Metadata API Dev Guide — deployRecentValidation SOAP+REST, deploy monitoring; SF CLI ref — project deploy validate/quick/resume]. Key: validation deploy = checkOnly:true, earns qualified validation ID; quick deploy = POST to validatedDeployRequestId, skips tests, valid for 10 days, returns NEW deploy ID; rollback = re-deploy prior version (no native undo); RunSpecifiedTests requires 75% per-class in package (stricter than RunLocalTests); Deployment Status page shows per-test drill-down during/after deploy. |
| DONE | vscode-salesforce-extensions | VS Code for Salesforce: extension pack setup, Apex LSP, deploying from editor, code completion, debugging integration. NOT for CLI commands. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Salesforce Extensions for VS Code docs — Installation, Apex Language Server, Deploy on Save, Development Models; developer.salesforce.com]. Key: Apex LSP requires JDK 21 (recommended) or 11/17 and activates only when sfdx-project.json is the top-level folder; deploy-on-save differs by org type — source-tracked orgs trigger project:deploy:start, non-tracked orgs trigger force:source:deploy; two debugger options — Apex Interactive Debugger (live, requires license) vs Apex Replay Debugger (replays captured debug log, no license). |
| DONE | migration-from-change-sets-to-sfdx | Transitioning from change set deployment to SFDX source-driven development: org conversion, team onboarding. NOT for greenfield SFDX setup. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Salesforce DX Developer Guide — Migrate Existing Source; sf project convert mdapi]. Key: canonical path is retrieve via Metadata API then convert format with sf project convert mdapi; incremental component-by-component conversion recommended to preserve git history; no duplicate — adjacent skills cover CLI/source-tracking prereqs but not the migration workflow. |
| DONE | deployment-error-troubleshooting | Common deployment errors: dependency resolution, component validation failures, API version mismatches, test failures. NOT for Apex runtime errors. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Metadata API Dev Guide — DeployMessage/DeployDetails; help.salesforce.com Troubleshoot Deployment Failures; help.salesforce.com Dependent class is invalid; Salesforce CLI Troubleshooting Guide]. Key: DeployMessage.componentFailures is the canonical error surface (not top-level errorStatusCode); dependency errors from missing transitive dependencies or pre-broken classes in target; rollbackOnError defaults false for sandboxes (partial deploy risk); RunSpecifiedTests uses per-class 75% (stricter than RunLocalTests org-wide 75%); API version mismatch shows as UNSUPPORTED_API_VERSION or metadata XML shape differences. |
| DONE | salesforce-dx-project-structure | sfdx-project.json configuration: source paths, package directories, namespace, API version, plugin configuration. NOT for CLI commands. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Salesforce DX Developer Guide — sfdx_dev_ws_config, sfdx_dev_ws_mpd, unlocked pkg config file; developer.salesforce.com DX guide]. Key: sfdx-project.json is the root config file — must have packageDirectories (array, at least 1 path), sourceApiVersion (string e.g. "62.0"), namespace (optional, blank for unlocked); packageDirectories entry can have: path, default (bool), package (string), versionName, versionNumber (major.minor.patch.NEXT); multiple dirs enable multi-package mono-repo; plugins section enables SFDX plugin config; sourceApiVersion must match a deployed API version or deploy rejects with UNSUPPORTED_API_VERSION; sfdxAuthUrl and sandbox credentials must never be committed here. No duplicate. |
| DONE | scratch-org-pools | Automating scratch org creation pools for CI: CumulusCI pool management, prebuilt orgs, parallel test execution. NOT for single org creation. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [CumulusCI Docs — Manage Scratch Orgs (cumulusci.readthedocs.io/en/latest/scratch-orgs.html); Salesforce DX Dev Guide — Scratch Org Editions and Allocations]. Key: No native sf CLI pool support — CumulusCI is the canonical pool manager; `cci org scratch_pool` command pre-creates orgs saved to CumulusCI keychain; each pooled org counts against Dev Hub active-org limit AND daily creation limit (daily limit varies by edition: Developer Hub 6/day, Scratch Org Add-On increases); pool use case = parallel CI matrix jobs each claim a pre-warmed org instead of creating fresh; orgs automatically initialized on first use; pools do NOT share data state — each is a clean scratch org with metadata installed; distinct from scratch-org-management (lifecycle/CLI commands) and data-seeding-for-testing (data loading). No duplicate. |
| DONE | metadata-coverage-and-dependencies | Tracking metadata dependencies: impact analysis before deployment, dependency graphs, metadata coverage report. NOT for package.xml generation. | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-05. |
| DONE | automated-regression-testing | End-to-end testing with Provar/Selenium: regression suites for Salesforce, test automation strategy, UI test patterns. NOT for Apex unit testing. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [UTAM Dev Guide, SF Dev Blog (Selenium/UTAM), Trailhead (Provar), LWC Shadow DOM docs]. Key: Shadow DOM breaks standard Selenium locators — UTAM (727+ page objects) is SF's official E2E framework; Provar is the metadata-aware commercial leader; tri-annual releases mandate pre-release regression windows. |
| DONE | rollback-and-hotfix-strategy | Rollback planning: hotfix deployment procedures, emergency change processes, safe rollback patterns. NOT for release planning. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Metadata API Dev Guide — deployRecentValidation SOAP+REST; SF CLI ref — project deploy start/validate/resume; help.salesforce.com Troubleshoot Deployment Failures; developer.salesforce.com blog — Hotfix in Salesforce CI/CD]. Key: Salesforce has no native metadata rollback — rollback = re-deploy previous version of the affected components; pre-deploy archive pattern: retrieve current production state of each component being deployed and store as a "rollback bundle"; quick deploy (validatedDeployRequestId) can be used to fast-path hotfixes; hotfix branch = minimal change targeting a single defect, deployed to hotfix sandbox → UAT → production; rollback timing window matters — if subsequent deploys have run, the rollback bundle may conflict; non-rollbackable components: Record Types, Picklist values, active Flow versions (cannot redeploy deleted version); distinct from release-management (which covers planning) and post-deployment-validation (which covers smoke tests) — this skill covers the emergency response and pre-deploy archive discipline. No duplicate. |
| DONE | salesforce-devops-tooling-selection | Comparing DevOps tools (Gearset, Copado, Flosum, AutoRABIT, native SFDX): selection criteria, feature comparison. NOT for implementing any specific tool. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Help (DevOps Center), SF Dev Blog, Gearset/Copado/Flosum comparisons]. Key: 6 contenders — Gearset (SaaS, fastest), Copado (managed pkg, ALM), Flosum (native), AutoRABIT (all-in-one), Blue Canvas (Git-native), DevOps Center (free, native); selection axes = hosting model, team composition, compliance, budget. |
| DONE | pre-deployment-checklist | Pre-deploy validation steps: metadata review, test execution requirements, backup procedures, dependency verification. NOT for post-deployment. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Deployment Best Practices (platform.deploy_best_practices.htm); developer.salesforce.com blog — Master Metadata API Deployments with Best Practices (Oct 2025); Metadata API Dev Guide — deploy + checkOnly option; SF CLI Ref — sf project deploy validate]. Key: Validation deploy = `checkOnly: true` — zero-save test run that earns a validated deploy ID redeemable for 10-day quick deploy window; canonical pre-deploy gates: run validation deploy in UAT/staging → confirm Apex test pass ≥75% → check MetadataComponentDependency for missing transitive deps → check Trust site for maintenance windows → schedule off-peak; break large deployments into small logical units to isolate failures; backup = retrieve current production state of changed components BEFORE deploying; `sf project deploy validate` is the CLI command (generates validatedDeployRequestId for quick deploy); RunSpecifiedTests stricter (75% per class in package) than RunLocalTests (75% org-wide); distinct from post-deployment-validation (smoke tests after deploy) and go-live-cutover-planning (full cutover sequence). No duplicate. |
| DONE | go-live-cutover-planning | Go-live cutover planning: deployment sequencing, code freeze procedures, mock deployments, go/no-go checklists, rollback triggers, hypercare support model, smoke testing. NOT for deployment mechanics (use post-deployment-validation). | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Salesforce Architecture Center — Go-Live Checklist; help.salesforce.com Deploy to Production; architect.salesforce.com Well-Architected — Operational Excellence; Trailhead — Prepare Your Org for a Successful Go-Live]. Key: Salesforce go-live has 3 windows — validation deploy (1-7 days before), quick deploy (10-day window after validation), and cutover execution (within quick deploy window); code freeze = Salesforce metadata locked in source control; mock deployment = full validation deploy run in production equivalent sandbox to confirm timing; go/no-go criteria: all Apex tests pass at 75%+, validation deploy approved, UAT sign-off, business stakeholders confirmed; hypercare = defined support schedule for first 2 weeks post-go-live; cutover execution sequence: activate flows, deploy metadata, run smoke tests, confirm with business; rollback trigger conditions must be defined in advance; distinct from post-deployment-validation (which covers smoke test mechanics) and release-management (which covers the planning phase). No duplicate. |
| DONE | performance-testing-salesforce | Performance testing for Salesforce: load testing approaches, concurrent user simulation, API throughput benchmarks, LWC rendering performance, governor limit headroom analysis. NOT for Apex code optimization (use apex-cpu-and-heap-optimization). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Help (Scale Test FAQs), SF Dev Blog (Load Test Using Scalability Tools 2025, Performance Testing series), Trailhead (Scale Test, EPT optimization)]. Key: Scale Test is first-party load testing against Full Copy sandboxes; EPT target <3s; concurrent API limit applies only to requests >20s; JMeter/BlazeMeter/k6 for API load testing. |
| DONE | multi-package-development | Managing multiple packages in one project: inter-package dependencies, deployment ordering, namespace strategy. NOT for single package development. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF DX Dev Guide (MPD, pkg config, best practices), SF Architects (5 dependency anti-patterns), SF Dev Blog (modular dev parts 2-3), Trailhead (organize metadata)]. Key: Covers cross-package orchestration (dependency DAG, layered architecture, install ordering, mono/multi-repo) complementing existing single-package skills; no duplicate. |
| DONE | api-version-management | Managing API versions across metadata: deprecation tracking, upgrade planning, version alignment across components. NOT for REST API usage. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Developer Docs (API End-of-Life Policy, Metadata API Support Policy), SF CLI Setup Guide, SF Dev Blog (API Retirement Tools Oct 2024, LWC Component Versioning Jan 2024)]. Key: 3-layer version drift risk — transport API vs sourceApiVersion vs per-component apiVersion; versions 7.0-30.0 retired; ApiTotalUsage event logs detect deprecated usage; LWC requires explicit apiVersion in .js-meta.xml from Spring '25. |
| DONE | org-cleanup-and-technical-debt | Identifying unused metadata: removing deprecated components, org health maintenance, dead code detection. NOT for code-level refactoring. | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-05. |
| DONE | copado-essentials | Copado deployment pipelines: user stories, branch management, conflict resolution, promotion paths. NOT for native SFDX CLI workflows. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Copado Docs — User Story and User Story Tasks; Copado Docs — Pipeline Configuration; Copado Docs — Branch Management; Copado Essentials Help Center — Essentials Plus Setup Guide]. Key: Copado Essentials is a free-tier Salesforce-native DevOps platform; user stories link to Git feature branches named feature/{user-story-number}; two deployment modes — Work Items (in-app approvals + conflict resolution) and Deployments with Pull Requests (Git-native PRs); pipelines require one Git branch per org; merge order override required when default ascending User Story Reference order causes dependency issues. No duplicate. |
| DONE | cumulusci-automation | CumulusCI for Salesforce development: task and flow configuration, robot framework integration, CI automation. NOT for native SFDX. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [CumulusCI Key Concepts v4.8.1; cumulusci.yml Structure docs; CumulusCI Flow docs; Robot Framework acceptance testing; Trailhead — Tasks and Flows]. Key: CumulusCI is open-source Python framework; core authoring unit is cumulusci.yml declaring tasks (class_path + options), flows (ordered steps), orgs (scratch org shape), and sources (cross-project reuse); standard flows include dev_org, qa_org, install_beta; Robot Framework acceptance tests via robot task; CI via cci flow run with JWT auth. No duplicate. |
| DONE | metadata-api-coverage-gaps | Metadata types not supported by Metadata API or SFDX: manual migration workarounds, known coverage gaps by release, tracking unsupported components. NOT for Metadata API usage (use metadata-api-and-package-xml). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Metadata API Dev Guide — Unsupported Metadata Types; developer.salesforce.com/docs/metadata-coverage; Metadata API Support Policy; SF Dev Blog Oct 2025]. Key: Official Unsupported Metadata Types page in Metadata API Dev Guide; Coverage Report tracks ~873+ types; v66 (Spring 26) last version retiring Winter 27; canonical unsupported examples: ForecastingSettings, OrgPreferenceSettings (removed v48), active Flow versions, some Industry Cloud setup types; workaround = manual per-org configuration documented in release runbooks. No duplicate. |
| DONE | environment-specific-value-injection | Managing environment-specific values across orgs: Named Credential per-env config, Custom Metadata for env settings, post-deploy scripts, CI variable substitution. NOT for sandbox refresh (use sandbox-refresh-and-templates). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Named Credentials Dev Guide, Metadata API Dev Guide, SF DX Dev Guide (String Replacements), Custom Metadata Types Help]. Key: 4 mechanisms — Named Credentials (secrets stay per-org), Custom Metadata (deployable config), sfdx-project.json replaceWithEnv (CI substitution), post-deploy scripts (Connect REST for credential population); secrets never in source control. |
| DONE | sandbox-data-isolation-gotchas | Sandbox data pitfalls: production data leaking into sandbox emails, scheduled jobs running in sandboxes, integration endpoints hitting production, post-copy cleanup. NOT for sandbox strategy (use sandbox-strategy). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Help (Sandbox Email Deliverability, Setup Considerations), Apex Ref Guide (SandboxPostCopy Interface), SF Release Notes]. Key: ~60-70% overlap with sandbox-refresh-and-templates and sandbox-data-masking; Contact/Lead emails NOT modified on refresh (only user emails get .invalid); SandboxPostCopy runs as Automated Process user with limited perms; recommend narrow pre-flight checklist scope. |

Key: 4 classification attributes on every field (SecurityClassification, ComplianceGroup, BusinessOwnerId, BusinessStatus); Metadata API deployable since API v46.0; queryable via Tooling API FieldDefinition; classification is metadata-only — no runtime enforcement; Einstein Data Detect (Shield) auto-populates recommendations; ComplianceGroup not updatable via Tooling API (known gap); distinct from data-quality-and-governance which mentions GDPR erasure. |
| DONE | gdpr-data-privacy | Right to erasure implementation: data subject requests, consent management, data retention policies, individual rights. NOT for general data quality. | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Individual object, Privacy Center, Right to Be Forgotten, consent management objects/fields]. Key: Individual sObject (API v42) links to Contact/Lead/PersonAccount via IndividualId; ShouldForget=true is a flag only — no automated deletion; Privacy Center (separately licensed) provides RTBF policy engine and data portability; native consent model uses ContactPointTypeConsent + ContactPointConsent objects; no automated retention enforcement without Privacy Center or custom Batch Apex; anonymization (tokenization) recommended over hard delete for referential integrity. |

| DONE | experience-cloud-security | External user security: sharing sets, external org-wide defaults, community security best practices, portal security. Key: External OWD is independent of internal OWD and must be equal or more restrictive; Sharing Sets grant access via lookup field relationship (not role hierarchy), Guest users excluded; Secure Guest User Record Access toggle forces all-private OWD for guests; Share Groups allow portal users to share among themselves; CSP/clickjack/LWS are site-level toggles. |

Key: IP Relaxation has 3 values with distinct security postures (Enforce/Relax with 2FA/Relax); PKCE requires disabling Require Secret for Web Server Flow; JWT Bearer clock drift of 60s causes invalid_grant; High-assurance has 3 states (default/Switch/Blocked); client secret rotation has NO grace period — staged ECA model (v65) promotes instantly. |

| DONE | xss-and-injection-prevention | XSS prevention in Visualforce and Apex: output encoding, Locker Service, CRLF injection, open redirect prevention. NOT for Apex CRUD/FLS enforcement. | Researched 2026-04-04. Key: Visualforce auto-escapes {!field} in HTML context but NOT inside JavaScript — use JSENCODE() in JS blocks; HTMLENCODE/JSINHTMLENCODE/URLENCODE/HTMLENCODINGMAP are the four VF encoding functions; Locker Service isolates LWC DOM from third-party components but is NOT a substitute for server-side encoding in Apex strings; SOQL injection prevention = bind variables only (never string concatenation in dynamic SOQL); CRLF injection prevented by rejecting \r\n in user-supplied HTTP header values; open redirect prevention = whitelist allowed domains on PageReference targets; Content Security Policy headers configurable per site for Experience Cloud. No duplicate. DONE 2026-04-04 |
| DONE | secure-coding-review-checklist | Security review checklist for AppExchange: ISV security requirements, Checkmarx patterns, common vulnerabilities. NOT for implementing fixes. | Researched 2026-04-04. Key: #1 failure = CRUD/FLS enforcement gaps — check every SOQL query and DML for WITH USER_MODE or explicit stripInaccessible; required scans: Salesforce Code Analyzer (PMD rules) + Source Code Scanner (Checkmarx — partner portal only) + ZAP for web security; Checkmarx common hits: CRUD/FLS, SOQL injection, stored XSS via User/Contact fields, open redirect via PageReference; periodic re-reviews required for AppExchange listings; Security Policy doc required (company commitment to security program); 3 submission paths: automated, manual, or partner portal submission; test credentials required for review team; timing: allow 4-8 weeks for initial review; no duplicate. |

| DONE | session-management-and-timeout | Session security: timeout configuration by user type, concurrent session limits, session-level IP locking, logout messaging, inactivity handling, CMS ARC-AMPE session controls. Key: Session timeout configured at 3 levels: org-wide (Setup > Session Settings > Timeout Value), Connected App-level (OAuth Policies > Session Timeout), Profile-level (Profile > Session Settings); effective timeout = minimum of all applicable levels; concurrent session limits per user: configurable 1-20 simultaneous sessions (default unlimited); session IP locking = Sessions tied to IP address at creation, new IP triggers re-auth; Extended Session Management (Lightning) vs Classic Session Mgmt have different behaviors; Logout URL configurable per Connected App for branded logout; timeout values in Metadata API SecuritySettings: TwoHours/FourHours/EightHours/TwelveHours/TwentyFourHours enum; no duplicate (api-security-and-rate-limiting touches timeout at Connected App level only; login-forensics covers session forensics; this skill covers the full session lifecycle configuration). |

Key: @RestResource + @HttpPost is the primary inbound webhook surface; unauthenticated webhooks require a Salesforce Site (Force.com site) with guest profile access to the Apex class; authenticated webhooks use OAuth Client Credentials flow with integration user + connected app; idempotency = check for duplicate via External ID field before processing (UPSERT pattern); HMAC signature verification done in Apex: compute HMAC-SHA256 of raw body with shared secret, compare to X-Signature header in constant-time comparison; response must be 200 with 5s timeout window or sender retries; async handling = enqueue Queueable from @HttpPost so callout ACK is fast; distinct from apex/apex-rest-services (which covers @RestResource design patterns generically — webhook-inbound adds site routing + HMAC + idempotency). NOT for HTTP implementation details. | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — apex_callouts_timeouts, apex_gov_limits, apex_continuation_limits; Apex Ref Guide — Continuation class; SF App Limits Quick Reference — apexgov]. Key: Synchronous callout limits: 100 callouts/transaction, 120s timeout per callout, 10MB response body; Continuation: max timeout 120s, max 3 requests/continuation, max 3 continuations chained = 360s total wait (new Apex transaction each callback, limits reset); Queueable callout: async context gets same 100 callout limit, timeout still 120s per callout; DML-before-callout rule — callout after uncommitted DML throws System.CalloutException; fix = Queueable with callout=true; @future(callout=true) is simple but no chaining; Queueable enables chaining via System.enqueueJob in execute(); Continuation supported in LWC/Aura/VF controllers only (not triggers or batch); no duplicate (continuation-callouts covers the Continuation class specifically; this skill covers the decision layer across all async callout patterns). |

NOT for Salesforce Files administration. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [SF Help (Files Connect, File Size Limits, EDM for Contracts), SF Developer Docs (ContentVersion Object Ref, REST API Blob Insert, ExternalDocStorageConfig), SF Architects (Async Processing)]. Key: ContentVersion is primary upload sObject; REST multipart up to 2 GB; SF has NO built-in virus scanning for CRM uploads — must implement via callout; Files Connect = read external files in SF (not store SF files externally); EDM = store SF-generated docs externally (Industries CLM). |
| DUPLICATE | stub-and-mock-testing-patterns | Integration stub testing: mock endpoints for sandbox environments, HttpCalloutMock in Apex, stub response configuration, test isolation for callouts, partner connectivity testing. NOT for Apex unit testing patterns (use test-class-standards). | Covered by skills/apex/apex-mocking-and-stubs — HttpCalloutMock, StaticResourceCalloutMock, StubProvider, and seam-based test isolation all present. |
| DONE | api-error-handling-design | API error response design: HTTP status code strategy, error payload structure, retry-safe error codes, client-side error parsing, timeout handling, circuit breaker patterns. NOT for Apex exception handling. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [REST API Dev Guide, Salesforce Architects Integration Patterns, Marketing Cloud Rate Limiting]. Key: High overlap with retry-and-backoff-patterns (circuit breaker) and apex-rest-services (error payload design); unique gap is narrow — client-side error classification and RFC 7807 envelope design. Consider merging scope into existing skills instead of standalone. |
| DONE | retry-and-backoff-patterns | Integration retry strategies: exponential backoff, jitter, retry budget, idempotency keys, dead-letter queues, circuit breaker implementation in Apex callouts. NOT for Apex async retry (use apex-queueable-patterns). | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — apex_callouts_timeouts, apex_gov_limits Queueable Callout; help.salesforce.com — Platform Events replay, Outbound Messages retry; developer.salesforce.com blog — Resilient Integrations; AWS architecture patterns — exponential backoff with jitter]. Key: Apex callout retry cannot use Thread.sleep() — use Queueable chaining to implement delay (each enqueue = async execution, not immediate); exponential backoff formula: delay = baseDelay * 2^retryCount with +jitter (Math.random() * baseDelay); jitter prevents thundering-herd from concurrent retry storms; idempotency key = External_Id__c upsert prevents duplicate processing on retry; Retry__c counter field tracks attempts — max retry guard prevents infinite loops; dead-letter pattern: after maxRetries exceeded, write a Failed_Integration_Log__c record for manual review; circuit breaker in Apex = custom metadata flag (Circuit_Breaker_Config__c) checked before callout; outbound messages auto-retry up to 24 hours at increasing intervals natively; Platform Events replay up to 3 days; distinct from callout-limits-and-async-patterns (limits and continuation) and apex-queueable-patterns (generic queueable). No duplicate. |
| DONE | sis-integration-patterns | Student Information System integration with Salesforce: enrollment sync, transcript data, financial aid, advisor assignment, EDA/Education Cloud data mapping. NOT for generic integration patterns. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Education Cloud Developer Guide v66.0 — knowledge/imports/edu-cloud-dev-guide.md; developer.salesforce.com Education Cloud Data Model Overview; salesforce.com Next-Gen SIS; Lingk SIS Migration Guide]. Key: Key objects: AcademicTermEnrollment, CourseOfferingParticipant, LearnerProfile, CourseOfferingPtcpResult (grades), PersonAcademicCredential; Education Cloud Business APIs at /connect/education/academic-operations/ (v64+); primary patterns: batch nightly upsert keyed on Banner PIDM/PeopleSoft EMPLID, CDC for enrollment status writeback, MuleSoft Object Store watermarks; SIS platforms: Banner, Colleague, Anthology, PeopleSoft, Workday Student. No duplicate. |

## Phase 1 — Core Platform (Foundation)

Core Platform skills apply across all clouds. Build these first.
Every skill here should work regardless of which Salesforce cloud the org has licensed.

| DONE | user-access-policies | User Access Policies: automatic permission set assignment based on user attributes, provisioning rules, dynamic group membership, login-based license management. Key: User Access Policies (UAP) became GA in release 242; enhanced filter support in release 246; UAP automatically grants OR revokes permission sets and permission set groups based on user field criteria (Profile, Role, UserType, Department, custom fields); policy runs on user Create and on any qualifying user-field Update — no Apex required; UAP evaluation order matters — grant policies evaluated before revoke policies; policies can reference standard and custom user fields as filter criteria; login-based license management is partially covered by UAP (can assign/revoke PSL via UAP); distinct from permission-set-architecture (design patterns) and delegated-administration (delegated user management). | DONE | batch-job-scheduling-and-monitoring | Monitoring scheduled and batch jobs: Apex Jobs monitoring, Flow scheduled jobs, job queue management, concurrent limits, failure notification, retry patterns. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — apex_scheduler, apex_batch_interface, apex_gov_limits scheduled; help.salesforce.com — Monitor Apex Jobs, Manage Your Apex Jobs; REST API — AsyncApexJob]. Key: Setup > Apex Jobs shows AsyncApexJob records for all Batch, Scheduled, Queueable, and Future jobs; AsyncApexJob queryable via SOQL: SELECT Status, NumberOfErrors, CompletedDate FROM AsyncApexJob WHERE JobType='BatchApex'; scheduled jobs viewable in Setup > Scheduled Jobs — shows next fire time, cron expression, and user context; org-wide limit: 5 concurrent Batch Apex jobs; 100 scheduled Apex jobs; concurrent Batch Apex limit can be increased via support case for Enterprise+; Flow scheduled jobs appear in Setup > Scheduled Jobs as "Schedule-Triggered Flow Interview" — not in Apex Jobs; failure notification: Batch finish() method should explicitly check error counts and notify; no native email on job failure by default — must implement; retry for Batch = re-execute the batch class; Scheduled Apex auto-reschedules on failure (fires again at next scheduled time, not immediately retried); distinct from apex-scheduled-jobs (covers Schedulable interface implementation) and batch-apex-patterns (covers batch Apex authoring). No duplicate. |
| DONE | standard-object-quirks | Non-obvious behaviors of standard objects: Task/Event polymorphic WhoId/WhatId, Lead conversion field mapping gotchas, Account/Contact deletion cascades, Person Account dual-nature, Case comment quirks. NOT for object creation (use object-creation-and-design). | Researched 2026-04-04. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — sObject Types, polymorphic lookups; help.salesforce.com — Lead Conversion Field Mapping, PersonAccounts, Cases and Related Object Behavior; Salesforce Object Reference — Task, Event, CaseComment, Case]. Key: WhoId polymorphic = Contact or Lead; WhatId polymorphic = any of 20+ standard objects; both are not queryable in same SOQL relationship query without separate queries; Lead conversion: maps Lead fields to Contact/Account/Opportunity via lead field mapping setup — unmapped custom fields are lost; Account deletion does not cascade delete Contacts (unlinks instead) unless Contact has no other relationships; PersonAccount is simultaneously an Account AND Contact record (single sObject with dual-nature); CaseComment is a child object that does not fire standard triggers on Case — only its own triggers; Task completion date is not same as ActivityDate; Event EndDateTime required when creating programmatically even though UI shows Duration; Person Account SOQL must use PersonEmail not Email; no duplicate (data-model-documentation covers schema documentation; this skill covers runtime behavioral gotchas). |
| DONE | picklist-field-integrity-issues | Picklist data integrity: unrestricted vs restricted picklists, values loaded via API bypassing picklist validation, record type picklist mapping drift, dependent picklist loading order. NOT for picklist setup (use picklist-and-value-sets). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Salesforce Help (Picklist Limitations, Known Issues), Metadata API Guide, UI API Guide]. Key: Unrestricted picklists silently accept any API value; dependent picklist enforcement is UI-only; record type mapping drift requires manual audit — all gaps the existing picklist-and-value-sets skill does not cover. |
| DONE | record-type-strategy-at-scale | Record type design patterns at scale: page layout explosion prevention, business process alignment, record type ID dependencies, migration between record types, sharing implications. NOT for basic record type setup (use record-types-and-page-layouts). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [architect.salesforce.com Decision Guides — Build Forms; Metadata API Dev Guide — RecordType metadata type (meta_recordtype.htm); developer.salesforce.com — Assign Record Types and Page Layouts in Profiles (Security Guide)]. Key: Page layout explosion = N record types × M profiles = N×M layout assignments — grows quadratically; Dynamic Forms (Lightning App Builder field visibility filters) breaks the N×M problem by replacing layout-per-record-type with component visibility rules on a single layout; RecordType metadata XML includes BusinessProcess reference, compactLayoutAssignment, picklistValues overrides; Record Type ID is NOT stable across orgs — never hardcode; canonical pattern is Schema.SObjectType.Account.getRecordTypeInfosByDeveloperName() for ID resolution; migration between record types via DataLoader/Bulk API update of RecordTypeId + DataPack redeployment of picklist values; Dynamic Forms not available for all objects (check compatibility before migrating); no overlap with record-types-and-page-layouts (which covers basic setup). No duplicate. |
| DONE | salesforce-release-preparation | Preparing for Salesforce seasonal releases: sandbox preview, release notes review, regression testing, feature deprecation tracking, org readiness assessment, critical update management. NOT for deployment mechanics. | Researched 2026-04-05. Key: Sandbox preview opens ~4-6 weeks before production upgrade with explicit per-sandbox opt-in; Release Updates at Setup > Release Updates toggle on/off until enforcement date; use Feature Impact filter in release notes for admin triage; partially overlaps release-management but focuses on admin-centric Release Updates management, release notes triage, and stakeholder communication. No duplicate. |
| DONE | org-limits-monitoring | Monitoring org-level limits: API call usage, storage consumption, custom object count, field-per-object limits, automation limits, setup audit trail, limit alert patterns. NOT for governor limits in Apex (use limits-and-scalability-planning). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Ref Guide — OrgLimits Class (apex_class_System_OrgLimits.htm); REST API Dev Guide — Limits resource (resources_limits.htm); developer.salesforce.com blog — API Limits and Monitoring Your API Usage (Nov 2024); help.salesforce.com — Proactive Alert Monitoring: API Request Limit (000382493); help.salesforce.com — Analyze Total API Requests Consumption (000385367)]. Key: Three monitoring surfaces: (1) Apex `OrgLimits.getAll()` returns Map<String,OrgLimit> with .getMax()/.getValue() per limit name; (2) REST `GET /services/data/vXX.0/limits` returns JSON map — data accurate within 5 min; (3) Setup > Company Information for storage + license counts; key limit names: DailyApiRequests, DataStorageMB, FileStorageMB, DailyBulkApiBatches, ActiveScratchOrgs, ConcurrentAsyncGetReportInstances; proactive alerting = scheduled Apex polling OrgLimits + Platform Event or email when threshold exceeded (e.g., >80% of DailyApiRequests); Event Log Files (API event type) for historical API call analysis; Setup Audit Trail for configuration change history; distinct from limits-and-scalability-planning (architecture-level capacity planning) and api-security-and-rate-limiting (Connected App throttling). No duplicate. |
| DONE | salesforce-support-escalation | Navigating Salesforce support: case severity levels, known issue tracking, Trailblazer Community resources, partner support tiers, Trust site monitoring, escalation paths. NOT for Service Cloud case management. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Severity Level Descriptions (000382814), Escalate Case to Technical Support Management (000386150), Known Issues Site (000386216), Trust Site (000387502), Incident Trust Communications (000389335); trust.salesforce.com Status User Guide; Salesforce Success Plans page; Trailhead — Critical Incident Management]. Key: 4 severity levels (Sev1=business down, Sev2=major broken, Sev3=workaround exists, Sev4=cosmetic); Premier SLA = 1-2h for Sev2 24/7; escalation path: in-case Escalate button -> Success Manager; Known Issues at help.salesforce.com/s/issues; distinct from admin/escalation-rules (declarative platform rules). No duplicate. |
| DONE | lightning-page-performance-tuning | Lightning page performance: component count limits, lazy loading, conditional visibility for heavy components, page load analysis, Lightning Usage App metrics. NOT for LWC component performance (use lwc-performance). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Help - Lightning Page Performance; Designing Lightning Pages for Scale - developer.salesforce.com blog; Lightning Experience Insights - help.salesforce.com]. Key: No hard component count limit but SF flags pages with unusually high component counts as slow in Lightning Experience Insights; primary performance pattern is progressive disclosure - place secondary components in tabs (skip DOM and XHR on initial load) and use conditional rendering (if:true) to defer heavy components, with tests showing tab-deferral of 8 components saving 0.4s and 7 XHR calls. Lightning Usage App (now Lightning Experience Insights) tracks EPT (Experienced Page Time) at P75 percentile, distinguishes first vs subsequent page load EPT, and surfaces High-Impact Slow-Performing Pages view. No duplicate. |
| DONE | report-performance-tuning | Report and dashboard performance: filter optimization, report type selection impact, custom report types vs standard, dashboard refresh scheduling, report row limits. NOT for CRM Analytics (use crm-analytics-* skills). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Improve Report Performance; Salesforce Object Reference — Report, Dashboard; knowledge/imports LDV best practices]. Key: selective filters mandatory on large objects (date range, owner, record type); custom report types perform worse than standard when spanning 4+ objects; dashboard refresh scheduling caps at 24hr minimum for dynamic; async reports for >2M rows via Analytics API; report row limit = 2,000 detail rows displayed (up to 2 billion queryable with filters); no duplicate — reports-and-dashboards-fundamentals covers creation basics, this covers performance tuning. |
| DONE | license-optimization-strategy | Salesforce license management: license type comparison, permission set license usage, feature license audit, login-based license strategy, license reclamation from inactive users. NOT for license purchasing decisions. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — View Your Org License Information, Permission Set Licenses, Login-Based Licensing; Metadata API — UserLicense]. Key: 3 license tiers: CRM (full), Platform (limited objects), Community/Identity (portal/SSO); PSLs gate features independently of user license (e.g., Einstein Analytics PSL, Flow Orchestration PSL); Login-Based Licenses count monthly logins not seats — suited for infrequent portal users; inactive user reclamation: query LastLoginDate, freeze via UserLogin.IsFrozen, then deactivate; license usage visible in Setup > Company Information and REST /limits; no duplicate. |
| DONE | system-field-behavior-and-audit | System fields and audit behavior: CreatedDate vs SystemModstamp, LastModifiedDate triggers, system field queryability, audit field overrides on insert, IsDeleted behavior, formula field recalculation timing. NOT for field history tracking (use field-history-tracking). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Object Reference - System Fields; SF Engineering Blog - SystemModstamp vs LastModifiedDate; SF Help - Create Audit Fields; REST API - QueryAll]. Key: SystemModstamp >= LastModifiedDate because it updates on user edits AND automated system processes (workflow field updates, formula recalcs) while LastModifiedDate only updates on direct user/API modifications; SystemModstamp is indexed, LastModifiedDate is not - use SystemModstamp for performant SOQL delta queries. Create Audit Fields org permission (enabled via SF Support) allows setting CreatedDate, CreatedById, LastModifiedDate, LastModifiedById on insert for data migration only. IsDeleted=true when record enters Recycle Bin; queryable via ALL ROWS or REST QueryAll until permanently deleted. No duplicate. |
| DONE | in-app-guidance-and-walkthroughs | In-App Guidance setup: prompts, walkthroughs, floating prompts, docked prompts, targeting rules, scheduling, adoption tracking, user segment targeting. NOT for change management (use change-management-and-training). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — In-App Guidance overview; Types of In-App Guidance; Considerations; Salesforce Ben]. Key: 3 prompt types: floating (repositionable), docked (bottom-corner, supports video), targeted (anchored to UI element); walkthroughs = up to 10 steps; free tier = 3 custom walkthroughs, additional require Sales Enablement license; audience filtering is profile-based only (not roles/territories/behavioral); scheduling: start/end dates, frequency caps, page-load delay; analytics via Prompt Actions object; targeted prompts break silently if anchor element removed; 3-walkthrough limit counts active walkthroughs not total; Experience Cloud requires PRM license. LLM anti-patterns: claiming permission sets work for targeting (profiles only as of Spring '25); assuming unlimited free prompts; recommending >5 steps; conflating prompt with walkthrough. No duplicate. |
| DONE | lightning-app-builder-advanced | Advanced Lightning App Builder: dynamic pages, component visibility filters, custom address fields in pages, template cloning, org vs app vs record pages, page assignment rules. NOT for LWC development. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Lightning App Builder Limits; Visibility Rules on Lightning Pages; LWC Dev Guide — Configure for App Builder]. Key: 5 focus areas: (1) component visibility filters (up to 10 conditions, AND/OR, based on fields/record types/profiles/permissions/device); (2) Dynamic Forms — field-level visibility on record pages (not all standard objects qualify); (3) Dynamic Actions — action bar control from LAB canvas with per-action filters; (4) custom app page templates via Aura `lightning:template` + `<flexipage:region>` nodes; (5) performance — 8 or fewer visible components per region for mobile. Critical gotchas: visibility filters are cosmetic — FLS must enforce security; mixing Dynamic Actions with page-layout actions causes duplicates; formula fields recommended for complex cross-field visibility; LWC `targetConfigs` for record pages cannot expose `recordId` in design resource. Distinct from admin/dynamic-forms-and-actions (that covers Dynamic Forms/Actions only). No duplicate. |
| DONE | nfr-definition-for-salesforce | Non-functional requirements for Salesforce projects: performance benchmarks, scalability targets, availability SLAs, security requirements, data volume projections, concurrent user capacity. NOT for technical implementation. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [architect.salesforce.com — Well-Architected Overview; Resilient pillar; Trusted pillar]. Key: WAF organises NFRs across Trusted (security, compliance, reliability), Easy (usability, process efficiency), Adaptable (scalability, resilience, composability); 5 NFR categories: (1) Performance — SLIs like "X% pages load under Ns" validated in Full sandbox; (2) Scalability — governor limits are hard ceilings, not recommendations; (3) Availability — Salesforce 99.9% SLA covers infrastructure only, NOT data recovery (shared responsibility); (4) Security/Compliance — GDPR/HIPAA/PCI impose Shield, encryption, audit logging constraints; (5) Usability — page load time, field count, mobile readiness. Critical gotchas: vague NFRs ("fast", "secure") cannot be tested; governor limits are architectural constraints; scale testing requires Full sandbox or prod-equivalent. LLM anti-patterns: claiming Salesforce SLA guarantees data recovery; treating governor limits as soft; omitting compliance NFRs; generating NFR statements without measurable thresholds. No duplicate. |

| DONE | order-of-execution-deep-dive | Complete Apex order of execution: before triggers, validation rules, after triggers, workflow, process builder, flow, assignment rules, auto-response, DML cascading, recursion implications. NOT for trigger framework design (use trigger-framework). | DONE 2026-04-05. Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide — Triggers and Order of Execution (apex_triggers_order_of_execution.htm)]. Key: Canonical 18-step OOE for single DML statement: (1) Load record from DB, (2) Overwrite record with new values, (3) Execute all before triggers, (4) Run system validation (required fields, max field length, foreign keys), (5) Run custom validation rules, (6) Execute duplicate rules, (7) Save record to DB (no commit), (8) Execute all after triggers, (9) Execute assignment rules, (10) Execute auto-response rules, (11) Execute workflow rules, (12) If workflow field updates → rerun before+after triggers ONCE, (13) Execute processes (Process Builder — legacy), (14) Execute escalation rules, (15) Execute record-triggered Flows (after-save runs here, after workflow+process), (16) Execute entitlement rules, (17) Execute roll-up summary fields → parent triggers can re-fire, (18) Commit to DB + post-commit logic (@future, emails, etc.); Critical: before-save Flows run at step 3 (same as before triggers — more efficient for field updates); workflow field update reruns triggers only once (not infinitely); Apex trigger recursion guard (`Set<Id> processed`) required if trigger logic is update-triggering. Distinct from trigger-framework (design patterns), record-triggered-flow-patterns (Flow-specific behavior). No duplicate. |
| DONE | mixed-dml-and-setup-objects | Mixed DML operation errors: setup vs non-setup objects, System.runAs workarounds, future method separation, test class implications, common scenarios that trigger mixed DML. NOT for general DML patterns. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide - sObjects That Cant Be Used Together in DML Operations; Apex Developer Guide - Mixed DML in Test Methods; local corpus apex/test-data-factory-patterns]. Key: Setup objects (User, UserRole, PermissionSet, Group, GroupMember) cannot be inserted or updated in the same transaction as non-setup objects because they affect org-level access permissions; violating throws MIXED_DML_OPERATION runtime error. Two workarounds: System.runAs() in test contexts (wraps setup-object DML in separate transaction context) and @future methods in production code (defers setup-object DML to async transaction). In test classes, perform non-setup DML first then wrap setup-object DML in System.runAs() block; @testSetup methods subject to same restriction. No duplicate. |
| DONE | record-locking-and-contention | Record locking in Salesforce: row-level locking, FOR UPDATE queries, lock contention in high-volume orgs, parent record locking on child insert, deadlock patterns, retry strategies. NOT for sharing model (use sharing-and-visibility). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide - Locking Records; SOQL FOR UPDATE Reference; SF Help - How to Prevent UNABLE_TO_LOCK_ROW Errors; Designing Record Access for Enterprise Scale]. Key: FOR UPDATE in SOQL acquires exclusive row lock for transaction duration; DML on child record also locks parent, meaning concurrent child inserts against same parent contend on parent lock and fail with UNABLE_TO_LOCK_ROW after 10-second wait timeout. Deadlock risk rises with data skew (10,000+ children per parent) or different lock ordering; mitigations: sort Bulk API CSV by parent ID, switch Bulk API to serial mode, catch UNABLE_TO_LOCK_ROW and retry via Queueable, request Granular Locking from SF Support so child locks dont escalate to full parent hierarchy. No duplicate. |
| DONE | timezone-and-datetime-pitfalls | DateTime vs Date field behavior: timezone conversion pitfalls, user timezone vs org timezone, SOQL date literals, GMT storage, Visualforce timezone rendering, Flow datetime handling. NOT for formula field syntax. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — Date/Datetime methods; SOQL/SOSL Reference — Date Literals; help.salesforce.com — Date and Time Field Types; knowledge/imports salesforce-soql-sosl.md]. Key: DateTime fields stored as UTC in DB, displayed in user timezone; Date fields have NO timezone — stored as midnight UTC, so Date.today() in Apex returns server-side date not user date; SOQL date literals (TODAY, LAST_WEEK) use running user timezone; Datetime.format() uses user locale by default; Visualforce renders DateTime in user TZ but Date as-is; Flow DateTime comparisons are UTC-based — comparing to user-entered date needs conversion; common pitfall: reporting across timezones shows records on "wrong" day due to UTC midnight crossing. No duplicate. |
| DONE | formula-field-performance-and-limits | Formula field compile size limits, cross-object formula performance impact, formula field recalculation timing, SOQL filter limitations on formulas, compiled character limit workarounds. NOT for formula syntax (use formula-fields). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Formula Field Limits and Considerations; help.salesforce.com — Operators and Functions: Formula Size Limits; Apex Dev Guide — SOQL WHERE clause formula limitations]. Key: compile size limit = 5,000 characters (not source characters — compiled includes field references expanded); cross-object formulas limited to 10 spanning relationships (count includes through lookups); formula fields NOT indexable — SOQL WHERE on formula = full table scan; formula recalculation is on-read (not stored) — no trigger fires on formula change; SOQL filter on formula forces runtime evaluation per row — severe LDV performance hit; workaround: use workflow/flow to write formula result to a real field for indexing; EXISTS in formula-fields skill but scoped to syntax — this skill covers performance/limits depth. No duplicate. |
| DONE | fflib-enterprise-patterns | FFLib (Apex Enterprise Patterns): Unit of Work, Domain layer, Selector layer, Service layer, Application factory, adoption strategy, when to use vs simpler patterns. NOT for basic trigger framework (use trigger-framework). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [github.com/apex-enterprise-patterns — fflib-apex-common, fflib-apex-mocks; Trailhead — Apex Enterprise Patterns; developer.salesforce.com blog — Separation of Concerns in Apex]. Key: 4-layer architecture: Service (entry points, transaction boundary), Domain (sObject validation/behavior), Selector (all SOQL centralized, enforces FLS), Unit of Work (registers DML, commits in one transaction); Application class is the factory/registry; adopt incrementally �� Selector first (immediate SOQL centralization), then Service, then Domain; overkill for < 10 triggers — use simple handler pattern instead; fflib-apex-mocks enables true unit testing via dependency injection; no duplicate — trigger-framework covers dispatch only, this covers full enterprise layering. |

| DONE | feature-flags-and-kill-switches | Feature flag patterns in Salesforce: Custom Metadata-based toggles, Custom Permissions as flags, hierarchical custom settings for user-level flags, runtime feature gating, emergency kill switches. Key: Three mechanisms: (1) Custom Metadata Type with IsEnabled__c checkbox field — `FeatureFlag__mdt.getInstance('MyFeature').IsEnabled__c` — deployable, packageable, hot-swap without code deploy; (2) Custom Permissions + `FeatureManagement.checkPermission('My_Permission')` — user-scoped visibility gate, assigned via permission sets, revocable immediately; (3) Hierarchical Custom Settings — user/profile/org hierarchy level for per-user flag values; Kill switch pattern = CMDT row with `IsEnabled__c = false` — no code deploy required, instant effect; CMDT not available in formula fields for dynamic flags (use Apex only); emergency kill switch should be testable in unit tests via Test.loadData(); `custom-metadata-types` skill covers CMDT fundamentals — this skill covers the pattern of using them as feature flags specifically. | DONE | governor-limit-recovery-patterns | Recovering from governor limit errors: CPU timeout analysis, heap size diagnosis, SOQL query optimization under pressure, bulkification retrofit, limit-safe coding patterns. NOT for general limits overview (use limits-and-scalability-planning). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — Execution Governors and Limits; Apex Governor Limits Quick Reference; Apex Hours — Transaction Savepoints and Rollback Strategies]. Key: LimitException is UNCATCHABLE — terminates transaction immediately with full rollback; recovery must happen before limit hit using Limits.* class proactive checks (Limits.getQueries() vs Limits.getLimitQueries()); Database.setSavepoint()/rollback() for partial-transaction recovery — max 5 savepoints per transaction, each counts as DML statement, static vars NOT reset on rollback; BatchApexErrorEvent for post-failure scope recovery (check DoesExceedJobScopeMaxLength before processing JobScope); adjacent skill apex/governor-limits covers prevention/bulkification; this skill covers in-flight recovery mechanics and limit budgeting. LLM anti-patterns: suggesting try/catch (LimitException e) — not possible; savepoints as general limit-recovery without noting DML cost; conflating async offload with recovery; omitting Limits.* pre-checks in loop-heavy code. No duplicate. |
| DONE | apex-performance-profiling | Apex performance analysis: Limits class usage, debug log analysis for CPU time, heap profiling, SOQL query plan analysis, identifying N+1 patterns, benchmark testing approaches. NOT for debug log setup (use debug-logs-and-developer-console). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Apex Log Analyzer - SF Dev Blog; Apex Developer Guide - Execution Governors and Limits; Apex Performance Troubleshooting Blog]. Key: Existing apex-cpu-and-heap-optimization covers Limits.getCpuTime() and heap patterns; this skill is distinct covering the diagnostic toolchain (Apex Log Analyzer flame graph in VS Code, Developer Console timeline, debug log structure for isolating hotspots) and SOQL Query Plan analysis. Sync CPU limit 10,000ms, heap 6MB; async 60,000ms CPU, 12MB heap. Apex Log Analyzer renders flame graphs from debug logs with 0.001ms zoom precision showing DML/SOQL call trees alongside Apex method timing. No duplicate. |
| DONE | cross-object-formula-and-rollup-performance | Cross-object formula and rollup summary field performance: spanning relationship limits, rollup recalculation triggers, DLRS alternatives, rollup on large data volumes, formula spanning cascade effects. NOT for formula syntax. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Help - Roll-Up Summary Field; SF Help - Maximum 15 object references error; SF Engineering Blog - Record Locking]. Key: Cross-object formulas hard-limited to 15 unique spanning relationships per object across all formulas and rules combined (cap at 20 even with increase request). Rollup recalculation fires at step 13 of save order so trigger-time queries see stale rollup values; cross-object formula fields in rollup filters do not re-fire recalculation when distant referenced record changes. On LDV orgs (300k+ children) full recalculations time out with REQUEST_RUNNING_TOO_LONG when filter criteria reference non-indexed fields. No duplicate. |
| DONE | long-running-process-orchestration | Orchestrating long-running processes: chaining Queueable jobs, Continuations, Platform Event-driven state machines, process checkpointing, timeout handling, progress tracking patterns. NOT for basic async Apex (use async-apex). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Dev Guide — Queueable Interface, AsyncOptions, Finalizer; Apex Dev Guide — Continuations for Lightning; help.salesforce.com — Platform Events Developer Guide]. Key: Queueable chaining via System.enqueueJob() in execute(); AsyncOptions.setMaximumQueueableStackDepth(N) caps chain length (default 1 in tests, 5 in async); Finalizer interface (FinalizerContext) runs after Queueable regardless of success/failure — use for retry/cleanup; Platform Event state machine: publish checkpoint events, subscribe in trigger to continue next step; Continuation for long callouts (up to 120s, runs async in LWC/Aura); progress tracking via Custom Object or Platform Event updates; distinct from apex-queueable-patterns (single-job patterns) — this covers multi-step orchestration across transactions. No duplicate. |
| DONE | callout-and-dml-transaction-boundaries | Transaction boundaries with callouts: uncommitted work errors, callout-before-DML vs DML-before-callout, mixed transaction patterns, queueable callout separation, future method boundaries. NOT for callout implementation (use callouts-and-http-integrations). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide - Callout Limits and Limitations; SF Help KB - You have uncommitted work pending; local skills: callout-limits-and-async-patterns]. Key: Any callout in a transaction with prior uncommitted DML throws System.CalloutException: You have uncommitted work pending - restriction is transaction-scoped not method-scoped, so DML in any helper class blocks later callouts. Canonical fix: Queueable implementing Database.AllowsCallouts (enqueued after DML commits) or callout before any DML synchronously; @future(callout=true) is legacy alternative but cannot accept sObject params or chain. DML between two callouts also triggers the error - mixed callout-DML-callout patterns require separate async boundaries. No duplicate. |
| DONE | common-apex-runtime-errors | Common Apex runtime errors and fixes: UNABLE_TO_LOCK_ROW, MIXED_DML_OPERATION, FIELD_CUSTOM_VALIDATION_EXCEPTION, TOO_MANY_SOQL_QUERIES, System.LimitException diagnosis and resolution patterns. NOT for error handling framework design. | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [Apex Built-In Exceptions; Apex Governor Limits; Exception Statements]. Key: 6 most common exceptions: NullPointerException (uninitialized var / missing null guard on SOQL scalar), QueryException (single-row SOQL returns 0 or 2+ rows), DmlException (required fields, dup rules, mixed sObject DML), ListException (index out of bounds), LimitException (governor limit — UNCATCHABLE), TypeException/StringException (cast/conversion failures). Diagnostic path: read debug log FATAL_ERROR or EXCEPTION_THROWN event → match exception class → isolate trigger context. Distinct from apex/exception-handling (covers try/catch structure/boundary translation) — this skill covers per-exception-type diagnosis and root-cause resolution. LLM anti-patterns: generating catch (Exception e) { return null; } that swallows LimitException; adding null guards after the fact without bulkifying the query; recommending try/catch as fix for governor limits instead of Limits class checks. No duplicate. |
| DONE | trigger-and-flow-coexistence | Managing triggers and flows on the same object: execution order interactions, recursion prevention across automation types, before-flow vs after-trigger timing, context variable conflicts. NOT for trigger framework (use trigger-framework). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide - Triggers and Order of Execution; SF Architects - Record-Triggered Automation Decision Guide]. Key: Before-save flows and before Apex triggers both run at step 3 with no guaranteed relative order, making same-field writes a common silent conflict; after-save flows run at step 15 after workflow rules and Process Builder, so trigger-then-flow recursion requires field-value guard patterns. SF Well-Architected recommends single entry-point per object (one trigger or one flow set, not both); coexistence is a tolerated legacy state requiring explicit governance. Flow Trigger Explorer used to sequence multiple flows. No duplicate - order-of-execution-deep-dive covers mechanics, this covers coexistence governance. |
| DONE | pdf-generation-patterns | PDF generation in Salesforce: Visualforce renderAs PDF, page size and styling, dynamic PDF content, PDF from LWC via Visualforce, third-party PDF libraries, attachment and ContentVersion storage. NOT for quote PDF templates (use quote-pdf-customization). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [VF Developer Guide - Render as PDF; VF PDF Rendering Considerations; PageReference.getContentAsPDF() Reference; ContentVersion Object Reference]. Key: SF uses Flying Saucer HTML-to-PDF engine for renderAs='pdf' on apex:page which completely ignores JavaScript and external CDN stylesheets - all CSS must be inline and all data loaded server-side in Apex controller. PageReference.getContentAsPDF() renders VF page to raw PDF bytes programmatically for storage as ContentVersion (VersionData field) linked to records via ContentDocumentLink. LWC cannot render as PDF natively; documented pattern is VF wrapper page delegating to Flying Saucer renderer. No duplicate. |

## Phase 2 — Sales Cloud

### Sales Cloud × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | lead-management-and-conversion | Lead settings, lead conversion mapping, lead queues, auto-response rules, web-to-lead, lead processes. NOT for lead assignment rules (use assignment-rules). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Lead Conversion Field Mapping; Web-to-Lead spam/CAPTCHA; Salesforce Well-Architected Overview]. Key: No single local skill covers this — scattered across assignment-rules, queues-and-public-groups, standard-object-quirks, duplicate-management. Configuration chain: (1) Lead Settings (default assignment, conversion settings, notify owner); (2) assignment rules — one active rule at a time; (3) lead queues as assignment targets with queue-email; (4) web-to-lead — 500 leads/day hard limit, reCAPTCHA prevents spam blocking limit, Block duplicate rules silently reject web submissions unless Default Web-to-Lead Creator excluded from matching rule; (5) lead conversion field mapping (Object Manager > Lead > Fields > Map Lead Fields) — unmapped custom fields silently dropped on conversion, data type and picklist value mismatches cause silent data loss; (6) lead scoring via Einstein Prediction Builder or Flow-based point scoring. LLM anti-patterns: assuming all custom lead fields auto-map; recommending multiple active assignment rules; forgetting dup Block rules block web-to-lead. No duplicate. |
| DONE | opportunity-management | Opportunity stages, sales processes, similar opportunities, big deal alerts, stage history tracking, contact roles. NOT for forecasting (use collaborative-forecasts). | Researched 2026-04-05. Sources: [help.salesforce.com — Opportunity Teams and Splits; Guidelines for Opportunity Splits; Pipeline Forecasting Implementation Guide Spring '26]. Key: Configuration chain: (1) Define Stage picklist values — each carries IsWon/IsClosed flags, default Probability, ForecastCategoryName (5 fixed categories: Pipeline/Best Case/Commit/Closed/Omitted — cannot be renamed); (2) Create Sales Processes — filter which Stage values available per business motion; (3) Assign Sales Process to each Record Type; (4) Configure Path on top of Sales Process stages (Path = guidance/key fields only, does NOT enforce stage progression — validation rules do); (5) Enable Team Selling before enabling Opportunity Splits — revenue-type splits must total exactly 100%, overlay splits can exceed 100%; (6) Collaborative Forecasting: choose forecast object, set hierarchy, enable per profile. Critical gotchas: deleting a Stage picklist value in use corrupts records; splits cannot be disabled once data exists; forecast types limited to 4 custom by default. LLM anti-patterns: conflating Sales Process with Path; assuming revenue and overlay splits share same 100% rule; treating ForecastCategoryName as editable. No duplicate. |
| DONE | collaborative-forecasts | Collaborative Forecasts setup: forecast types, adjustments, quotas, forecast categories, forecast hierarchy, cumulative vs individual. NOT for custom report-based forecasting. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Help - Defining Forecast Types; Pipeline Forecast Types; SF Ben - Complete Guide to Salesforce Forecasting]. Key: Supports up to 4 active Forecast Types (extensible via support case) sourced from Opportunity, Opportunity Product, Opportunity Splits, Product Splits, or Line Item Schedule; admins choose role-based or territory hierarchy and configure single-category vs cumulative rollup (switching rollup method deletes all existing adjustments). Five fixed forecast categories (Pipeline, Best Case, Commit, Closed, Omitted) map to opportunity stages; Manager Judgment not available for split-based forecast types; quotas load per user per period and display attainment %. No duplicate. |
| DONE | products-and-pricebooks | Product catalog setup: standard vs custom pricebooks, multi-currency pricebooks, product schedules, archiving products. NOT for CPQ pricing (use Revenue Cloud skills). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Help - Products and Pricebooks; PricebookEntry Object Reference; sfdcamplified.com - Product and Price Book]. Key: Data model is Product2 + Pricebook2 joined by PricebookEntry junction object; every org has exactly one Standard Pricebook (cannot be deleted, only deactivated) and unlimited custom Pricebooks (cannot be deleted while referenced by open Opportunities/Quotes). Multi-currency requires one PricebookEntry per currency per product per Pricebook. Product Schedules split into Revenue Schedules (installment payments) and Quantity Schedules (phased delivery), enabled per-org and per-product. Deactivating product (IsActive=false) hides from new selection but preserves existing line items. No duplicate. |
| DONE | quotes-and-quote-templates | Quote configuration: quote templates, PDF generation, email quotes, quote sync to opportunity, discount approval. NOT for CPQ quote configuration. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Help - Quotes Limitations; SF Help - Quote Sync Overview; SF Help - Quote Template Landing Page]. Key: Only one quote per opportunity can be synced at a time (SyncedQuoteId on Opportunity); when synced, quote line items and opportunity products update bidirectionally. Quote templates use rich-text editor with 32,000-character limit per Text/Image field and do not support right-to-left text or custom font/color branding; standard templates only render QuoteLineItem (not CPQ SBQQ__QuoteLine__c). Custom fields on Opportunity/OpportunityLineItem do not auto-map to Quote/QuoteLineItem - require custom Apex or AppExchange package. No duplicate. |
| DUPLICATE | territory-management-sales | Enterprise Territory Management for Sales Cloud: territory types, assignment rules, territory-based forecasting. NOT for general ETM admin (use enterprise-territory-management). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Sales Territories Implementation Guide Spring 26; SF Help - Territory Forecasts; SF Help - Set Up Territory Types]. Key: DUPLICATE — comprehensive enterprise-territory-management skill already exists at skills/admin/enterprise-territory-management covering territory types with priority values for OTA tie-breaking, assignment rules, territory-based forecast types, and limits (1,000 territories/model default, 20,000 on Performance/Unlimited). The NOT for clause explicitly defers to enterprise-territory-management and official Spring 26 docs confirm all ETM mechanics documented under a single unified framework with no Sales Cloud-specific variant. Covered by skills/admin/enterprise-territory-management. |
| DONE | sales-engagement-cadences | Sales Engagement / High Velocity Sales setup: cadences, call scripts, email templates, work queue, sequence steps. NOT for Marketing Cloud campaigns. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [SF Sales Engagement Implementation Guide Spring 26; SF Help - Cadence Considerations; Trailhead - Standard Cadences for Sales Engagement]. Key: Sales Engagement (formerly HVS) uses Cadence Builder 2.0 with multi-step sequences: Email, Call, LinkedIn, Wait, and Custom step types across three branching tracks (main, positive, negative) based on prospect engagement signals. Work Queue surfaces due steps for reps, embeddable in Outlook/Gmail; org-wide active target cap 500,000 and 150,000 active tracker limit. Bundled with Sales Cloud Unlimited, add-on for Professional/Enterprise. Setup requires enabling feature, assigning permission sets, configuring dialer, customizing page layouts. No duplicate. |
| DONE | einstein-activity-capture-setup | Einstein Activity Capture configuration: email sync, calendar sync, activity metrics, privacy settings, user assignment. NOT for manual activity logging. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [help.salesforce.com Einstein Activity Capture Setup; Considerations for Setting Up EAC; salesforceben.com Ultimate Guide to EAC]. Key: EAC syncs emails/calendar via configuration profiles — admins must create Configuration in Setup defining sync scope, auth type (User-Level or Org-Level OAuth), excluded domains, and privacy mode; as of Summer '25 synced emails stored as standard Activity records consuming org storage. Common mistakes: assigning PSL without Configuration, failing to configure excluded domains before go-live, no storage/archival strategy. No duplicate. |

Justified if scoped strictly to analysis/mapping artifact, not configuration. |

| DONE | territory-design-requirements | Territory hierarchy design: alignment criteria, coverage model requirements, assignment rules, geographic considerations. Key: ETM hierarchy is independent of role hierarchy and drives record access plus forecast rollups; account assignment rules support up to 10 filter criteria per territory on numeric fields for performance; target ~3:1 territory-to-user ratio; geographic contiguity is best practice but non-contiguous supported. No duplicate. |
| DONE | lead-scoring-requirements | Lead scoring model design: qualifying criteria, MQL/SQL definitions, handoff requirements, scoring dimensions. Key: Lead scoring implemented via formula/numeric custom fields combining demographic/firmographic dimensions with behavioral signals; MQL threshold defined by composite score, SQL validated by sales rep applying BANT/MEDDIC framework; handoff SLA must define score threshold, required data fields, max response time, and recycling process for failed SQLs. No duplicate. |
| DONE | quote-to-cash-requirements | Quote-to-cash process mapping: approval requirements, discount policies, document output specs, order handoff. NOT for CPQ implementation. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Salesforce Help — Quotes Overview; Trailhead — Negotiate Enterprise Quotes; Trailhead — Build a Discount Approval Process]. Key: Standard flow is Opportunity → Quote (with line items) → Synced Quote (only one per Opportunity) → Approval Process (entry criteria on Discount/Amount) → PDF via Quote Template (30-page/100-line-item limits) → Order creation on Quote Accepted status; CPQ pricing rules and discount schedules explicitly out of scope. No duplicate. |

### Sales Cloud × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `apex`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | opportunity-trigger-patterns | Apex trigger patterns for Opportunity: stage change automation, amount rollups, team member sync, split calculations. NOT for generic trigger patterns (use trigger-framework). | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [OpportunitySplit Object Reference; OpportunityTeamMember Object Reference; Apex Trigger Best Practices; local corpus]. Key: Three high-risk automation areas — stage-change detection via Trigger.oldMap, cascading rollups to Account, and TeamMember/Split sync; DML on OpportunitySplit not supported in before-triggers; team member removal cascade-deletes split records; split percentages must sum to 100 on revenue split types but not overlay types. No duplicate. |
| DONE | quote-pdf-customization | Quote PDF generation with Visualforce: custom templates, dynamic sections, multi-language quotes, logo placement. NOT for LWC-based documents. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [VF Developer Guide: Render Page as PDF; PDF Rendering Considerations; Quote Template Limitations — help.salesforce.com]. Key: Standard Quote templates use declarative editor (no VF), cannot render CPQ lines or JS content; custom requires VF page with renderAs='pdf' and Standard Controller or custom Apex; PageReference.getContentAsPDF() for programmatic generation; logos must use absolute static resource URLs; PDF renderer has no support for advanced CSS, SVG, or JavaScript. No duplicate. |
| DONE | territory-api-and-assignment | Territory2 API: territory assignment via Apex, territory member management, bulk territory assignment, rule evaluation. NOT for ETM admin setup. | Researched 2026-04-06. Key: UserTerritory2Association supports standard DML; ObjectTerritory2Association supports DML but triggers don't fire on it; bulk assignment rule evaluation requires SOAP API callout (not available natively in Apex); UserInfo.getSessionId() unavailable in async contexts; 200-record-per-SOAP-call limit applies. No duplicate. |
| DONE | lead-conversion-customization | Customizing lead conversion with Apex: custom field mapping, related record creation, conversion triggers, LeadConvert. Key: Database.LeadConvert with setLeadId, setConvertedStatus, setDoNotCreateOpportunity, setAccountId, setContactId, setOwnerId controls conversion; custom field mapping must be handled post-conversion in trigger or separate DML since convertLead does not transfer unmapped custom fields; 100 lead conversion limit per call; LeadConvertResult cannot be instantiated in tests — requires JSON-deserialization workaround. No duplicate. |
| DONE | sales-engagement-api | Sales Engagement / HVS API: cadence enrollment via Apex, step customization, call result logging, action customization. NOT for cadence admin setup. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Sales Engagement Actions — Actions Developer Guide; Cadence Objects Data Model; ActionCadenceTracker/StepTracker Object References]. Key: ActionCadence* object family — enrollment via assignTargetToSalesCadence invocable action (callable from Apex, Flow, REST); triggers not supported on these objects — requires CDC via Async Apex Triggers; cadence structure (steps, variants, branching) is read-only via API — must be built in Cadence Builder UI. No duplicate. |
| DONE | einstein-activity-capture-api | Einstein Activity Capture data access: activity metrics API, email and event sync data, reporting on captured activities. NOT for email template design. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [ActivityMetric Object Reference; UnifiedActivity Object Reference; EACSettings Metadata API]. Key: Pre-Summer '25 EAC data lived in external AWS store invisible to SOQL/triggers/reports; primary API surface is ActivityMetric (aggregate counts) and, for newer orgs, EmailMessage/Task objects plus UnifiedActivity; EmailMessage cannot be joined to Task/Event in single report type; developers can read but cannot write or trigger against EAC-managed records. No duplicate. |
