Key: Correct insert order is Account/PersonAccount → FinancialSecurity (instrument records must pre-exist before FinancialHolding) → FinancialAccount → FinancialAccountRole (Primary Owner) → FinancialHolding → FinancialAccountTransaction; both managed-package FinServ__FinancialAccountTransaction__c and Core FSC standard FinancialAccountTransaction (API v61.0+) are native transaction history objects — not always custom. Critical gotcha: Rollup-by-Lookup Apex triggers fire on every DML causing row-lock errors during bulk load — disable "Enable Rollup Summary" for the ETL user via Wealth Application Config custom setting before load and run RollupRecalculationBatchable or DPE post-load; in managed-package FSC balance is a single overwritable field (no snapshot history) while Core FSC stores balance history as child FinancialAccountBalance records requiring a different migration approach. Overlaps with financial-account-setup (configuration) and fsc-data-model (object reference) — this skill focuses on bulk migration execution patterns only. |
| DUPLICATE | household-data-setup | Household data model setup: member relationships, primary designation, financial data aggregation, group setup. NOT for standard contact import. | Covered by skills/admin/household-model-configuration — ACR-based membership, FinServ__PrimaryGroup__c, financial rollup aggregation, and FSC-vs-NPSP incompatibility all documented there. |
| DONE | fsc-data-model | FSC data model: financial objects, relationship objects, rollup relationships, industry-specific standard objects. NOT for standard data model. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Financial Services Cloud Data Models — Salesforce Help (help.salesforce.com); Financial Services Cloud Object Reference — Salesforce Developer Docs (developer.salesforce.com); Industries Common Resources Developer Guide v66.0]. Key: FSC extends the standard data model under the FinServ__ namespace with objects including FinServ__FinancialAccount__c, FinServ__FinancialAccountRole__c, FinServ__FinancialHolding__c, FinServ__AssetsAndLiabilities__c, FinServ__ContactContactRelation__c, FinServ__AccountAccountRelation__c, FinServ__FinancialGoal__c, and FinServ__LifeEvent__c; client-household relationships flow through AccountContactRelation and AccountAccountRelation; FSC Record Rollups aggregate financial data to Household Account via the FinServ rollup framework, not native ROLLUP summary fields. Partial overlap with data/person-accounts skill (Person Account model in FSC). LLM anti-pattern: assuming native Salesforce roll-up summary fields aggregate financial data — FSC uses its own async rollup engine configured via FSC Admin settings.|
| DONE | financial-data-quality | Financial data quality: account validation, duplicate financial records, data reconciliation with source systems. NOT for generic data quality. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Financial Services Cloud Admin Guide — Availability and Limitations; Financial Services Cloud Developer Guide (Spring 26)]. Key: Standard Salesforce Duplicate Rules do not cover the FSC-specific FinancialAccount object — duplicate detection must be custom-built using Matching Rules on Account/Contact or Apex triggers since FinancialAccount has no out-of-box duplicate rule support; the FSC rollup batch aggregating household-level financial data does not self-heal after failure meaning stale KPI values persist silently and must be reconciled manually against source systems. Distinct scope from generic data-quality and duplicate-management skills — none address FSC-specific FinancialAccount validation or reconciliation against core banking/custodial systems. LLM anti-pattern: incorrectly advising applying standard Duplicate Rules directly to FinancialAccount — it is a custom FSC object not supported by standard Duplicate Rules. |

### FSC × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | fsc-architecture-patterns | FSC solution architecture: data model decisions, sharing model design, integration strategy, compliance framework. NOT for individual feature design. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Financial Services Cloud Data Model (Salesforce Help); Compliant Data Sharing — FSC (Salesforce Help); Financial Services Cloud Data Model Gallery (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: FSC's foundational architectural decision is choosing between the managed-package data model (Person Accounts + FinServ__ objects) and the platform-native model shipping since Winter '23 — this choice drives every downstream integration and sharing design; Compliant Data Sharing (CDS) controls cross-team visibility of sensitive financial records without relying on standard sharing rules, and over-sharing via broad sharing sets is a documented compliance risk. Closest overlaps: data/person-accounts (PA model) and architect/security-architecture-review (PCI/financial security posture); no cross-domain FSC architecture skill exists. LLM anti-pattern: conflating generic sharing-rule design with FSC Compliant Data Sharing — CDS is a separate FSC-specific framework with distinct objects, activation steps, and limitations that standard sharing rules cannot replace.|
| DONE | aml-kyc-process-architecture | AML/KYC process architecture: verification workflow, screening integration, risk scoring, regulatory compliance. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Salesforce Industries Developer Guide — Identity Verification and Risk Scoring (FSC); Salesforce Integration Patterns Guide — Remote Call-In and Batch Data Synchronization]. Key: FSC has no native AML engine or sanctions screening — the platform provides orchestration primitives (Flows, OmniStudio Integration Procedures, Apex) and data model objects (PartyProfileRisk with riskCategory for loan onboarding) to store and route results from mandatory third-party ISV screening calls (Refinitiv World-Check, Accuity, LexisNexis); Identity Verification in FSC is a contact-center caller-authentication feature backed by Connect APIs and Metadata-configurable flow — it confirms identity against stored data but performs no biometric or sanctions check. The Industries Scoring Framework (requires CRM Plus license plus FSC product CRM license) supports generic propensity model scoring via CRM Analytics apps — it is not an AML risk-rating system; custom Apex or DataWeave scoring logic is the standard pattern for regulatory risk tiering. Distinct from compliance-documentation-requirements (KYC data collection workflow) — this skill covers the architecture for screening integration patterns and risk scoring design. |
| DONE | wealth-management-architecture | Wealth management platform architecture: advisor workspace, client portal, portfolio analytics, integration. NOT for investment advice. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Salesforce Industries Developer Guide — IndustriesSettings metadata, Wealth Management AI pref, Financial Deal Management and Compliant Data Sharing flags; Salesforce Integration Patterns Guide — Batch Data Synchronization and Remote Call-In]. Key: The FSC wealth management platform requires explicit enablement of discrete features — enableWealthManagementAIPref (API v63.0+) unlocks AI-powered portfolio analysis and client insights; enableDealManagement enables Financial Deal Management (exposes Interaction-to-Deal junction objects); Compliant Data Sharing must be independently enabled per object type (Account, Opportunity, Interaction, Interaction Summary, custom objects) and is off by default. Critical gotcha: the Scoring Framework powering advisor analytics dashboards requires the CRM Plus license plus the FSC product CRM license — teams assuming analytics are included in base FSC licensing will be blocked at deployment. Custodian-to-FSC portfolio data follows Batch Data Synchronization pattern using Bulk API 2.0 for large datasets; real-time custodian updates use Remote Call-In via FSC Integrations API. |
| DONE | insurance-cloud-architecture | Insurance-specific FSC architecture: policy administration, claims processing, underwriting workflow design. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Insurance Developer Guide v66.0 (Salesforce Developers); Get Started With Financial Services Cloud for Insurance (Salesforce Help)]. Key: Insurance Cloud on FSC is composed of separately licensed modules (Brokerage, Claims Management, Policy Administration, Group Benefits) each surfacing distinct ConnectAPI namespaces — activating one module does not activate others making license-to-feature mapping a critical architectural gate before any workflow design begins. Underwriting rules are managed via the InsuranceUnderwritingRule object and Insurance Product Administration APIs (not native Flow decision elements) with Active/Inactive/Draft statuses. No overlap with fsc-architecture-patterns (broad FSC) or payer-vs-provider-architecture (Health Cloud payer only). LLM anti-pattern: conflating FSC Insurance (P&C/life policy objects) with Health Cloud payer features (MemberPlan) — they are separate licensed products with different object models. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | banking-lending-architecture | Banking and lending architecture: loan origination, account servicing, payment processing integration. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Financial Services Cloud Developer Guide (Salesforce Industries Reference); Financial Services Cloud Data Model Gallery]. Key: Digital Lending — FSC loan origination platform — is built on OmniStudio (OmniScripts, FlexCards, Integration Procedures) and the industriesdigitallending Apex namespace not on FSC standard objects alone; provisioning OmniStudio is a hard prerequisite that is commonly missed. The ResidentialLoanApplication object anchors the data model with child objects (LoanApplicant, LoanApplicantAsset, etc.) and the loanApplicantAutoCreation IndustriesSettings flag must be enabled for automatic Person Account association. Partial overlap with fsc-architecture-patterns on core banking integration patterns but that skill does not cover loan origination or Digital Lending platform architecture. LLM anti-pattern: designing payment processing as synchronous Apex callouts from record-save events violating the 100-callout-per-transaction limit. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |

## Phase 10 — Nonprofit Cloud (NPSP)

### NPSP × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | npsp-household-accounts | NPSP Household Account model: household naming, household management, primary contact designation, merge rules. NOT for FSC households. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Customize Household Names — Salesforce Help (help.salesforce.com); Merge or Split Households — Salesforce Help; What is the Household Account Model? — Salesforce Help; Configure Household Naming — NPSP Trailhead]. Key: NPSP auto-enrolls every Contact in a Household Account (record type Household, default name '[Last Name] Household'); Account Name, Formal Greeting, and Informal Greeting are regenerated by NPSP triggers on Contact name changes — manually overridden names are flagged as Customized and stop auto-updating. Merging households requires NPSP's Merge Duplicate Contacts flow, not the native Salesforce merge UI, because native merge bypasses NPSP triggers leaving household names, rollups, and relationship records stale. NPSP Household Accounts use a direct Contact-Account lookup (no junction object); FSC uses ACR junction — the two models are incompatible. LLM anti-pattern: advising use of native Account merge UI for NPSP deduplication, which corrupts rollup totals and household naming.|
| DONE | gift-entry-and-processing | Gift entry setup: gift entry templates, batch gift entry, payment processing, donation allocation, receipting. NOT for standard opportunity creation. | Researched 2026-04-06. Sources: [Salesforce Help — Configure Gift Entry (NPSP); Salesforce Fundraising Dev Guide — GiftEntry Object and processGiftEntries Action (API v59.0+); Trailhead — Set Up Gift Entry in Nonprofit Success Pack]. Key: Gift Entry uses a staging object (GiftEntry, API v59.0+) — gifts are stored in staging records before the processGiftEntries invocable action promotes them to GiftTransaction, GiftDesignation, and GiftSoftCredit target records, supporting an isDryRun validation pass; Advanced Mapping must be enabled before Gift Entry can be activated. Default Gift Entry Template is the only template usable for single-gift entry — custom templates are batch-only; TaxReceiptStatus tracked on GiftTransaction (API v62.0+). No overlap with existing skills. LLM anti-pattern: conflating NPSP Gift Entry with direct Opportunity creation — skipping processGiftEntries leaves records in staging and never produces GiftTransaction or allocation records.|
| DONE | recurring-donations-setup | Recurring Donations setup: installments, schedules, amount changes, status tracking, payment methods. NOT for standard opportunity products. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [NPSP Recurring Donations Overview - Salesforce Help; Configure Recurring Donations - Salesforce Help; Manage Recurring Donations - Trailhead]. Key: Enhanced Recurring Donations (ERD), default since March 2021, generates only one future pledged installment Opportunity at a time (not 12 like legacy) -- LLM anti-pattern is assuming all future installments exist as Opportunity records. Schedules are driven by npe03__RecurringDonationSchedule__c objects; the Upcoming Installments UI shows projected installments from schedule calculations (not actual records), so manual edits to future Opportunities are invisible there. Amount or schedule changes use an Effective Date field; Active/Lapsed/Closed status can be automated by days-unpaid thresholds; nightly batch recalculates Total Paid Amount and Number of Paid Installments rollups. |
| DONE | soft-credits-and-matching | Soft credit management: matching gifts, corporate giving attribution, soft credit roles, partial credits. NOT for standard opportunity contact roles. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [Soft Credits Overview — NPSP Help; Manage Soft Credits — NPSP Help; Configure Matching Gifts — NPSP Help; Donation Soft Credit Management with NPSP — Trailhead]. Key: NPSP soft credits are driven by OpportunityContactRole records — partial credits use the custom npsp__Partial_Soft_Credit__c object; soft credit rollup fields on Contact/Account update only via nightly batch or manual recalculation, not in real time. Known platform bug: using Find Matched Gifts for a contact with multiple gifts against one matching gift opportunity creates duplicate OCRs and Partial_Soft_Credit__c records inflating rollup totals. Distinct scope from gift-entry-and-processing (covers staging flow, not soft credit roles or matching gift OCR automation). LLM anti-pattern: confusing standard OCR-based household auto-credits with explicit matching gift partial soft credits, which require a separate Matching Gift opportunity record linked via Find Matched Gifts. |
| DONE | npsp-program-management | Program management module: program setup, cohorts, services, service deliveries, outcome tracking, attendance. NOT for case management. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [Program Management Module Managed Package (help.salesforce.com); Program Management Module Documentation (help.salesforce.com); Service Delivery with Program Management Module — Trailhead; Customize Bulk Service Deliveries (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: PMM is a separate managed package (not core NPSP) with eight custom objects — Program__c, Service__c, ProgramEngagement__c, ProgramCohort__c, ServiceDelivery__c, ServiceSchedule__c, ServiceParticipant__c; Bulk Service Delivery field set requires Client first, Program Engagement second, Service third — marking fields required in the field set does NOT enforce save validation (must use validation rules). Rowlock errors occur under concurrent bulk saves. No duplicate — existing NPSP skills are donor-side; PMM is beneficiary/program-delivery-side, fully distinct. LLM anti-pattern: conflating PMM with NPSP case management or assuming PMM records roll up into NPSP donation reporting — they do not share rollup or trigger infrastructure. |
| DONE | grant-management-setup | Grant management: funding requests, deliverables, milestones, compliance requirements, reporting, disbursements. NOT for standard opportunity tracking. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [Grants Management Product Documentation (Salesforce Help); Manage Funding Awards and Disbursements (Trailhead); Fund Management Requirements and Disbursements Guide (Trailhead); Grantmaking and Budget Management Data Model (Salesforce Developers)]. Key: Two distinct paths exist — NPSP uses Outbound Funds Module (managed package, Opportunity-based) for basic tracking; Nonprofit Cloud for Grantmaking (now Agentforce Nonprofit, requires separate licensing) uses FundingAward, FundingDisbursement (payment tranches), and FundingAwardRequirement (deliverables, status: Open→Submitted→Approved) as purpose-built objects; the two platforms are architecturally incompatible for migration without data transformation. No overlap with npsp-household-accounts or gift-entry-and-processing (different NPSP domains). LLM anti-pattern: conflating NPSP Outbound Funds Module with Nonprofit Cloud for Grantmaking — they have entirely different data models, licensing, and upgrade paths; recommending one when the org uses the other produces incorrect guidance. |
| DONE | npsp-engagement-plans | Engagement plan templates: donor stewardship, event follow-up, volunteer engagement, automated task creation. NOT for marketing campaigns. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Configure Engagement Plans — Salesforce Help (sfdo.npsp_config_engage_plans); Create and Manage Engagement Plans — Salesforce Help; Engagement Plans and Levels NPSP — Trailhead; NPSP GitHub Issue #3687]. Key: Engagement Plans create standard Task records only — they do NOT send emails, update fields, or post to Chatter; three objects: npsp__Engagement_Plan_Template__c (template), npsp__Engagement_Plan__c (instance applied to a record), npsp__Engagement_Plan_Task__c (generated tasks); templates are stored as data not metadata — Change Sets cannot deploy them, use manual recreation or data migration; template changes are NOT retroactive to existing plans; Auto-Update Child Due Date recalculates only when parent task is marked Complete (not when its due date is edited); plans can be applied to Account/Contact/Opportunity/Campaign/Case/Recurring Donation or custom objects (requires enabling Activities, adding lookup to npsp__Engagement_Plan__c). LLM anti-pattern: conflating Engagement Plans with automation — plans create Tasks only; must be paired with Flow for emails/field updates/Chatter posts. |

### NPSP × BA Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | fundraising-process-mapping | Fundraising process design: cultivation, solicitation, stewardship cycles, major gift workflow, donor pipeline. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Moves Management with Nonprofit Success Pack (Trailhead); Opportunity Settings in Nonprofit Success Pack (Trailhead)]. Key: NPSP ships four pre-configured Opportunity sales processes (Donation, Grant, In-Kind, Major Gift) each with its own stage picklist values; the Opportunity Stage field drives the cultivation to solicitation to stewardship lifecycle. As of December 2025 NPSP is no longer offered as a pre-configured package in new production orgs so guidance must flag whether the org is on legacy NPSP or Nonprofit Cloud (NPC). Not duplicated by npsp-engagement-plans (implementation mechanics) or sales-process-mapping (generic non-nonprofit). LLM anti-pattern: recommending NPSP Engagement Plan setup on NPC orgs where the feature does not exist in the same form. |
| DONE | program-outcome-tracking-design | Program outcome measurement: logic model design, indicator tracking, impact reporting requirements, evaluation. Key: PMM (pmdm namespace) ships NO dedicated Outcome or Indicator objects -- the package provides 8 operational objects (Program__c, Service__c, ProgramEngagement__c, ProgramCohort__c, ServiceDelivery__c, ServiceSchedule__c, ServiceParticipant__c, ServiceSession__c) where outcomes are captured only as Quantity__c plus UnitOfMeasurement__c on ServiceDelivery__c and Stage__c picklist on ProgramEngagement__c. Structured logic-model indicator tracking requires custom objects or custom fields built by the implementor. Newer Nonprofit Cloud (NPC) has separate Outcome Management feature with dedicated objects -- skill must explicitly scope to NPSP-PMM vs NPC. Overlap risk: skills/admin/npsp-program-management covers PMM configuration; this skill focuses on design layer (logic model structure, indicator taxonomy, report design for grant compliance). Key: NPSP/NPC models donor lifecycle through Moves Management stages, Engagement Plans for upgrade paths, ERD status transitions (Active to Lapsed to Closed) for re-engagement triggers, LYBUNT reports for lapsed donors, and Actionable Segmentation for classification. As of December 2025 NPSP is no longer offered in new production orgs. Overlaps with npsp-engagement-plans and recurring-donations-setup but addresses full lifecycle requirements mapping not individual feature mechanics. LLM anti-pattern: conflating Nonprofit Cloud Actionable Segmentation with marketing automation — segmentation here means donor classification for upgrade/re-engagement strategy not campaign execution. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | volunteer-management-requirements | Volunteer management process: recruitment, scheduling, hours tracking, recognition, skills matching. NOT for HR systems. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Volunteers for Salesforce (V4S) Managed Package — Salesforce.org Open Source Commons; Nonprofit Cloud Developer Guide: Introduction to Nonprofit Cloud]. Key: Two distinct platforms handle volunteer management — NPSP orgs use V4S open-source managed package (Volunteer Campaign/Job/Shift/Hours objects; no native skills-matching; recognition is custom-built) while Nonprofit Cloud uses native Volunteer Initiative and Job Position Assignment objects with TotalVolunteerHours calculated by Data Processing Engine as a scheduled batch job not real-time. No existing skill overlaps with this scope. LLM anti-pattern: conflating V4S (managed package for NPSP) with NPC-native volunteer objects generating SOQL that mixes namespaces or assumes real-time rollup recalculation without a scheduled DPE run. |

### NPSP × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `apex`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | npsp-trigger-framework-extension | Extending NPSP trigger framework (TDTM): custom trigger handlers, recursion management, NPSP-specific patterns. NOT for standard Apex triggers. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Deploy a Custom Apex Class in the TDTM Framework for NPSP — Salesforce Help (sfdo.npsp_deploy_apex_tdtm); Manage Trigger Handlers for NPSP — Salesforce Help (sfdo.NPSP_Manage_Trigger_Handlers); SalesforceFoundation/NPSP GitHub — ACCT_Accounts_TDTM.cls; NPSP GitHub Issue #690]. Key: Custom handlers extend npsp.TDTM_Runnable (npsp. namespace required) and override run(List newRecs, List oldRecs, TDTM_Runnable.Action triggerAction, DescribeSObjectResult objResult) — return a DmlWrapper (add to objectsToInsert/Update/Delete) instead of issuing direct DML; register via npsp__Trigger_Handler__c records with fields: npsp__Class__c, npsp__Object__c, npsp__Trigger_Action__c (semicolon-delimited e.g. AfterInsert;AfterUpdate), npsp__Load_Order__c (use values higher than packaged handlers with gaps), npsp__Owned_by_Namespace__c (prevents NPSP upgrades from deleting custom handlers); recursion guard must use static Set<Id> (custom code cannot add flags to TDTM_ProcessControl.flag enum); test isolation via npsp.TDTM_Global_API.setTdtmConfig() — do NOT call getTdtmConfig() first (cache bug causes custom handlers to silently skip). LLM anti-pattern: issuing direct DML inside run() instead of DmlWrapper; omitting Owned_by_Namespace__c causing NPSP upgrade to silently delete custom handlers; using npsp. namespace prefix on class extends without testing in subscriber org context. |
| DUPLICATE | gift-entry-customization | Gift entry customization: custom templates, payment gateway integration, form field customization, validation. NOT for standard form development. | Covered by skills/admin/gift-entry-and-processing |
| DONE | npsp-api-and-integration | NPSP API: gift processing API, recurring donation API, wealth screening integration, third-party connectors. NOT for standard Salesforce API. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Recurring Donations Schedules API (NPSP Help); Recurring Donations Installments API (NPSP Help); NPSP Data Import Administrator Guide; NPSP BDI_DataImport_API source (SalesforceFoundation GitHub)]. Key: The primary NPSP gift-processing API is the Bulk Data Import (BDI) framework -- integrations must insert records into npsp__DataImport__c and invoke BDI_DataImport_API programmatically rather than direct-inserting Opportunity and Payment records, which bypasses NPSP allocation, soft-credit, and household rollup logic. The Enhanced Recurring Donations (ERD) API exposes two Apex-invocable surfaces: RD2 Schedules API (returns projected schedule JSON) and RD2 Installments API (returns calculated future installments, NOT persisted Opportunity records) -- LLMs routinely confuse these. Wealth screening tools (iWave, DonorSearch) integrate via AppExchange managed packages that write scores to Contact/Account custom fields; there is no built-in NPSP wealth screening API. LLM anti-pattern: generating direct Opportunity inserts instead of routing through BDI pipeline, silently skipping rollups and Elevate payment linkage. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | npsp-custom-rollups | Custom rollup summaries in NPSP: rollup configuration, custom fiscal years, custom filter groups, CRLP. NOT for standard rollup summaries. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Customizable Rollups Overview — NPSP Help; Configure Customizable Rollups — NPSP Help; Create Filter Groups — NPSP Help; Batch Job Modes for Customizable Rollups — NPSP Help]. Key: CRLP replaces legacy NPSP rollups one-way — enabling it removes existing user-defined rollups, silently breaking dependent formula fields or automations. Configuration uses linked Rollup Definition and Filter Group objects; filter group names are limited to 40 characters and large filter group saves can time out. Critical gotcha: CRLP rollups are batch-driven, not real-time — they require scheduled or manual recalculation via NPSP Settings > Batch Processing with three job modes (Incremental, Full, Scheduled). |

### NPSP × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | constituent-data-migration | Constituent data migration: contact import, household creation, relationship mapping, duplicate detection. NOT for standard contact import. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [How NPSP Data Importer Processes Data — Salesforce Help; Configure Duplicate Detection and NPSP Contact Merge — Salesforce Help; NPSP Data Model for Nonprofit Organizations — Trailhead]. Key: NPSP uses the dedicated NPSP Data Importer (not standard Data Import Wizard), staging records in npsp__DataImport__c — each row maps Contact1+Contact2, a Household Account, org accounts, home address, and a donation with auto-created households via configurable Contact Matching Rules. Critical gotcha: importing Contacts via Data Loader or standard import bypasses NPSP Apex triggers entirely, leaving Household Account rollups stale and creating orphaned one-contact households — always use the NPSP Data Importer or NPSP-aware APIs for constituent migration. |
| DONE | gift-history-import | Donation and gift history import: payment mapping, soft credit creation, campaign attribution, GAU allocation. NOT for standard opportunity import. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Standard NPSP Data Import Fields (Salesforce Help); Configure NPSP Data Importer (Salesforce Help); How NPSP Data Importer Processes Data (Salesforce Help); Advanced NPSP Mapping (Salesforce Help)]. Key: NPSP Data Importer uses staging object DataImport__c (BDI) to bulk-create Opportunities, OppPayment records, Opportunity Contact Roles (soft credits), GAU Allocations, and Campaign Members in a single pass -- direct Data Loader inserts to Opportunity bypass all BDI automation leaving OCRs, GAU allocations, and payment records missing. Supports up to 50,000 records per batch file (100 MB max); Advanced Mapping must be enabled to map custom payment/GAU fields or they silently go unmapped. LLM anti-pattern: loading gift history directly into npe01__OppPayment__c or Opportunity via Data Loader, bypassing DataImport__c. |
| DONE | npsp-data-model | NPSP data model: NPSP objects, relationship objects, GAU allocations, recurring donation objects, data dictionary. NOT for standard data model. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [NPSP Data Model Gallery - Salesforce Developers; NPSP Objects and Fields Data Dictionary - Salesforce Help; Trailhead - Explore the NPSP Data Model]. Key: NPSP uses four distinct namespace prefixes -- npe01__ (Households/Payments: npe01__OppPayment__c), npe03__ (Recurring Donations: npe03__Recurring_Donation__c), npe4__ (Relationships), npe5__ (Affiliations), and npsp__ (GAU Allocations: npsp__Allocation__c, General Accounting Units: npsp__General_Accounting_Unit__c) -- LLMs commonly collapse these to a single npsp__ prefix generating wrong API names for half the objects. GAU Allocations link Opportunities to multiple General Accounting Units via lookup (not master-detail) so deleting an Opportunity does not cascade-delete its allocations. Direct creation of installment Opportunities without parent npe03__Recurring_Donation__c bypasses schedule tracking and breaks rollup fields on Contact and Account. |
| DONE | nonprofit-data-quality | Nonprofit data quality: address standardization, duplicate household detection, NCOA processing, data hygiene. NOT for generic data quality. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [NPSP Address Management Overview (help.salesforce.com); About National Change of Address Updates (help.salesforce.com); Configure Duplicate Detection and NPSP Contact Merge (help.salesforce.com); Insights Platform Data Integrity (Trailhead)]. Key: NPSP stores addresses as npsp__Address__c objects linked to Household Accounts enabling multiple addresses per household; address verification integrates with Cicero/Google Geocoding/SmartyStreets but only validates records created after setup, historical records need a separate mass-verification run. NCOA processing requires the separately licensed Insights Platform Data Integrity add-on (premium subscription, incompatible with Agentforce Nonprofit). LLM anti-pattern: recommending standard Salesforce duplicate rules or native Account merge for NPSP households -- requires NPSP Contact Merge flow so Apex triggers fire and rollup totals recalculate correctly. |

### NPSP × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | npsp-vs-nonprofit-cloud-decision | Decision framework: NPSP (open source) vs new Nonprofit Cloud, migration path, feature comparison, timeline. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [Nonprofit Cloud Migration and Implementation Guides (Salesforce Help); Nonprofit Cloud Developer Guide — Introduction to Nonprofit Cloud]. Key: Salesforce ended all new feature development for NPSP in March 2023 when Nonprofit Cloud (NPC) launched; NPSP is now feature-frozen with no hard EOL date announced, making NPC the only path to future innovation; there is no in-place upgrade path — organizations must provision a new org, rebuild configurations, then migrate data. No duplicate (nearest skill admin/npsp-household-accounts covers internal NPSP config only; this skill is a distinct decision-framework scope). LLM anti-pattern: telling users they can upgrade an existing NPSP org to Nonprofit Cloud — this is false; NPC uses a fundamentally different data model (Person Accounts by default vs. Household Accounts, new Fundraising and Program Management objects) and always requires a net-new org plus formal data migration. |
| DONE | nonprofit-platform-architecture | Nonprofit platform architecture: program management, fundraising, engagement, volunteer, reporting strategy. NOT for individual feature design. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Nonprofit Cloud Developer Guide: Introduction to Nonprofit Cloud (developer.salesforce.com); Nonprofit Cloud Data Model Gallery (developer.salesforce.com); Volunteer Management Data Model (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Nonprofit Cloud (rebranded Agentforce Nonprofit Oct 2025) is a native Industry Cloud built on the Standard Industry Data Model with Person Accounts -- NOT a managed package like NPSP -- spanning six independently adoptable modules: Fundraising (Connect API v59.0+), Program/Case Management, Outcome Management, Volunteer Management (19 objects), Grantmaking, and AI/Agentforce agents. Distinct from npsp-vs-nonprofit-cloud-decision skill; this skill covers holistic architecture strategy across all modules. LLM anti-pattern: conflating NPSP configuration patterns (npsp namespace objects, CRLP rollups) with Nonprofit Cloud -- entirely separate data models with no in-place upgrade path. |
| DONE | fundraising-integration-patterns | Fundraising system integration: payment gateway, wealth screening, email marketing, event platforms. NOT for generic integration. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Nonprofit Cloud Developer Guide -- GiftTransaction and Connect API (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce.org Elevate Payment Services documentation (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: NPSP and Nonprofit Cloud support payment gateway integration via Salesforce.org Elevate (Payment Services) which exposes Connect REST API at /connect/fundraising/transactions/payment-updates (POST) to update gateway metadata on GiftTransaction records from API v59.0+; wealth screening tools integrate via AppExchange managed packages writing scores to Contact/Account fields, not a native Salesforce API. LLM anti-pattern: recommending custom Apex blng.PaymentGateway adapter for NPSP payment processing -- that interface is for Salesforce Billing only; Elevate connector is not replaceable with custom Apex. |
| DONE | nonprofit-data-architecture | Nonprofit data architecture: constituent 360, household model, giving history, program participation, reporting. NOT for standard data model. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [NPSP Data Model Gallery — developer.salesforce.com; Nonprofit Cloud Data Model Developer Guide (Spring '26); Trailhead: Explore the NPSP Data Model]. Key: NPSP constituent 360 uses three layers: HH_Account (record type on standard Account) for household grouping, Contact for the individual, and npo02__ namespace rollup fields (npo02__TotalOppAmount__c, last gift date, streak) driven by Customizable Rollups engine against Opportunity and npe01__OppPayment__c. Program participation uses PMM objects pmdm__ServiceDelivery__c, pmdm__Program__c, pmdm__ProgramEngagement__c (separate pmdm__ namespace, separate managed package from NPSP core). Critical LLM anti-pattern: conflating NPSP Household Account model with Nonprofit Cloud's independent data model or FSC's AccountContactRelationship-based Household Group — these are three incompatible architectures. |

## Phase 11 — Commerce Cloud

### Commerce Cloud × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | b2b-commerce-store-setup | B2B Commerce store setup: storefront configuration, buyer groups, entitlements, account management, catalogs. NOT for B2C Commerce. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Buyer Group Data Limits; B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Entitlement Data Limits; Salesforce Help — Set Up a Storefront; Trailhead — Organize Commerce Store Access: Buyer Accounts and Groups]. Key: Core model is WebStore → BuyerGroup (via WebStoreBuyerGroup) → CommerceEntitlementPolicy (via CommerceEntitlementBuyerGroup) → BuyerAccount/BuyerGroupMember; hard limit of 200 BuyerGroups per EntitlementPolicy cannot be raised, and a product entitled across more than 2,000 buyer groups per store causes silent search indexing exclusions beyond that cap. No local coverage found. LLM anti-pattern: assuming all Contacts under a BuyerAccount automatically get storefront access — only contacts explicitly assigned Buyer or Buyer Manager roles can transact; omitting this step causes silent access failures that appear as entitlement misconfiguration. |
| DONE | b2c-commerce-store-setup | B2C Commerce (SFCC) store configuration: cartridges, site configuration, customer management, storefronts. NOT for B2B Commerce. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [B2C Commerce Developer Guide — Architecture and Site Management (developer.salesforce.com); SFRA Developer Guide — Configure SFRA; Trailhead — Architecture of Commerce Cloud Digital; Trailhead — Guide to B2C Commerce Cartridges; SFCC Quota Survival Guide (rhino-inquisitor.com)]. Key: B2C Commerce (SFCC) runs on proprietary infrastructure managed via Business Manager — no WebStore/BuyerGroup/CommerceEntitlementPolicy objects exist (entirely distinct from B2B Commerce on Lightning); site created at Administration > Sites > Manage Sites > New (ID max 32 alphanumeric chars, no spaces); SFRA cartridge path is colon-separated left-to-right, custom cartridges go LEFT of app_storefront_base (never modify app_storefront_base directly — voids upgrade compatibility); key limits: active promotions performance threshold 1,000 (hard limit 10,000), max 400 product line items per basket, session 10 KB, API HTTPClient calls per page max 16, custom objects max 400,000 replicable per instance; search index must be manually rebuilt after catalog/preference changes — no auto-index trigger. LLM anti-pattern: applying B2B Commerce data model concepts (WebStore, IsBuyer, BuyerGroup) to SFCC setup; modifying app_storefront_base directly. |
| DONE | commerce-product-catalog | Commerce product catalog: categories, product attributes, entitlement policies, catalog configuration, variants. NOT for CPQ product catalog. | Researched 2026-04-07. Sources: [Product and Catalog Data Model — B2B Commerce Developer Guide; Entitlement Data Limits — B2B Commerce Developer Guide; Product Variations and Attributes — Salesforce Help; Commerce Product and Category APIs — B2B Commerce Developer Guide]. Key: A store can be associated with only one ProductCatalog but a catalog can serve multiple stores; core objects are ProductCatalog, ProductCategory, ProductCategoryProduct (junction), WebStoreCatalog, and CommerceEntitlementPolicy; buyer entitlements per product capped at 2,000 for search indexing — groups beyond 2,000 silently excluded from search results. Distinct from admin/cpq-product-catalog-setup (CPQ bundles/options) and data/product-catalog-data-model (standard Product2/Pricebook2 loading). LLM anti-pattern: confusing Commerce Cloud ProductCatalog/ProductCategory with CPQ catalog concepts or standard Pricebook2-based pricing, or assuming a store can reference multiple catalogs. |
| DONE | commerce-pricing-and-promotions | Commerce pricing: pricebooks for commerce, promotions, coupons, tiered pricing, cart-level discounts, rules. NOT for CPQ pricing. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Pricing and Promotions APIs; Promotions Data Model — B2B and D2C Commerce Developer Guide; Promotions Data Limits; Price Book Data Limits (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Help — Set Up a Pricing Strategy in a B2B Store]. Key: Pricebooks attach to stores via WebStorePricebook (max 5 per store) and to BuyerGroups via BuyerGroupPricebook (max 50 pricebooks per BuyerGroup, max 100 BuyerGroups per pricebook); price resolution evaluates at most 25 pricebooks per call — extras silently excluded; tiered pricing uses PriceAdjustmentSchedule (API v60.0+) + PriceAdjustmentTier (API v47.0+) linked to PricebookEntry; promotions scope via PromotionSegmentSalesStore and PromotionSegmentBuyerGroup junctions; evaluate API applies at most 50 automatic + 50 manual promotions ranked by Priority (extras silently ignored); hard limits: max 5 coupon codes per cart, max 24 item-level + 6 order-level adjustments per cart; promotions do NOT apply automatically — checkout flow must include the Promotions subflow (PromotionsCartCalculator). LLM anti-pattern: assigning pricebooks via standard Sales Cloud Pricebook2Id on Account/Opportunity — Commerce requires WebStorePricebook+BuyerGroupPricebook; assuming Promotion activation alone applies discounts without the checkout flow integration. |
| DONE | commerce-checkout-configuration | Checkout flow configuration: payment methods, shipping methods, tax calculation, guest checkout, order summary. NOT for CPQ quoting. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Checkout Flow Architecture; Shipping and Tax Integration — B2B Commerce Developer Guide; Payment Architecture — B2B and D2C Commerce Developer Guide; Set Up Guest Checkout for Headless Commerce Stores]. Key: Checkout is orchestrated via CartCheckoutSession progressing through sequential states (inventory, shipping, tax, payment authorization, order creation) — LWR stores use Managed Checkout while Aura stores use Flow Builder checkout flows. Payment requires an Apex Payment Adapter class bridging Salesforce to the gateway; shipping and tax fetched in a single async API call on address entry. Gotcha: billing address must be set on the cart before order creation or OrderSummary silently lacks billing contact data; guest checkout requires email and phone in shipping address fields. |
| DONE | commerce-order-management | Order management: order lifecycle, fulfillment, returns, exchanges, order status tracking, order summaries. NOT for CPQ orders. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Salesforce Order Management Developer Guide v66.0 Spring '26; Connect REST API Developer Guide — Order Management Actions; Platform Events Developer Guide — FOStatusChangedEvent, OrderSumStatusChangedEvent, OrderSummaryCreatedEvent]. Key: Core objects: Order (must be activated to trigger OMS) → OrderSummary (OrderLifeCycleType: MANAGED or UNMANAGED, immutable after creation) → OrderItemSummary + OrderDeliveryGroupSummary → FulfillmentOrder + FulfillmentOrderLineItem → ReturnOrder + ReturnOrderLineItem; in MANAGED mode all quantity/price changes must use Connect API core actions (submit-cancel, submit-return, adjust-item-submit) — direct DML on OrderItemSummary will fail or produce inconsistencies; ensure-funds-async and ensure-refunds-async are enqueued async jobs (subscribe to ProcessExceptionEvent for errors); adjust-item-submit can produce up to 3 separate change orders (pre/in/post-fulfillment splits); CPQ orders do NOT create OrderSummary records — OMS requires a separate Salesforce Order Management/Commerce license. LLM anti-pattern: recommending direct DML updates to OrderItemSummary/Order after a Managed OrderSummary exists; conflating submit-return (change order only, no ReturnOrder) with the formal ReturnOrder path for RMA+refund workflows. |

### Commerce Cloud × BA Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | b2b-vs-b2c-requirements | B2B vs B2C Commerce requirements: buyer journey differences, account-based vs consumer features, licensing. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Developer Guide (Salesforce Developers); B2B and D2C Commerce Licenses (Salesforce Help)]. Key: B2B Commerce requires account-based access gated by BuyerGroup and CommerceEntitlementPolicy records — anonymous/guest purchasing is not the default and requires explicit enablement (added Winter 24) while D2C Commerce supports guest checkout natively; both share the same WebStore object and LWR framework but diverge at the buyer-entitlement layer. Licensing is separate: B2B unlocks BuyerGroup-gated catalog and contract pricing; D2C enables consumer storefront flow. Distinct from admin/b2b-commerce-store-setup and admin/b2c-commerce-store-setup (implementation mechanics) — this skill covers the pre-build platform selection decision. | DONE | commerce-checkout-flow-design | Checkout flow UX design: cart requirements, payment options, shipping rules, guest vs registered experience. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Developer Guide — Checkout Flow; B2B Commerce Checkout Flow (Aura) — Salesforce Developer Documentation]. Key: Salesforce Commerce supports only two mutually exclusive checkout runtime models (LWR Managed Checkout via Extension Points vs Aura via Flow Builder) and design decisions must be locked to one model before any configuration begins since migration requires a full storefront rebuild — no hybrid path exists. Potential overlap with admin/commerce-checkout-configuration which may already subsume the design-only framing — verify scope of existing skill before building. LLM anti-pattern: describing a unified checkout flow applying to both store types — Experience Builder Flow configuration has zero effect on LWR stores and vice versa; always confirm store template type first. |
| DONE | commerce-catalog-strategy | Product catalog strategy: taxonomy design, attribute management, search and navigation requirements, merchandising. Key: Salesforce distinguishes a product catalog (system-of-record import, not site-assigned) from a storefront catalog (navigation structure, one per site) -- conflating the two at design time is the primary LLM anti-pattern. D2C/B2C stores support max 50 searchable fields/attributes per product (exceeding breaks next search index rebuild); search uses full-token matching only with no prefix or infix support, constraining attribute taxonomy and search UX decisions. No duplicate; existing admin/commerce-product-catalog covers configuration, not strategy. |
| DONE | digital-storefront-requirements | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2C Commerce Storefront Options (developer.salesforce.com); SFRA Standards Compliance (developer.salesforce.com); SFRA Features and Components (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Salesforce Commerce Cloud offers two primary storefront architectures: SFRA (server-side, Bootstrap 4, cartridge-based) and PWA Kit/Composable Storefront (React/Node.js, SCAPI-driven, recommended for new builds); SFRA branding is customized exclusively through overlay cartridges prefixed app_custom_* without touching app_storefront_base; accessibility compliance (WCAG 2.1 AA) is the merchant's sole legal responsibility — SFRA provides partial AA scaffolding but does not certify compliance. Gotcha: practitioners assume SFRA's Bootstrap 4 responsive layout satisfies WCAG AA compliance by default, but SFRA only implements a small subset of WCAG criteria and full compliance requires merchant-side audit and ongoing testing. | Digital storefront requirements: branding, content management, personalization, mobile experience, accessibility. ### Commerce Cloud × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `lwc` or `apex` as noted

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | commerce-extension-points | Commerce Cloud extension points: checkout extensions, pricing hooks, cart calculators, custom components. NOT for standard LWC. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [B2B Commerce Extensions — Available Extensions; Cart Calculate API — B2B Commerce Developer Guide; Commerce Apex Reference — CartCalculate; Get Started with B2B Commerce Extensions]. Key: Extensions use the CartExtension Apex namespace — custom cart calculators extend CartExtension.PricingCartCalculator (EPN: Commerce_Domain_Pricing_CartCalculator), all registered via RegisteredExternalService metadata. Extensions are synchronous Apex — DML is not permitted inside hooks, callouts are only allowed in before hooks not after hooks. LLM anti-pattern: writing async or @future Apex inside a cart calculator causes runtime exceptions since extensions run inline during cart recalculation. |
| DONE | headless-commerce-api | Headless Commerce development: Commerce API, storefront API, custom frontends, React/Angular integration. NOT for standard storefront. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [B2C Commerce API -- Why Use SCAPI (developer.salesforce.com); Headless Commerce with Salesforce Commerce API -- Composable Storefront (developer.salesforce.com); B2B Commerce APIs -- Storefront APIs (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: SCAPI is the mandatory replacement for OCAPI for all new headless storefronts -- it splits into Shopper APIs (customer-facing: browse, basket, checkout) and Admin APIs, uses SLAS (Shopper Login and API Access Service) OAuth2 JWT tokens rather than Account Manager sessions, and implements load-shedding at 90% server capacity (HTTP 503) rather than uniform hard rate limits. Commerce SDK React (react-query hooks) is the recommended frontend integration layer. Partial overlap with skills/admin/headless-commerce-architecture (architecture patterns) -- this skill is scoped to SCAPI development and custom frontend wiring. LLM anti-pattern: assuming OCAPI session/hook patterns apply to SCAPI, or applying response-level caching instead of object-level caching. |
| DONE | commerce-payment-integration | Payment gateway integration: payment adapters, custom payment methods, PCI compliance patterns, tokenization. NOT for billing. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Developer Guide -- Payment Architecture; B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Developer Guide -- Commerce Payment Gateway; Apex Developer Guide -- Payment Gateway Adapters]. Key: The Commerce payment framework uses the CommercePayments Apex namespace; all gateway adapters implement a processRequest method handling RequestType values including Tokenize, Auth, PostAuth, Capture, ReferencedRefund, and AuthorizationReversal. PCI compliance is achieved by isolating raw card data in the cross-domain client-side component owned by the payment provider -- the Apex adapter only ever sees a tokenized reference, never card numbers or CVV. Three integration paths: Salesforce Payments (native Stripe, supports Apple Pay), vetted AppExchange packages, and fully custom CommercePayments Apex adapters. Overlap risk: skills/admin/commerce-checkout-configuration covers sfdc_checkout.CartPaymentAuthorize adapter pattern. LLM anti-pattern: conflating CommercePayments namespace with the older sfdc_checkout.CartPaymentAuthorize interface, or routing raw card data through Apex. |
| DONE | commerce-search-customization | Commerce search: search indexing, faceted navigation, search ranking, product recommendations, Einstein search. NOT for SOSL. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2B Commerce Search Settings APIs — Salesforce Developer Guide; Commerce Einstein APIs — Salesforce Developer Guide; Adjust Criteria for Ranking Storefront Search Results — Salesforce Help]. Key: B2B/D2C Commerce search uses three API-configured attribute sets — Searchable Attributes, Facetable Attributes, Sort Rules — set via Connect REST APIs (POST /commerce/webstores/{webstoreId}/search/indexes) with explicit index rebuild required after changes (capped at 60 rebuilds/hour/store). Einstein recommendations require Activity Tracking API instrumented first; B2B recommenders auto-resolve anchor type. Critical LLM anti-pattern: confusing Commerce search (WebStore-scoped, BuyerGroup-governed, 2000 BuyerGroup-per-product cap) with SOSL or Experience Cloud search — entitlement visibility enforced at query time so products without entitlement policy silently disappear. |
| DONE | commerce-lwc-components | Custom LWC for Commerce: product display, cart components, checkout components, wishlist, comparison. NOT for standard LWC. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Build Custom Components -- B2B Commerce Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Storefront APIs for Custom LWC (developer.salesforce.com); Commerce Cart and Wishlist APIs (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Custom LWC for B2B/D2C LWR stores uses Commerce Storefront wire adapters (commerce namespace) to bind product data, cart state, and wishlist operations declaratively; LWS and Lightning Locker are both disabled in LWR store templates so components must declare lightningCommunity__RelaxedCSP in capabilities or behave inconsistently. Deployed via SFDX metadata and registered in Experience Builder. LLM anti-pattern: scaffolding standard lightning/ui*Api wire adapters instead of Commerce-specific storefront adapters, or assuming normal Locker security rules apply. |
| DONE | commerce-order-api | Order management API: order creation, fulfillment API, returns processing, order status updates, webhooks. NOT for standard REST API. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Salesforce Order Management Developer Guide v66.0 Spring 26 (developer.salesforce.com); Connect REST API Developer Guide -- Order Management Resources (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Heavy overlap with existing skills/admin/commerce-order-management (search score 4.855) which covers Connect REST API order creation via OrderSummary, FulfillmentOrder routing, cancel/return/adjust actions, ensure-funds/refunds-async, and OMS platform events (FOStatusChangedEvent, ProcessExceptionEvent) as webhook equivalent; this skills scope should be narrowed strictly to B2C Commerce SCAPI/OCAPI Orders API for headless storefront order submission to avoid duplication. LLM anti-pattern: conflating OMS Connect API actions with standard REST CRUD endpoints or doing direct DML on OrderItemSummary in MANAGED mode -- both corrupt financial aggregates. |

### Commerce Cloud × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | product-catalog-migration-commerce | Commerce product catalog migration: category hierarchy, product attributes, images, pricing data, variants. NOT for CPQ product migration. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2B Commerce Import APIs Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Product Data Limits — B2B Commerce Developer Guide]. Key: Commerce Import API (async CSV, /commerce/management/import/product/jobs) is recommended path; synchronous Connect REST import deprecated at API v63.0. Strict load order: ProductCatalog > ProductCategory > Product2 > ProductCategoryProduct > WebStoreCatalog > Pricebook2/PricebookEntry. Hard limits: 3M products/catalog, 200 variants/parent, 9 images/product. Distinct from admin/commerce-product-catalog (post-migration config) and admin/commerce-catalog-strategy (taxonomy planning). Gotcha: LLMs conflate Commerce Import API CSV with Data Loader object insertion; category assignments require separate ProductCategoryProduct records even when using Import API. |
| DONE | commerce-order-history-migration | Order history migration: historical orders, customer purchase history, returns data, payment records. NOT for standard opportunity migration. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Order Management Developer Guide Importing Order Data; Salesforce Help Order Management Object Reference]. Key: Historical order migration requires strict object creation sequence Order (Status=Draft) then OrderDeliveryGroup then OrderItem then Order activation after which OrderSummary must be created via ConnectAPI or Flow core action Create Order Summary never via direct DML insert; historical orders no longer being serviced should use LifeCycleType=Unmanaged which disables refund/fulfillment core actions; LLM anti-pattern is inserting OrderSummary via Bulk API or Data Loader (fails silently) and conflating this skill with CPQ legacy-order migration using SBQQ objects. |
| DONE | commerce-analytics-data | Commerce analytics: conversion funnel data, cart abandonment, product performance, revenue metrics, trends. NOT for CRM Analytics. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2C Commerce Reports and Dashboards App — Trailhead; B2C Commerce Historical Reports: Conversion (documentation.b2c.commercecloud.salesforce.com)]. Key: B2C Commerce analytics live in Business Manager Reports and Dashboards app (9 dashboard types, CSV export capped at 1,000 rows); legacy Business Manager Analytics retired Jan 1 2021. B2B Commerce on Core has no built-in analytics UI — cart abandonment derived via SOQL on WebCart or CRM Analytics B2B Commerce template (bi_template_b2bcommerce). No existing skill covers commerce-native analytics. Gotcha: LLMs conflate the two platforms — B2C analytics are in a separate SaaS Business Manager realm; standard SOQL and Lightning reports do NOT apply to B2C Commerce data. |
| DONE | commerce-inventory-data | Inventory data management: stock levels, warehouse mapping, inventory sync, availability data, reorder points. NOT for FSL inventory. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Omnichannel Inventory OCI Connect REST API Developer Guide; Salesforce Help OCI Inventory IMPEX Best Practices]. Key: OCI exposes real-time inventory availability via REST APIs (availability, reservation, fulfillment, IMPEX bulk upload); batchInventoryUpdate is capped at 100 SKUs per call and bulk IMPEX imports must use gzip for files over 100 MB with spacing enforced between full imports to prevent data corruption; LLM anti-pattern is conflating FSL inventory with OCI stock management and scheduling IMPEX imports too close together which has caused production data inconsistencies. |

### Commerce Cloud × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | b2b-vs-b2c-architecture | B2B vs B2C Commerce architecture decisions: platform features, integration patterns, data model differences. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Data Model and Integration Architecture (developer.salesforce.com); B2C Commerce Developer Guide — SFRA Overview (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Help — B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Intro]. Key: B2B Commerce (on Core) is native Lightning platform using Apex/LWC/Flow with CRM objects (WebStore, BuyerGroup, CommerceEntitlementPolicy, OrderSummary); B2C Commerce (SFCC) is a separate infrastructure with own servers, SFRA cartridge customization, Business Manager — they share NO objects, APIs, or org data. Choose B2B for known business accounts with complex pricing/approvals/quote-to-order/CRM integration; B2C for anonymous consumers at high volume. Critical LLM anti-pattern: conflating the two — Commerce Extensions (pricing/inventory/shipping/tax, Winter '24) apply only to B2B/D2C on Core, not SFCC; B2B checkout is Flow Builder, B2C is SFRA cartridges. |
| DONE | headless-commerce-architecture | Headless Commerce architecture: API-first design, frontend framework selection, performance strategy, caching. NOT for standard storefront. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [B2C Commerce API — Headless Commerce with Salesforce Commerce API (Composable Storefront); B2C Commerce API — Load Shedding and Rate Limiting]. Key: The canonical Salesforce headless commerce stack is Composable Storefront (PWA Kit on Managed Runtime) consuming SCAPI exclusively — SCAPI enforces a hard 10-second Shopper API timeout (HTTP 504) and web-tier cache TTLs capped at 86400 seconds making latency budgets and cache-key design critical architectural decisions. No existing skill covers this domain: architect/headless-vs-standard-experience addresses Experience Cloud (not Commerce Cloud); admin/b2c-commerce-store-setup covers SFRA Business Manager configuration only. LLM anti-pattern: conflating SCAPI/Composable Storefront (Commerce Cloud) with headless Experience Cloud CMS delivery — separate stacks with different auth models (SLAS for SCAPI vs guest/authenticated Community for CMS). |
| DONE | multi-store-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2B Commerce Developer Guide — Product and Catalog Data Model (developer.salesforce.com); Support Multiple Currencies in a Commerce Store (help.salesforce.com); B2C Commerce Architecture and Localization (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: In org-based B2B/D2C Commerce, a WebStore can be associated with only one storefront catalog but a single catalog can be shared across multiple WebStore records — shared catalog does not mean shared pricing or entitlement; each store independently manages buyer groups, entitlement policies, price books, and language/currency. For B2C Commerce (SFCC), multi-store is realized through multiple sites sharing a master catalog in Business Manager; sites across different realms cannot share catalog data natively. Multi-currency requires org-level multi-currency enabled first; carts do not auto-switch currency mid-session. Gotcha: LLMs recommend creating a separate catalog per regional store when the correct pattern is a single shared catalog with locale-specific translations and per-store entitlement configuration. | Multi-store Commerce architecture: shared catalog, localization, multi-currency, multi-language, regional stores. NOT for single store. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | commerce-integration-patterns | Commerce integration: ERP integration, PIM, payment gateways, shipping providers, tax engines, OMS. NOT for generic integration. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [B2B Commerce and D2C Commerce Developer Guide — Payment Architecture (developer.salesforce.com); B2B Commerce Extensions — Cart Calculate API (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Commerce Extensions — Get Started (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: External system integration (ERP, tax, shipping) uses CartExtension Apex namespace — classes extend CartExtension.PricingCartCalculator, ShippingCartCalculator, InventoryCartCalculator, registered via RegisteredExternalService custom metadata with Extension Point Name (EPN); only one class per EPN per store allowed; callouts only permitted in before-phase hooks (after-phase callouts throw System.CalloutException). Payment gateways implement sfdc_checkout.CartPaymentAuthorize — raw card data never transits Salesforce; SOM handles capture/refund if licensed. PIM sync to Product2 has no native connector — use External IDs on Product2 for ERP/PIM upserts to prevent duplicates. |
| DONE | order-management-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Order Management Developer Guide v66.0 Spring '26; Connect REST API Developer Guide — Fulfillment Orders; Routing with Omnichannel Inventory (Salesforce Help)]. Key: OMS split-order architecture routes each OrderDeliveryGroupSummary into one FulfillmentOrder per fulfillment location; the 'Find Routes with Fewest Splits' flow action iteratively tests single locations then pairs to minimize shipment splits; two routing variants exist: Connected Commerce Order Routing (B2B only) and Growth Order Routing (B2B+B2C). Omnichannel Inventory (OCI) is the inventory truth layer that reserves quantities at order placement; OCI availability is eventually consistent so routing decisions can act on slightly stale counts. Returns flow through submit-return to create ReturnOrder records, and refund issuance is deliberately decoupled — the refund job does not fire until the return is explicitly progressed. Gotcha: architects treat OMS routing as a simple 'pick nearest warehouse' rule and overlook that split-order logic requires explicit OCI wiring — if OCI is not provisioned, OMS has no real-time inventory signal and all orders route to a single default location. | Order management architecture: fulfillment workflow, returns process, inventory management strategy, split orders. NOT for individual order setup. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |

| DONE | agentforce-sales-ai-setup | Einstein for Sales setup: opportunity insights, lead scoring, email insights, pipeline inspection, forecasting AI. Sources: [Einstein for Sales Overview — Salesforce Help; Einstein Opportunity Scoring — Salesforce Help; Pipeline Inspection Guidelines and Limits — Salesforce Help]. Key: Near-duplicate of skills/agentforce/einstein-copilot-for-sales; if building separately, key prerequisites are minimum 200 closed opportunities in last two years for Opportunity Scoring (does NOT train in sandboxes) and Collaborative Forecasting enabled before Pipeline Inspection AI insights appear. Gotcha: Einstein email composition requires a separate Einstein Generative AI license beyond the base Einstein for Sales add-on — these are distinct license tiers. |
| DONE | agentforce-service-ai-setup | Einstein for Service setup: case classification, article recommendations, reply recommendations, work summaries. NOT for core Agentforce setup. | Researched 2026-04-10. Sources: [Einstein for Service Setup Guide — Salesforce Help; Einstein AI Features for Service Cloud — Salesforce Docs; Spring 25 Release Notes — Einstein for Service]. Key: Einstein for Service features split across predictive AI (Case Classification, Article Recommendations — require 1000+ closed cases for model training) and generative AI (Reply Recommendations, Work Summaries — require Einstein generative AI add-on or Einstein 1 edition). Work Summaries also requires Messaging or Voice channels plus a Data Cloud entitlement in many configurations. LLM anti-pattern: enabling features without verifying channel and Data Cloud prerequisites, or expecting Classification to work well without sufficient clean historical case data. |
| DONE | einstein-search-personalization | Einstein Search personalization: search results ranking, promoted results, searchable objects, natural language search. NOT for SOSL. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Get Personalized Results — Einstein Search (help.salesforce.com); Manage Einstein Search Settings (help.salesforce.com); Einstein Search Limitations (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: Einstein Search personalization uses four signals — activity (recent/frequent views), location (related record geography), ownership (important contacts), specialization (industry/status) — available in Enterprise, Performance, Unlimited editions with Lightning Experience only. Natural Language Search supports conversational queries but is scoped to Accounts, Contacts, Opportunities, Cases, Leads only; FLS enforced. Einstein Search is English-only; object label renaming does not update NLS (API names drive matching). Setup at Setup > Einstein Search > Settings. Critical LLM anti-pattern: claiming personalization or NLS works across all custom objects or supports multiple languages. |
| DUPLICATE | einstein-activity-capture-admin | Einstein Activity Capture administration: email sync, calendar sync, activity metrics, privacy settings, exclusions. | DUPLICATE | ai-assistant-channel-setup | AI assistant channel deployment: embedded service bot, Slack Agentforce, API access, web deployment, mobile. NOT for standard messaging setup. | Covered by skills/agentforce/agent-channel-deployment. Minor gap: sfap_api OAuth scope added in late 2025 releases not yet documented in existing skill. |

### Agentforce × BA Role

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |

| DONE | ai-use-case-assessment | AI use case assessment: identifying AI opportunities, evaluating feasibility, ROI estimation, data readiness. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-11. Key: The canonical Salesforce framework for AI use case assessment uses an Impact-Effort Matrix with four quadrants (Quick Wins, Low-Hanging Fruit, Big Bets, Money Pits) and evaluates each candidate across four feasibility dimensions: Technical, Operational, Data Readiness (availability, quality, unification, governance scored 1-3 per source), and Risk Profile. ROI estimation uses IRR, NPV, payback period, and opportunity cost -- no single Salesforce-mandated formula exists. Overlap: skills/agentforce/agentforce-service-ai-setup covers prerequisites for Einstein for Service features specifically; skills/architect/ai-ready-data-architecture covers data architecture for AI readiness. Key: Local skill architect/einstein-bot-architecture already covers dialog design, utterance mapping (20+ utterances per intent minimum, 50+ recommended for production), fallback intent behavior, and escalation path design -- this skill must focus tightly on the conversation-script and copy-writing craft layer to avoid duplication. Critical platform behavior: Agentforce topics replace Dialogs, and topic descriptions are the routing signal -- a vague description causes the agent to over-match. Overlap: architect/einstein-bot-architecture covers platform structure; agentforce/agentforce-persona-design covers persona and tone; this skill unique ground is utterance authoring strategy, fallback copy, escalation criteria phrasing, and persona-consistent dialog scripting across channels. | DONE | ai-ethics-and-governance-requirements | AI governance requirements: bias mitigation, transparency, human oversight, audit requirements, responsible AI. NOT for Trust Layer configuration. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Salesforce Trailhead -- AI Governance: Establishing Responsible Practices; Salesforce Trailhead -- Trusted Agentic AI; Salesforce Help -- Detect and Remove Bias from a Model; Salesforce Help -- Implement Data Governance Permissions for Audit]. Key: Salesforce responsible AI framework rests on five pillars (accuracy, safety, honesty, empowerment, sustainability); Einstein Trust Layer provides prompt defense, toxicity scoring, and zero data retention with third-party LLMs; governance requirements include risk inventorying, explainability, AI-generated content disclosures, and timestamped audit trail logging stored in Data Cloud. LLM anti-pattern: conflating AI ethics governance requirements work (policies, human oversight design, regulatory docs) with Trust Layer configuration -- governance is a requirements-gathering exercise distinct from Trust Layer implementation. |
| DONE | ai-adoption-change-management | AI adoption strategy: user training, trust building, feedback collection, success measurement, rollout planning. NOT for general change management. | Researched 2026-04-15. Key: Salesforce's LEVERS model (Leadership, Ecosystem, Values, Enablement, Rewards, Structure) for AI change management is the official framework — successful AI change is 10x more likely when 4+ levers are engaged; distinct from generic change-management-and-training skill which has zero AI-specific content. The Feedback API (thumbs-up/down + reason text, accept/regenerate/decline signals) is the canonical mechanism for collecting structured user feedback on Agentforce responses post-deployment; Agentforce Analytics via Data 360 is the native adoption measurement surface. Critical trust-building pattern: transparency into how the AI model makes decisions — the 'black box' problem is the primary driver of employee AI distrust requiring a communication strategy beyond standard CRM rollout comms. Gaps: success metrics benchmarks for 'good' Agentforce adoption rates by role/use case had no official numeric targets; Dreamforce session content or Salesforce blog posts may be needed during build.|

| DONE | ai-model-integration-apex | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Access Models API with Apex — Agentforce Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Einstein Platform Services Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Apex Developer Guide — Named Credentials as Callout Endpoints (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: The modern path for calling AI models from Apex is the aiplatform.ModelsAPI class (autogenerated via External Services), providing createGenerations(), createChatGenerations(), and createEmbeddings() methods keyed by a model API name such as sfdc_ai__DefaultOpenAIGPT4OmniMini; responses surface at typed paths like Code200.generation.generatedText. Legacy Einstein Vision and Language services use an OAuth 2.0 JWT bearer token flow and that token does not auto-refresh — Apex must manage token lifecycle via Platform Cache to avoid redundant callout overhead. All aiplatform.ModelsAPI calls count against Einstein Request entitlements and standard Apex callout governor limits (100 callouts per transaction, 120s timeout); bulk AI processing must use asynchronous Queueable chains. Gotcha: LLMs treat aiplatform.ModelsAPI as authentication-free because the External Services wrapper hides the token exchange, then skip Platform Cache entirely — causing every transaction to burn a fresh Einstein Request and hit callout-per-transaction limits under moderate load. | Integrating external AI models via Apex: Einstein Platform APIs, external model callouts, response parsing, caching.
