| DONE | data-cloud-vector-search-dev | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Data Cloud Vector Search (Salesforce Help); Data 360 Developer Guide — Features Overview (developer.salesforce.com); Supported Chunking Strategies (Salesforce Help); Search Index Reference — Data Cloud (Salesforce Help)]. Key: Data Cloud vector search (branded Data 360 vector database) stores embedding vectors generated from chunked DMO or Unstructured Data Lake Object text fields; the Salesforce-managed embedding model requires no additional configuration, but chunk size is not tunable in Easy Setup — Advanced Setup is required to adjust chunking strategy and model. The Query API requires a dedicated Data Cloud access token separate from the standard CRM Connected App token; at runtime top-K chunks are injected into the Agentforce prompt via a Grounding configuration record referencing the search index, subject to Einstein Trust Layer masking. Gotcha: LLMs assume chunk size is a free numeric parameter settable in the UI — in practice Easy Setup auto-selects chunk parameters and only Advanced Setup exposes chunking strategy options; developers who skip Advanced Setup cannot tune precision and incorrectly blame retrieval quality on the embedding model. | Data Cloud vector search development: embedding generation, search index configuration, RAG implementation. NOT for Data Cloud admin. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | agentforce-custom-channel-dev | Building custom Agentforce channels: API-based integration, webhook handling, conversation management, session state. NOT for standard channels. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Agentforce Agent API Session Lifecycle (developer.salesforce.com); Bring Your Own Channel for CCaaS Agentforce Service Agent (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: The Agentforce Agent API creates session via POST (UUID as externalSessionKey) uses monotonically increasing sequenceId per message and DELETE to end; context variables at session start are immutable for session lifetime except Context.EndUserLanguage; BYOC for CCaaS uses Interaction API and Establish Conversation API to route through Omni-Channel via messagingEndUser records distinct from raw Agent API usage; overlaps with agentforce/agent-channel-deployment so this skill scopes to webhook handling BYOC integration and custom conversation state design. |

### Agentforce × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | data-cloud-data-streams | Data Cloud data streams: ingesting data, mapping to DMOs, identity resolution, calculated insights, activation. NOT for CRM Analytics data. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Data Cloud Data Streams (Salesforce Help, sf.c360_a_data_streams.htm); Data 360 DMO and Mapping Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Data 360 Limits and Guidelines (Salesforce Help, sf.c360_a_limits_and_guidelines.htm); Real-Time Ingestion API Reference (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Data Cloud ingests data via connectors into Data Lake Objects (DLOs) which are mapped to DMOs using Starter Data Bundles or custom field mapping -- every customer data stream MUST map to both the Individual DMO (Individual ID as primary key, plus FirstName/LastName) AND at least one Contact Point DMO (Email, Phone, Address, App) or Party Identification DMO, or identity resolution rulesets cannot be created; the limit is 2 identity resolution rulesets per org. Calculated Insights are batch-processed SQL-defined metrics for segmentation, distinct from Streaming Insights which process Web/Mobile SDK events in near-real-time. Real-time ingestion (Ingestion API) supports only appends and upserts -- deletions go through the standard pipeline. Overlap: ai-ready-data-architecture covers identity resolution strategy but not step-by-step data stream setup or DMO mapping workflow. LLM anti-pattern: mapping only to the Individual DMO (blocks ruleset creation) or mapping DLO primary key directly to the Party Identification ID field. |
| DONE | ai-training-data-preparation | Preparing data for Einstein: data quality for ML, feature engineering, label generation, dataset curation. NOT for generic data quality. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Einstein Discovery Determine Data Requirements (help.salesforce.com); Einstein Prediction Builder Considerations (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: Einstein Discovery requires minimum 400 rows with outcome values populated; fields below ~70% fill rate are silently dropped from feature selection degrading predictions; leakage is critical with predictors over 30% correlation to outcome requiring scrutiny; LLM anti-pattern is treating outcome field selection as trivial and using proxy fields known only post-outcome which causes inflated model metrics; Einstein Prediction Builder (binary only no CRM Analytics license) and Einstein Discovery (regression and binary CRM Analytics license required) have distinct data preparation paths. IN_PROGRESS 2026-04-16T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | vector-database-management | Vector database setup in Data Cloud: embedding management, search index optimization, data refresh strategies. NOT for standard data management. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Data Cloud Vector Search — Salesforce Help (help.salesforce.com); Data 360 Limits and Guidelines — Salesforce Help]. Key: Vector indexes store embeddings from DMOs/UDLOs; changing embedding model after index creation requires full rebuild. Refresh cadence controlled via Data Stream (batch default; continuous mode for near-real-time). Chunking strategy (Easy vs Advanced Setup) cannot be changed in-place — requires delete+rebuild. Admin levers: chunking strategy, refresh mode, metadata filter design, PII field taxonomy. Partial overlap with skills/agentforce/data-cloud-vector-search-dev (developer lifecycle); this skill scopes to admin/Setup UI workflows only. Gotcha: LLMs recommend raising topK to fix poor retrieval precision — correct fix is chunk strategy via Advanced Setup rebuild, not topK adjustment. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | einstein-analytics-data-model | Einstein/CRM Analytics data model: datasets, dataflows, recipes, data sync from objects, augmented analytics. NOT for standard reporting. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring '26 (knowledge/imports/salesforce-analytics-rest-api.md); skills/admin/analytics-dataflow-development/SKILL.md; skills/admin/analytics-dataset-management/SKILL.md; skills/architect/analytics-data-architecture/SKILL.md]. Key: Significant scope overlap with existing skills — data ingestion mechanics (sfdcDigest, Augment, sfdcRegister, Data Sync incremental) are covered in analytics-dataflow-development; recipe node types are covered in analytics-recipe-design; dataset scheduling and row limits are covered in analytics-dataset-management. Genuine uncovered gap: the multi-layer XMD system (system XMD — platform-generated/immutable, main XMD — org-customizable, user XMD — per-user preference) and dataset versioning model are not covered in any existing skill. Builder should narrow scope exclusively to XMD/dataset-version conceptual model rather than attempting broad 'data model' coverage which would duplicate multiple existing skills. LLM anti-pattern: presenting CRM Analytics data model as analogous to Salesforce object model — datasets are columnar stores with no relationship graph; relationships are expressed in SAQL joins at query time, not as foreign key constraints. Gaps: XMD update API mechanics (PATCH /wave/datasets/{id}/xmds/{xmdtype}), field-level formatting properties, and augmented analytics auto-insights trigger conditions need web search at build time. IN_PROGRESS 2026-04-16T00:00:00Z |

### Agentforce × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | ai-platform-architecture | AI platform architecture: model selection, grounding strategy, trust layer design, multi-agent orchestration. NOT for individual agent design. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [Agentforce Developer Guide — Trust Layer; Enterprise Agentic Architecture and Design Patterns (Salesforce Architects)]. Key: The Einstein Trust Layer enforces a hard context limit of 65536 tokens when data masking is active and guarantees zero data retention by third-party LLM providers — non-negotiable architectural constraints affecting model selection and grounding strategy. Existing skills agentforce/model-builder-and-byollm covers BYOLLM registration and agentforce/rag-patterns-in-salesforce covers grounding mechanics — this skill is distinct covering holistic platform architecture: model tier selection strategy Trust Layer design decisions and multi-agent Supervisor/Specialist topology. LLM anti-pattern: conflating model selection (which model alias to assign in Model Builder) with platform model strategy (when to use Salesforce Default vs BYOLLM vs zero-data-retention partner models) leading to designs routing sensitive data through models without zero-retention agreements. |
| DONE | data-cloud-architecture | Data Cloud architecture: data lake strategy, identity resolution design, activation targets, segmentation strategy. NOT for individual stream setup. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Data 360 Architecture — Salesforce Architects (architect.salesforce.com); Data Cloud Architecture Strategy — Salesforce Help; Activation Targets in Data 360 — Salesforce Help; Building a Complete View with Data Cloud and Identity Resolution — Salesforce Developers Blog]. Key: Data Cloud lakehouse flows DSO (raw) → DLO (cleansed) → DMO (harmonized) → Unified Individual (golden profile); identity resolution uses configurable match rules (exact, fuzzy, normalized, compound) and reconciliation rules (Most Frequent, Most Recent, Source Priority) with automatic transitive matching across clusters. Activation targets: file-based (SFTP/S3/GCS), ad platforms (Meta/Google/LinkedIn/Amazon/TikTok), Salesforce platforms (MC, Core CRM, Commerce) — each needs a separate authenticated connection before segment publish. Critical gotcha: identity resolution only resolves against DMOs with Contact Point or Party Identification mappings — incomplete mapping silently leaves records outside Unified Profile; Calculated Insights add batch lag so time-sensitive filters need Streaming Insights. |
| DONE | ai-governance-architecture | AI governance architecture: model lifecycle, audit trail, responsible AI framework, regulatory compliance design. NOT for general security. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Agent Development Lifecycle — Salesforce Architects (architect.salesforce.com); Salesforce Generative AI Audit Trail (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: AI governance spans 4 layers: AI/ML Lifecycle, Security/Guardrails, Audit/Observability, and Responsible AI Controls. AI Audit Trail requires Data Cloud (no alternative storage); refreshes hourly — real-time detection impossible natively. 30-day audit retention (distinct from 180-day Setup Audit Trail); BYOLLM calls bypass audit trail unless explicitly routed. EU AI Act high-risk compliance required August 2026. Distinct from admin/ai-ethics-and-governance-requirements (policy layer); this skill covers system design — MLOps pipeline topology, audit trail architecture, Policy-as-Code engine. Gotcha: LLMs conflate enabling Einstein Trust Layer with completing AI governance — Trust Layer is one safety layer; full governance encompasses MLOps lifecycle, Policy-as-Code, immutable audit trail on Data Cloud, and regulatory documentation outside platform UI. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | conversational-ai-architecture | Conversational AI architecture: intent classification, dialog management, channel strategy, handoff design. NOT for chatbot configuration. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Agentic Patterns and Implementation with Agentforce (architect.salesforce.com); Enterprise Agentic Architecture and Design Patterns (architect.salesforce.com); The Seamless Handoff: Integrating Einstein Enhanced Bots with Agentforce Agents (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Agentforce uses a declarative Topics-and-Actions model where the Atlas Reasoning Engine performs intent routing at inference time — architecturally distinct from Einstein Bot NLU model training; any skill must draw a sharp line between these two paradigms. The scope overlaps partially with the existing architect/einstein-bot-architecture skill (handoff via Omni-Channel, channel strategy, analytics) but extends to multi-agent orchestration and Agentforce-specific channel routing patterns. Gotcha: LLMs treat Agentforce topic descriptions as interchangeable with Einstein Bot intent names and advise practitioners to 'write utterances for topics' — Agentforce topics have no utterance training set and scope is controlled entirely by precision of natural-language topic description; misunderstanding this produces agents that match too broadly or refuse valid requests. skill-builder 2026-04-13T00:00:00Z |

## Phase 13 — OmniStudio / Industries (Cloud-Specific)

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |

| DONE | industries-insurance-setup | Insurance-specific OmniStudio setup: policy administration objects, claim types, coverage configuration, quoting. Core objects: InsurancePolicy, InsurancePolicyCoverage, Claim, CoverageType, InsurancePolicyParticipant, InsurancePolicyProductClause. Key: Communications Cloud centers on Enterprise Product Catalog (EPC) for service catalog modeling TM Forum-aligned order decomposition (commercial to technical order) and Account record-type segmentation (Billing Account, Service Account, Consumer Account) not separate objects; Industries Order Management in Communications Cloud is distinct from Salesforce Order Management (B2C/B2B commerce) and conflating them leads to incorrect API and object model assumptions; LLM anti-pattern is treating Communications Cloud accounts like standard CRM accounts without RecordType filtering; this skill scopes to org setup sequence permission sets EPC config and contract lifecycle activation. |
| DONE | industries-energy-utilities-setup | Energy & Utilities Cloud setup: service points, usage data, rate plans, meter management, service orders. NOT for generic admin. | Researched 2026-04-13. Key: E&U Cloud adds industry-specific objects ServicePoint (physical metering location) Meter MeterReading Consumption ServiceAccount ServiceContract RatePlan on top of core Salesforce Account and Asset objects requiring an E&U Cloud license; rate plan assignment depends on service type market segment and external CIS/billing system integration so incomplete integration silently breaks billing cycles; LLM anti-pattern is assuming standard Salesforce setup patterns transfer directly as service point configuration must account for regulated vs competitive market rules; overlaps with architect/industries-data-model (schema reference) so this skill targets operational setup workflow. |
| TODO | industries-public-sector-setup | Public Sector Solutions setup: licensing, permits, inspections, case management for government, citizen portal. | DONE | omnistudio-admin-configuration | OmniStudio admin setup: namespace configuration, component access, user permissions, org settings, feature toggles. Key: OmniStudio admin setup has two independent axes: (1) runtime mode selection -- orgs must explicitly enable Standard OmniStudio Runtime in Setup > OmniStudio Settings and disable Managed Package Runtime (irreversible per-component once opened in standard designer), and (2) permission set assignment -- OmniStudio Admin (builders) and OmniStudio User (consumers), consolidated into one primary Permission Set License as of Winter 24. The Runtime Namespace field in OmniStudio Settings controls which managed package namespace (vlocity_ins, vlocity_cmt, vlocity_ps, or omnistudio) is active -- misconfiguring or leaving blank causes component activation failures. Experience Cloud users require additional custom permission sets with the community consumer permission enabled. Overlap: omnistudio/omnistudio-security covers permission security posture; omnistudio/vlocity-to-native-omnistudio-migration covers namespace migration. LLM anti-pattern: assuming permission sets alone unlock all functionality without verifying runtime mode toggle and namespace field. |

| DONE | omnistudio-testing-patterns | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Preview and Test an OmniScript (help.salesforce.com); Debug and Activate an Integration Procedure (help.salesforce.com); OmniStudio Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); UI Test Automation Model (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: OmniStudio provides three built-in manual test surfaces: OmniScript Preview mode (runs as admin user, excludes Navigation Actions), Integration Procedure Test Execution in the designer (per-step response JSON with vlcStatus, errorMessage, and timing), and DataRaptor Preview for field-mapping validation before wiring into an IP or OmniScript; none require deployment. Key: OmniStudio CI/CD follows two distinct paths by runtime: Package Runtime orgs use the OmniStudio Build Tool with DataPacks as the migration format — components exported as JSON records and imported via packExport/packDeploy or the sf omnistudio datapack CLI plugin, with --activate required post-import to make a version live; Standard/Core Runtime orgs bypass DataPacks entirely and use Metadata API or Unlocked Packages through SFDX. As of early 2026, Salesforce is building atomic deployment capabilities unifying OmniStudio items and standard metadata into a single pipeline; practitioners should confirm org runtime before choosing tooling. Gotcha: the most common mistake is treating a successful DataPack import as equivalent to a live deployment — packDeploy without --activate creates or updates component records but leaves the previously active version serving runtime traffic; always include --activate and verify the active version after every import. | OmniStudio CI/CD: DataPack export/import in pipelines, version control, automated testing, environment promotion. Key: Spring '25 adds export of all versions — default packExport only captures active versions, draft versions silently omitted. Version-number collision: if same version exists in target, import skips silently (ALREADY_EXISTS) without overwriting — must increment version or use --overwrite. Custom matchingKey post-VBT v15 overrides package defaults silently. OmniStudio Migration Assistant (OMA) is a separate SF CLI plugin for managed-package-to-standard-runtime migration, NOT DataPack-based org-to-org migration. Overlap with skills/omnistudio/omnistudio-deployment-datapacks; narrow scope to migration-specific scenarios only. Key: The four OmniStudio metadata API types (OmniProcess, OmniDataTransform, OmniUiCard, OmniInteractionConfig) carry deeply nested JSON dependency references that the standard Tooling API MetadataComponentDependency object does NOT fully resolve — FlexCard → DataRaptor and OmniScript → Integration Procedure links are embedded in component JSON bodies, not as standard tooling-API dependency edges. OmniStudio Metadata API Support must be enabled uniformly across the entire pipeline — a pipeline mixing legacy DataPack-mode orgs with Metadata-API-mode orgs cannot be deployed reliably. Automated dependency management and atomic deployment are on the roadmap (announced Feb 2026, targeted mid-2026) but not yet shipped. Distinct from omnistudio-deployment-datapacks (DataPack execution mechanics) and metadata-coverage-and-dependencies (standard Tooling API). ### OmniStudio × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | omnistudio-vs-standard-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Architects Building Forms Decision Guide (architect.salesforce.com); OmniStudio Overview — Industries Common Resources Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); OmniStudio Standard Runtime Blog (developer.salesforce.com, March 2026)]. Key: OmniStudio requires an OmniStudio license bundled with Salesforce Industries clouds and is the right choice for complex multi-step guided wizards with multi-source data orchestration or declarative HTTP callout sequencing — for simpler single-page forms or automation-only requirements, standard Screen Flow + LWC carries less overhead and no licensing dependency. The Salesforce Architects Building Forms Decision Guide places OmniStudio and Flow on a continuum from Dynamic Forms (least code) to LWC (full code); as of Spring '26 OmniStudio Standard Runtime is natively embedded in the platform and Salesforce is directing all new investment to the metadata-based Standard Runtime path — orgs on the Vlocity managed package runtime carry strategic migration debt. Gotcha: LLMs recommend OmniStudio wherever a guided multi-step UI is needed, ignoring the license gate — if the org does not have a Salesforce Industries cloud, OmniStudio is not available; always confirm license entitlement before proposing OmniStudio. | OmniStudio vs standard platform architecture: when to use OmniStudio, complexity tradeoffs, team skill requirements. NOT for implementation. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | industries-cloud-selection | Industries Cloud selection: which industry cloud fits, customization vs configuration, licensing implications. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Industries Common Resources Developer Guide (industries_reference/index); OmniStudio Package and Salesforce Industries Package (ind.v_contracts_omnistudio_package_and_salesforce_industries_package.htm); Salesforce Industries Feature Overview Spring '26 Release Notes (release-notes.rn_industries.htm); Industries Cloud Common Features (ind.industries_common_features.htm)]. Key: Salesforce Industries is a license-gated portfolio — each vertical cloud (Communications, Insurance, Energy & Utilities, Health, FSC, Public Sector, Automotive, Nonprofit, Manufacturing, Consumer Goods, Education) adds distinct standard objects (InsurancePolicy, ServicePoint, BillingAccount) unavailable without the corresponding license, making vertical selection a data-model compatibility decision not a configuration choice. As of Spring '26 OmniStudio is platform-native for new orgs; opening a component in the Standard Designer is one-way and irreversible — it can no longer be edited in the managed-package designer. Key selection drivers: Communications = TM Forum-aligned order decomposition + Enterprise Product Catalog; Insurance = FSC base + separately licensed modules; E&U = ServicePoint + CIS-authoritative RatePlan sync. No existing skill covers cross-cloud vertical selection. LLM anti-pattern: assuming industry cloud objects are available without the corresponding license PSL. Gaps: no official Salesforce-published cross-cloud selection decision matrix found; builder should confirm licensing tier breakdown (Growth vs Enterprise) and Hyperforce-specific packaging differences.|
| DONE | omnistudio-scalability-patterns | OmniStudio scalability: high-volume OmniScript handling, caching strategies, API limit management, performance. NOT for generic scalability. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [OmniStudio Integration Procedures Help (help.salesforce.com); OmniStudio Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: IP Chainable and Queueable Chainable are primary scalability levers — Queueable Chainable runs next IP step as async Apex with higher governor limits when SOQL/CPU thresholds are hit. Concurrent long-running Apex limit (25 requests over 20s) is the key org-wide constraint under portal concurrency. Spring '25+ Direct Platform Access mode bypasses Apex CPU governors for read-heavy operations; LWR + CDN required for high-volume Experience Cloud deployments. Distinct from omnistudio/omnistudio-performance (single-session tuning); this skill covers multi-user concurrency and high data-volume scenarios. Gotcha: LLMs conflate async fire-and-forget (removes UI blocking) with Queueable Chainable (escapes governor limits) — different problems, different mechanisms. |
| DONE | industries-integration-architecture | Industries-specific integration: insurance ecosystem, telecom BSS/OSS, utility CIS integration, data exchange. NOT for generic integration. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Energy and Utilities Cloud Developer Guide Spring '26 (energy-and-utilities-cloud-developer-guide); Communications Cloud TM Forum API Overview (developer.salesforce.com/docs/industries/communications/guide/get-started.html); OmniStudio Integration Architectures — Salesforce Architects (architect.salesforce.com/diagrams/reference-architectures/omnistudio-integrations); Integration Procedure OmniStudio Developer Guide (industries_reference/meta_omniintegrationprocedure.htm)]. Key: Industries integration has vertical-specific architectural patterns: (1) Insurance — OmniScript + Integration Procedure calling external policy admin systems; key decision is whether Salesforce or external system owns policy state (if external is authoritative, Salesforce is read-mostly engagement layer not a write-back system). (2) Communications/Telecom — BSS/OSS integration via TM Forum API layer; MuleSoft gateway path deprecated Winter '27, making Direct Access the only forward-compatible pattern. (3) E&U — CIS is authoritative for RatePlan definitions; Salesforce E&U is engagement + service-order orchestration layer with one-way sync from CIS for RatePlan records. Distinct from insurance-cloud-architecture (FSC data model and module licensing), industries-communications-setup (setup mechanics); fills the integration architecture layer not covered elsewhere. LLM anti-pattern: treating Salesforce Industries as a system of record for backend operational data (rates, policy state, fulfillment status) rather than an engagement + orchestration layer. Gaps: BSS/OSS vendor-to-Salesforce connector catalog not in official docs; builder should search 'Salesforce Industries MuleSoft Accelerator telecom' and 'insurance'.|

## Phase 14 — CRM Analytics / Tableau

### CRM Analytics × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | crm-analytics-app-creation | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring '26 (developer.salesforce.com); Trailhead Quick Start: Create an App and a Lens (trailhead.salesforce.com)]. Key: A CRM Analytics app is a container created via Analytics Studio (Create > App > Blank App or Template App) that holds datasets, lenses, and dashboards; a lens is a single saved exploration of one dataset used to build dashboard steps, while a dashboard assembles multiple lenses/steps with filters, faceting, and cross-widget interactions. Data flows in via Salesforce objects (dataflows/recipes), CSV upload, or external connectors; datasets are versioned and consumed by lenses/dashboards, not queried live from source. App sharing uses three roles — Viewer, Editor, Manager — assigned per app; datasets within an app do not inherit Salesforce FLS or OWD automatically, so row-level security must be added separately via security predicates. Gotcha: LLMs and practitioners assume assigning a CRM Analytics permission set is sufficient to give users data access — users also need explicit Viewer access on the specific app AND row-level security must be configured independently of Salesforce object permissions. | CRM Analytics app creation: dashboard design, lens creation, data sources, app sharing, template selection. NOT for standard reports and dashboards. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | analytics-dataset-management | Dataset creation and management: dataflow scheduling, field selection, date handling, data refresh. NOT for standard report types. | Researched 2026-04-11. Sources: [CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring 26 (developer.salesforce.com); Dataset Capacity and Limits (help.salesforce.com); Transformations for CRM Analytics Dataflows (help.salesforce.com); Date Functions in SAQL Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics datasets capped at 500M rows per org; dataflows limited to 60 runs per 24-hour period -- orgs with multiple concurrent dataflows can silently exhaust this quota. Date fields must be explicitly typed with a format string at ingest time; fields left as text cannot be filtered or grouped as dates in SAQL without a computeExpression conversion. No duplicate; existing einstein-analytics-basics covers license/tool-selection only, not dataset construction or scheduling mechanics. |
| DONE | analytics-dashboard-design | Analytics dashboard design: chart types, bindings, faceting, dashboard interaction, mobile layout, filters. NOT for standard dashboards. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [CRM Analytics Interactions Developer Guide — Bindings (developer.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Help: Visualize Data With Charts — CRM Analytics; Salesforce Help: Filter Dashboard Results with Faceting]. Key: Dashboards use two interaction mechanisms — faceting (auto-filters widgets sharing the same dataset on user selection, cannot cross datasets) and bindings (selection bindings update a query's grouping/measure/filter/order/limit; results bindings update a query from another query's output — can cross datasets). Chart types: bar, line, donut/pie, scatter, bubble, combo, waterfall, funnel, map (geo), metric, table. When dynamically binding measure or grouping, the static columnMap must be replaced with an empty columns array or charts render wrong data silently. Mobile layout is a separate Designer mode that must be explicitly configured. Critical LLM anti-pattern: leaving columnMap static when binding measure/grouping. |
| DONE | einstein-discovery-setup | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Manage and Deploy Models in Einstein Discovery (help.salesforce.com); Einstein Discovery Basics — Create a Model (Trailhead); Einstein Discovery Prediction Writeback Fields in Salesforce (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: Story creation in CRM Analytics Studio follows a three-step wizard — define the outcome variable (maximize/minimize or binary), choose Insights-only or Insights+Predictions, and configure explanatory variables; Einstein uses regression and GBM models and automatically selects the best performer. Deploying a story creates a prediction definition (prefix 1OR) and optionally a writeback field — a system-managed read-only custom field on the Salesforce object (max three per entity) populated only by bulk scoring jobs or explicit API calls, never by record saves; field-level security must be manually assigned before the field is visible in reports or page layouts. After a model refresh job completes, the new model version must be explicitly activated on the prediction definition before scoring uses it. Gotcha: LLMs conflate the admin-facing story wizard path (CRM Analytics Studio) with the developer API path — they are separate surfaces; additionally admins frequently miss that a refreshed model is not automatically activated, meaning scoring continues against the prior model indefinitely with no error or warning. | Einstein Discovery setup: story creation, model deployment, prediction fields, what-if analysis, recommendations. NOT for Prediction Builder. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | analytics-data-manager | Data Manager configuration: data sync, connected objects, local transformation, data monitoring, error handling. NOT for standard data management. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Connect and Sync Your Data to CRM Analytics (help.salesforce.com); Data Sync Limits and Considerations (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: Connected objects are intermediate replicated copies — do NOT count against dataset row limits but cannot be directly visualized; must feed a recipe or dataflow first. Hard limits: max 100 objects enabled for sync, max 3 concurrent syncs; incremental sync relies on LastModifiedDate, so formula fields driven by related-object changes go silently stale. Distinct from analytics-dataset-management (dataflow/recipe/dataset layer); Data Manager owns upstream sync configuration. Gotcha: LLMs treat connected objects as queryable datasets and generate SAQL or dashboard references against them directly — connected objects are staging-layer replicas only and must be materialized via recipe/dataflow first. |
| DONE | analytics-permission-and-sharing | Analytics permissions: app sharing, row-level security predicates, dataset security, license management, folders. NOT for standard sharing. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Analytics Security Implementation Guide Spring '26 (resources.docs.salesforce.com); Add Row-Level Security with a Security Predicate (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics has an independent security layer — app access, dataset predicate RLS, and Salesforce sharing inheritance are all separate and must each be explicitly configured. Sharing inheritance limited to 5 objects (Account, Case, Contact, Lead, Opportunity); backup predicate mandatory when user sees more than 3,000 source records without View All Data. Security predicates are SAQL filter strings capped at 5,000 chars with case-sensitive column names. No existing skill covers this domain. Gotcha: LLMs assume Salesforce OWD/sharing automatically controls CRM Analytics row visibility — it does not; without explicit sharing inheritance AND fallback predicate, all licensed users see every row. |

### CRM Analytics × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `admin` (SAQL/JSON-based, not Apex)

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | saql-query-development | SAQL queries: aggregation, windowing, cogroup, filter, foreach, ORDER statements, nested queries, piggyback. NOT for SOQL. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Analytics SAQL Developer Guide — Statements, Windowing Functions, cogroup, Aggregate Functions (developer.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring '26 (local import)]. Key: SAQL is a dataflow pipeline language — NOT SQL or SOQL; every query is named stream assignments: q = load ...; q = filter q by ...; q = group q by ...; q = foreach q generate ...; q = limit q N; — SQL syntax (SELECT/FROM/WHERE/GROUP BY) produces immediate parse errors. Windowing functions (rank, dense_rank, cume_dist, row_number, moving_average, percent of grand total) operate across groups without changing row count; cogroup merges streams on a common field with INNER/OUTER semantics; rollup modifier on group enables subtotals via grouping(). Piggyback queries use pigql attribute in dashboard JSON — filter/limit/order on query attribute are ignored when pigql is present. REST API requires datasetId/datasetVersionId, not dataset name. Critical LLM anti-pattern: writing SAQL with SQL/SOQL syntax. |
| DONE | analytics-dashboard-json | Dashboard JSON editing: advanced bindings, custom queries, layout manipulation, step parameters, interactions. NOT for standard dashboard builder. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [CRM Analytics Dashboard JSON Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring '26 (local corpus)]. Key: Dashboard JSON has three sections — steps (SAQL/SOQL queries), widgets (pixel-based layout referencing steps), and state (global filters/interactions). Bindings use mustache syntax {{cell(stepName.selection, 0, fieldName)}}; empty binding returns empty string (silent suppression). Hard limits: SAQL step limit defaults to 2,000 rows, max 10,000 per step. REST API supports GET/PUT of full dashboard body with automatic History API versioning. No existing skill covers this domain. Gotcha: LLMs reference datasets by name in SAQL steps — in deployed/migrated dashboards this fails silently; must use datasetId/datasetVersionId references. |
| DONE | analytics-recipe-design | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Transformations for Data Prep Recipes (Salesforce Help); Nodes for Data Prep Recipes (Salesforce Help); Join Operations — Analytics (Salesforce Help); CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics recipes use a node-based canvas in Data Prep with node types including Load, Filter, Join, Bucket, Formula, Append, Aggregate, Flatten, and Output; Join nodes support six types: Inner, LeftOuter, RightOuter, Outer, Lookup, and MultiValueLookup — Lookup preserves all left-side rows and adds right-side columns matched on up to 5 key fields. Bucket nodes are typed by field kind (Measure, Dimension, Date) and produce a new categorical dimension column; Formula nodes use a dedicated expression language distinct from SAQL; recipe scheduling is managed separately via the Schedule Resource API endpoint rather than embedded in recipe definition. Gotcha: LLMs confuse Lookup joins with Inner joins — a Lookup preserves every row from the left (primary) dataset while an Inner join silently drops unmatched rows from both sides, causing unexplained row count shrinkage in output datasets. | Recipe creation: data transformation, join patterns, bucket fields, row-level computations, scheduling. NOT for SAQL queries. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | analytics-dataflow-development | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Transformations for CRM Analytics Dataflows (help.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics Limits (help.salesforce.com); Analytics SAQL Developer Guide — Speed Up Queries with Dataflow Transformations (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics dataflows are JSON-defined ETL pipelines composed of typed nodes — ingestion (sfdcDigest, Digest, Edgemart), combination (Append, Augment left-join-only), enrichment (computeExpression for row-level SAQL, computeRelative for partitioned expressions, Flatten, dim2mea), and the terminal sfdcRegister node which overwrites the registered dataset by default; row storage is capped at 250 million rows per dataset and the org is limited to 60 dataflow and recipe runs per rolling 24-hour window. A single failing node aborts the entire dataflow run and the previously registered dataset remains unchanged; optimization requires filtering early via Filter nodes before expensive Augment joins, using SliceDataset to drop unused fields, and splitting large monolithic dataflows into smaller chained ones. Gotcha: LLMs treat the 2-minute run-count exemption as applying to total job runtime rather than individual step runtime — in reality a step completes the exemption check per node, not per total wall-clock time, so practitioners should monitor per-step duration in Job Progress Details. | Dataflow development: nodes, transformation types, append/update/upsert, scheduling, error handling, optimization. NOT for standard data processing. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | analytics-embedded-components | Embedding analytics: Analytics Dashboard Component in LWC, iframe embedding, context passing, action binding. NOT for standard LWC. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Analytics Dashboard Component Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Attributes for Analytics Dashboards LWC (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Correct LWC for Lightning pages is wave-wave-dashboard-lwc; wave-community-dashboard required for Experience Cloud — not interchangeable. Context passed via record-id (18-char entity ID) and state (JSON string for filters/selections). dashboard attribute (18-char ID starting 0FK) and developer-name are mutually exclusive. No existing skill covers this domain. Gotcha: LLMs conflate embedding a dashboard in an LWC page (wave-wave-dashboard-lwc with record-id/state) with embedding a custom LWC inside an Analytics dashboard (analytics__Dashboard target in js-meta.xml) — entirely different patterns with different setup paths. |
| DONE | einstein-discovery-deployment | Einstein Discovery model deployment: prediction fields on records, recommendations in Flow, model refresh, monitoring. NOT for Einstein Discovery setup. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Manage and Deploy Models in Einstein Discovery (help.salesforce.com); Einstein Discovery Action in Flow (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: After a model refresh job completes the new version is NOT automatically activated it must be explicitly set as active on the prediction definition before scoring uses it; bulk predict jobs must be run explicitly to update prediction scores on records as they do not update automatically when source field values change; LLM anti-pattern is conflating admin-facing deployment workflow (Setup UI prediction field mapping Flow action config) with developer API integration covered by existing agentforce/einstein-discovery-development skill; this skill scopes to declarative deployment tasks enabling prediction definitions mapping output fields to layouts adding Flow Einstein Discovery action and monitoring via Model Manager UI. |

### CRM Analytics × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | analytics-data-preparation | Data preparation for analytics: data cleansing, augmentation, external data integration, XMD metadata. NOT for CRM data quality. | Researched 2026-04-15. XMD is layered: system XMD (platform-generated, immutable), main XMD (org-customizable), user XMD (per-user preference); CRM Analytics does NOT back up previous XMD versions automatically. Builder should narrow to XMD metadata and field-level annotation as a distinct sub-skill — broad 'data preparation' scope would duplicate analytics-recipe-design. LLM anti-pattern: attempting to modify system XMD fields (immutable) instead of main XMD; using SAQL to query WaveXmd records (must use REST API, not SAQL). | DONE | analytics-external-data | External data in CRM Analytics: CSV upload, external connectors, live datasets, Tableau bridge, streaming data. NOT for standard data import. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Analytics External Data API Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics REST API Developer Guide Spring 26 (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics has three distinct external data paths Analytics External Data API (InsightsExternalData SObject) for programmatic CSV uploads into materialized datasets Data Connectors for prebuilt connections to external warehouses (Snowflake BigQuery Redshift) and live datasets which are read-through connections that do NOT materialize data; LLM anti-pattern is conflating these paths treating Remote Connections as equivalent to dataset uploads or claiming live datasets behave like refreshed materialized datasets; InsightsExternalData object supports chunked upload and requires a metadata JSON schema defining dataset structure before data rows are uploaded. |
| DONE | analytics-dataset-optimization | Dataset optimization: field selection, date granularity, partitioning, row count management, performance tuning. NOT for SOQL optimization. | Researched 2026-04-15. Key: Row-count management, 60-run rolling window, and ELT push-down patterns are covered in existing skills; three specific optimization sub-topics are NOT covered by any existing skill: (1) field count limits and selective field inclusion (field-count performance impact not discussed), (2) date granularity selection (epoch vs. date vs. datetime storage tradeoffs affecting SAQL timeseries performance), (3) dataset splitting strategy (partitionBy in computeRelative mentioned but partitioning as performance tool not discussed). Critical: CRM Analytics datasets have no native partition index — 'partitioning' is an architectural pattern (splitting by year/dimension into multiple datasets), not a platform feature; LLMs conflate this with database partitioning. Buildable as distinct skill if scoped to field selection, date granularity, dataset splitting, and run-budget optimization. Gaps: CRM Analytics Limits page needs web search for current field-per-dataset limits and Spring '25/'26 changes to storage quotas.|
| DONE | analytics-data-governance | Analytics data governance: dataset lineage, access logging, data classification, retention, compliance. NOT for general data governance. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Analytics Security Implementation Guide Spring '26 (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=analytics.analytics_security_implementation_guide); Event Monitoring Analytics App (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=sf.bi_app_admin_wave.htm); Enable CRM Analytics and Event Monitoring Integration (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=sf.bi_app_event_monitor_enable_select_PSL.htm); CRM Analytics Limits and Considerations (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=analytics.bi_limitations.htm)]. Key: CRM Analytics has no native per-dataset data classification or retention controls — Salesforce field-level classification metadata applies to source objects only; once data lands in a dataset it loses that lineage metadata. Access logging requires the Event Monitoring add-on (license-gated), surfacing 60+ event types as hourly CSV files (up to 1-year retention) or as queryable Event Log Objects available 15 minutes post-event in Summer '24+. True dataset lineage (which recipe/dataflow produced a dataset) lives in Data Manager and CRM Analytics REST API (/wave/dataflows, /wave/recipes) but is not surfaced in a native UI lineage graph. Distinct from analytics-security-architecture (row-level predicates and app sharing) and analytics-permission-and-sharing (licensing and sharing roles); neither covers audit logging, lineage traceability, data classification propagation, or compliance retention. LLM anti-pattern: assuming Salesforce Data Classification metadata (field-level) propagates automatically into CRM Analytics datasets — it does not. Gaps: dataset-level data retention enforcement (no native purge/TTL); GDPR/HIPAA guidance for analytics PII datasets; whether Data 360 tagging extends to CRM Analytics dataset columns needs Spring '26 verification.|

### CRM Analytics × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | crm-analytics-vs-tableau-decision | Decision framework: CRM Analytics vs Tableau Desktop/Server, feature comparison, licensing, integration depth. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Tableau Next product page (salesforce.com); CRM Analytics Direct Data SQL release notes (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics is Salesforce-native embedded analytics; Tableau native Salesforce connector is extract-only (incremental refresh capped at 30-day lookback, no Custom SQL, 10,000-char API query limit). Tableau Next (Tableau+ SKU) GA'd June 2025 — forward path for enterprise/agentic BI with Agentforce and Data 360. CRM Analytics licenses are Salesforce Permission Set Licenses assigned per user inside org; Tableau uses separate Creator/Explorer/Viewer role model. Architect-level supplement to admin/einstein-analytics-basics. Gotcha: LLMs conflate Tableau CRM (old name for CRM Analytics) with Tableau Desktop/Server; also recommend Tableau for Salesforce-heavy orgs without flagging extract-only connector limitation. |
| DONE | analytics-security-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Set Up Dataset Security to Control Access to Rows (Salesforce Help); Add Row-Level Security with a Security Predicate (Salesforce Help); Analytics Security Implementation Guide Spring '26 (Salesforce Docs)]. Key: CRM Analytics has three distinct security layers — app-level (Viewer/Editor/Manager roles), dataset-level (which datasets a user can see), and row-level (security predicate) — none of which inherit from Salesforce sharing automatically. Sharing inheritance (which mirrors Salesforce role hierarchy) is an alternative to hand-written predicates but carries a hard limit: it only applies when a user can see 3,000 rows or fewer in the source object, so a backup predicate set to 'false' is mandatory for datasets that could exceed that threshold. Cross-dataset security must be designed by embedding a user lookup or entitlement dataset into the main dataset via a dataflow/recipe augment step, since predicates reference only columns present in that specific dataset. Gotcha: LLMs assume that Salesforce record-level sharing automatically restricts what users see in CRM Analytics datasets — it does not; without an explicit security predicate or sharing inheritance configuration, every user with dataset access sees all rows regardless of OWD, role hierarchy, or sharing rules. | Analytics security: row-level security design, sharing predicates, dataset access strategy, cross-dataset security. NOT for standard sharing model. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | analytics-data-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Transformations for CRM Analytics Dataflows (help.salesforce.com); Verify Incremental Sync Settings for Salesforce Data (help.salesforce.com); CRM Analytics Limits (help.salesforce.com); Analytics SAQL Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics datasets are capped at 2 billion rows per dataset (org allocation-dependent) with 60 dataflow runs per 24-hour rolling window being the most common architectural bottleneck; the correct performance strategy is to push transformations (joins, filters, augments) into the ELT process rather than into SAQL queries at runtime. Incremental extraction within dataflows uses Data Sync replication's incremental mode (leveraging SystemModstamp), but Recipes have no native incremental support — practitioners must simulate it by joining current source data against a prior-run snapshot dataset comparing LastModifiedDate timestamps. Data lake and external source integration (Snowflake, Redshift, BigQuery) is handled via Remote Connections in Data Manager, not via dataflow JSON. Gotcha: LLMs describe CRM Analytics Recipes as supporting native incremental loads — they do not; every Recipe run reprocesses the full input dataset and any architecture claiming 'only changed rows are processed' without a snapshot-join step is incorrect. | Analytics data architecture: dataset design, dataflow performance, incremental extraction, data lake strategy. NOT for standard data architecture. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | embedded-analytics-architecture | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Analytics Dashboard Component Developer Guide — LWC Attributes (developer.salesforce.com); Aura Component for Analytics Dashboards (developer.salesforce.com); Filter and Selection Syntax for Embedded Dashboards (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: CRM Analytics dashboards embed in Lightning pages via the wave-wave-dashboard-lwc LWC component (Lightning Experience and Experience Cloud) or the legacy wave:waveDashboard Aura component (Visualforce); the LWC component requires either a dashboard 18-char 0FK ID or developer-name attribute, and filtering is driven by the state attribute using the Filter and Selection Syntax JSON spec, while record-id passes the current record context automatically. Dashboard state is a structured JSON object managed via getState/setState component methods, enabling cross-dashboard context propagation and dynamic filter updates without full re-renders; dashboardDevName should be resolved at runtime rather than hard-coded. Gotcha: LLMs conflate the filter attribute (legacy Aura, adds incremental selections) with the state attribute (LWC, replaces the full dashboard state as JSON) — using filter syntax against the LWC component silently produces no effect, and hard-coding a static dashboardDevName breaks when dashboards are promoted across sandboxes or renamed. | Embedded analytics architecture: dashboard context, filtering strategy, performance optimization, user experience. NOT for standard Lightning pages. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |

## Phase 15 — Integration (Cloud-Specific Patterns)

### Integration × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | integration-admin-connected-apps | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Manage OAuth Access Policies for a Connected App (help.salesforce.com); Connected App IP Relaxation and Continuous IP (help.salesforce.com); EventLogFile Supported Event Types (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Connected App OAuth policies have three independent controls: Permitted Users (All users may self-authorize vs. Admin approved users are pre-authorized — the latter enforced via Profile or Permission Set assignment), IP Relaxation (Enforce login IP / Relax IP / Relax for refreshes only), and Refresh Token Policy (Immediately expire / Expire after fixed period / Until revoked). As of September 2025, uninstalled Connected Apps are blocked by default for most users, requiring admins to audit Connected Apps OAuth Usage in Setup and explicitly permit any app still in active use. Monitoring relies on EventLogFile with ConnectedApp and ConnectedAppOAuth event types, which require the Event Monitoring add-on and are only available via REST API query on EventLogFile — NOT surfaced in the standard Setup UI audit trail. Gotcha: LLMs set Permitted Users to 'Admin approved users are pre-authorized' but omit assigning the connected app to a Profile or Permission Set, leaving no users actually able to authenticate. | Connected App management for integrations: policies, IP restrictions, refresh tokens, monitoring, user assignment. NOT for OAuth flows (use oauth-flows-and-connected-apps). | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | remote-site-settings | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Adding Remote Site Settings — Apex Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); RemoteSiteSetting — Metadata API Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Content Security Policy (CSP) — Security for Lightning Components (developer.salesforce.com); Manage CSP Trusted Sites — Salesforce Help (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: Remote Site Settings (Setup > Security > Remote Site Settings) are a server-side gate — every external URL that Apex code calls via Http.send() must be registered there or the callout is denied at the platform level, regardless of CSP configuration; CSP Trusted Sites are a separate browser-side gate controlling what external resources Lightning components can load in the user's browser. Remote Site Settings are deployable Metadata API components (type RemoteSiteSetting) but are NOT included in Change Sets by default, making sandbox-to-production promotion the most common failure point for Apex callouts post-deployment. Gotcha: LLMs tell practitioners to add a domain to CSP Trusted Sites (connect-src) to fix a failing Apex callout — but Apex callouts are server-side and gated by Remote Site Settings, not CSP; adding a CSP entry does nothing to unblock an Apex Http callout. | Remote Site Settings and CSP Trusted Sites: managing external endpoints, security considerations, troubleshooting. NOT for Named Credentials. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | outbound-message-setup | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Help — Outbound Messages; Metadata API Developer Guide — WorkflowOutboundMessage; Integration Patterns (Salesforce Architects)]. Key: Outbound Messages are triggered exclusively by Workflow Rules (not Flow or Apex) and deliver SOAP 1.1 only; they use at-least-once delivery with acknowledgment-based retry for up to 24 hours, after which messages are permanently dropped with no automatic replay. The external endpoint must return a SOAP envelope with true inside the http://soap.sforce.com/2005/09/outbound namespace — an HTTP 200 with any other body (JSON, empty, plain text) is treated as a delivery failure and triggers the full retry cycle. Monitoring is done via Setup > Process Automation > Outbound Messages; failed messages can be manually requeued to reset the 24-hour window. Gotcha: LLMs and developers assume HTTP 200 confirms successful delivery — the actual success signal is the SOAP acknowledgment body with the correct namespace; returning HTTP 200 without it silently launches a retry storm that delivers the same payload hundreds of times before the 24-hour window expires. | Workflow outbound message configuration: endpoint setup, retry settings, field selection, monitoring delivery. NOT for Platform Events. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | integration-user-management | | TODO | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Give Integration Users API Only Access (help.salesforce.com); Platform Integration User (help.salesforce.com); Invoke REST APIs with the Salesforce Integration User and OAuth Client Credentials (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Security Guide — Monitor Login History (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: The dedicated Salesforce Integration user license pairs with the 'Minimum Access - API Only Integrations' profile, which enforces API-only login at the profile level (non-editable) while granting no object or field permissions — all data access must be layered on via permission sets using the Salesforce API Integration PSL, following least-privilege per-integration assignment. Integration users are exempt from org-wide MFA enforcement but this exemption must be explicitly granted; new integration users created after MFA enforcement is enabled do NOT automatically inherit the waiver and will be blocked if the waiver is not applied. Monitoring relies on Setup > Login History (UI shows 20,000 records, 6-month window) and the LoginHistory SOQL object (available from API v21.0+) to audit all successful and failed login attempts. Gotcha: LLMs recommend granting the System Administrator profile or a cloned admin profile to integration users 'for simplicity' — this silently bypasses the API-only flag, grants interactive login capability, and violates least-privilege; the correct approach is always the Minimum Access - API Only Integrations profile plus targeted permission sets. | Integration user setup: dedicated user, API-only profiles, permission management, session policies, monitoring. NOT for standard user management. | | research-agent 2026-04-12T00:00:00Z |
| DONE | change-data-capture-admin | Change Data Capture admin setup: entity selection, channel management, monitoring, limits, enrichment. NOT for CDC Apex triggers. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Change Data Capture Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); integration/change-data-capture-integration SKILL.md v1.0.0]. Key: Substantial overlap with integration/change-data-capture-integration; distinct admin scope: (1) Data Cloud silently adds CDC selections to DataCloudEntities channel when a CRM Data Stream is created — modifying via Metadata/Tooling API causes unintended sync side effects; (2) PlatformEventUsageMetric monitoring for daily delivery usage vs edition allocation (50K/25K/10K events/24h for Performance+Unlimited/Enterprise/Developer). Enrichment supported on multi-entity channels only, NOT single-entity channels; formula fields not supported as enriched fields. If built, must redirect all subscriber/replay/Apex content to integration/change-data-capture-integration. Gotcha: LLMs recommend adding enrichment to single-entity per-object channels (e.g. /data/AccountChangeEvent) — unsupported; enrichment only works on PlatformEventChannelMember records in multi-entity channels. |

### Integration × BA Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | integration-pattern-selection | Integration pattern selection: point-to-point vs hub-and-spoke vs event-driven, decision criteria, cost analysis. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Integration Patterns and Practices — Pattern Selection Guide (architect.salesforce.com); Salesforce Architects Integration Patterns Fundamentals]. Key: Salesforce canonical selection uses two axes — integration type (Process, Data, Virtual) and timing (Sync vs Async) — mapping to 6 patterns: Remote Process Invocation Request/Reply, Fire-and-Forget, Batch Data Synchronization, Remote Call-In, UI Update Based on Data Changes, Data Virtualization. Hub-and-spoke orchestration must live in middleware — Salesforce cannot participate in distributed transactions initiated outside Salesforce. Bulk API 2.0 required above 2,000 records. Upstream from integration/event-driven-architecture-patterns (mechanism selection). Gotcha: LLMs recommend building hub-and-spoke orchestration inside Salesforce Apex, violating official guidance that multi-system orchestration with transactional integrity must live in middleware. |
| DONE | api-contract-documentation | API contract documentation: request/response specs, error codes, versioning policy, rate limits, SLAs. NOT for API implementation. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [REST API Developer Guide — Status Codes and Error Responses (api_rest/errorcodes.htm); REST API Developer Guide — API End-of-Life Policy (api_rest/api_rest_eol.htm); REST API Developer Guide — Versions resource (api_rest/resources_versions.htm); REST API Developer Guide — Limits resource (api_rest/resources_limits.htm); Salesforce Developer Limits Quick Reference — API Request Limits (salesforce_app_limits_platform_api.htm); OpenAPI 3.0 for sObjects REST API Beta (api_rest/openapi_beta.htm)]. Key: Salesforce REST API versioning uses integer version numbers (e.g. v60.0) with a guaranteed minimum 3-year support window and at least 1-year advance notice before retirement — the /services/data/ endpoint enumerates all live versions. API request limits are tracked in a rolling 24-hour window, surfaced via Sforce-Limit-Info response header and /limits resource; REQUEST_LIMIT_EXCEEDED (HTTP 403) or HTTP 429 returned when daily allocation exhausted. An OpenAPI 3.0 document generator for sObjects REST API exists as a beta feature but does NOT cover custom Apex REST (@RestResource) endpoints — teams must hand-author those specs. Distinct from apex-rest-services (covers implementation, not documentation artifacts). LLM anti-pattern: fabricating specific numeric rate limits or SLA percentages not published by Salesforce — all limits must be sourced from the Limits resource or quick reference cheatsheet, never from training data memory. Gaps: SLA uptime/latency commitments per endpoint are not in developer docs — require trust.salesforce.com and Order of Service agreements; Experience/Connect REST API rate-limit behavior differs from core REST and needs separate treatment.|

### Integration × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `integration`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | salesforce-to-salesforce-integration | Salesforce-to-Salesforce integration patterns: S2S feature, API-based sync, Platform Event bridging, data sharing. NOT for multi-org strategy. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce to Salesforce Help (help.salesforce.com); Integration Patterns and Practices (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Native S2S feature uses PartnerNetworkConnection and PartnerNetworkRecordConnection objects over SOAP API; enabling S2S is irreversible (cannot be deactivated) and consumes SOAP API call limits on both publishing and subscribing org simultaneously making it unsuitable for high-volume scenarios; modern cross-org integration should prefer Salesforce Connect Cross-Org adapter Platform Events with Pub/Sub API REST API callouts or MuleSoft for enterprise-scale sync; LLM anti-pattern is recommending legacy S2S as default cross-org record-sharing mechanism; overlaps with architect/multi-org-strategy but this skill provides hands-on implementation patterns. |
| DONE | middleware-integration-patterns | Middleware integration: MuleSoft, Dell Boomi, Workato, Informatica patterns for Salesforce connectivity. NOT for native API. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Integration Patterns and Practices (architect.salesforce.com); MuleSoft Anypoint Connector for Salesforce documentation (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Middleware is mandatory per Salesforce Architects guidance when integration requires orchestration message transformation queuing or transactionality that Salesforce cannot natively provide; key selection criteria are event handling protocol conversion asynchronous transport and transactional guarantees; repo already has deep MuleSoft coverage in integration/mulesoft-salesforce-connector and integration/api-led-connectivity so this skill scopes to multi-iPaaS vendor selection (MuleSoft vs Boomi vs Workato vs Informatica); LLM anti-pattern is conflating vendor-agnostic middleware selection with MuleSoft-specific connector configuration or recommending Apex callouts for scenarios requiring cross-system orchestration. |
| DONE | idempotent-integration-patterns | Idempotency in integrations: external ID upsert, duplicate prevention, retry-safe patterns, transaction boundaries. NOT for duplicate management. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Integration Patterns (architect.salesforce.com); REST API Developer Guide: Upsert a Record Using an External ID (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: Primary idempotency mechanism is External ID upsert (0 matches inserts, 1 updates, 2+ errors per-row — replay-safe). Platform Events replay via ReplayId (3-day retention); Outbound Messages retry 24h with stable message ID. Publish After Commit event setting mandatory for idempotent subscriber patterns — default Publish Immediately can fire before committing DML is visible. Synthesis skill: cross-cutting inbound+outbound idempotency strategy not owned by retry-and-backoff-patterns or external-id-strategy. Gotcha: LLMs regenerate idempotency key on each retry instead of computing once pre-enqueue, defeating duplicate prevention even with X-Idempotency-Key header. |
| DONE | real-time-vs-batch-integration | Real-time vs batch integration patterns: trigger-based sync, scheduled batch, hybrid approaches, decision criteria. NOT for Batch Apex (use batch-apex-patterns). | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Integration Patterns (architect.salesforce.com); Salesforce Asynchronous Processing Decision Guide (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Real-time patterns (synchronous callouts Platform Events CDC Pub/Sub API) suit small-volume event-driven needs; batch patterns (Bulk API 2.0 scheduled ETL) are required above ~2,000 records and must run outside business hours; core decision axis is latency tolerance vs volume with secondary axis of transactionality (synchronous callouts allow rollback CDC events cannot be rolled back Bulk API has no cross-batch atomicity); LLM anti-pattern is conflating trigger-based Apex callouts (120s timeout 100 callouts/transaction limit) with Platform Events (async 72-hour replay) as equivalent real-time solutions. |
| DONE | error-handling-in-integrations | Integration error handling: retry strategies, dead letter queues, error logging, notification patterns, circuit breaker. NOT for Apex exception handling. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Platform Events Developer Guide Retry Event Triggers with EventBus.RetryableException (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce Integration Patterns and Practices (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Platform Events retain messages for 72 hours and Replay ID can be corrupted after Salesforce maintenance so event id is the stable deduplication key; EventBus.RetryableException triggers up to 9 automatic retries before the trigger is suspended and must be re-enabled manually; existing skills integration/retry-and-backoff-patterns and integration/api-error-handling-design cover dead-letter queue and HTTP error contracts so this skill must scope to orchestration-layer error routing cross-channel notification/alerting patterns and event-bus replay recovery not Apex-level retry mechanics. |

### Integration × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | cdc-data-sync-patterns | Change Data Capture data sync: incremental replication, replay strategy, data consistency, ordering guarantees. NOT for CDC admin setup. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Change Data Capture Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Pub/Sub API Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: CDC provides 72-hour event retention with durable replay via replayId (-1 tip -2 full catch-up or specific ID); subscribers must persist replay ID externally as Salesforce maintains no per-subscriber cursors and offline over 72 hours requires full Bulk API re-sync; gap events (GAP_CREATE GAP_UPDATE etc.) contain no field data and require fallback REST query using recordIds from ChangeEventHeader; LLM anti-pattern is ignoring GAP_ prefix and processing gap events as normal change events causing silent data drift; heavy overlap with integration/change-data-capture-integration so this skill focuses on replication lifecycle (day-0 load incremental delta ordering/deduplication via transactionKey and sequenceNumber). |
| TODO | integration-data-quality | Data quality in integration: data validation at boundaries, cleansing during sync, reconciliation, conflict resolution. NOT for CRM data quality. | |
| DONE | etl-vs-api-data-patterns | ETL tools vs API for data integration: Informatica Cloud, Jitterbit, MuleSoft Batch, tool selection criteria. NOT for Data Loader. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Salesforce Architects — Leveraging MuleSoft and Informatica (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/fundamentals/guide/integration-informatica-mulesoft); Salesforce Architects — Data Integration Decision Guide (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/decision-guides/guide/data-integration); Salesforce Architects — Integration Patterns (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/fundamentals/guide/integration-patterns.html)]. Key: The official Salesforce Architects framing treats MuleSoft and Informatica as complementary — MuleSoft owns real-time API connectivity and orchestration; Informatica owns ETL/ELT for massive datasets, data quality, profiling, and lineage governance. Selection axis is 'application integration' (API-first, event-driven, latency-sensitive) vs. 'data integration' (bulk volume, transformation pipelines, MDM). ETL-style bulk middleware tools must support Salesforce Bulk API. Near-duplicate risk with middleware-integration-patterns (iPaaS vendor comparison) and data-migration-planning (one-time migration tool selection); distinct only if scoped to ongoing ETL pipeline architecture (not one-time migrations) and ETL-vs-API decision logic explicitly — builder must maintain tight scope. LLM anti-pattern: conflating one-time data migration tooling with ongoing ETL pipeline architecture, or recommending ETL tools for real-time event-driven scenarios where latency makes batch ETL inappropriate. Gaps: Jitterbit-specific selection criteria not documented in official Salesforce sources — only Informatica and MuleSoft have formal architect.salesforce.com treatment.|
| TODO | data-virtualization-patterns | Data virtualization: Salesforce Connect patterns, External Objects, OData integration, live data access tradeoffs. NOT for Salesforce Connect admin (use salesforce-connect-external-objects). | |

### Integration × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | api-led-connectivity-architecture | API-led connectivity architecture: system, process, experience API layers, design principles, governance. NOT for individual API implementation. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Trailhead: API-Led Connectivity Essentials; Architecting the Agentic Enterprise with MuleSoft (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Three-tier pattern — System (backend abstraction), Process (cross-system orchestration), Experience (consumer-tailored) — with primary benefit of change isolation. Governance is the architect concern: every API needs Exchange catalog entry, owner, version, and deprecation policy; rate limits designed top-down to prevent cascading exhaustion. Salesforce acts as both System-layer endpoint and Experience-layer consumer; Agentforce agents consume backends via Experience APIs through MuleSoft Agent Fabric. Partial overlap with skills/integration/api-led-connectivity (layer design mechanics); this architect skill scopes to governance, versioning policy, multi-consumer strategy. Gotcha: LLMs prescribe all three layers for every scenario — single-consumer simple mapping justifies System API only; layer-skipping must be documented in architecture decision log. |
| DONE | event-driven-architecture | Event-driven architecture: event design, event mesh, choreography vs orchestration, event sourcing patterns. NOT for Platform Events implementation. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Event-Driven Architecture Decision Guide (architect.salesforce.com); Integration Patterns and Practices — Appendix C: EDA (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Official EDA guide covers 5 bus patterns (Pub/Sub, Fanout, Passed Messages, Streaming, Queuing). Choreography (async, no central authority) commits to eventual consistency; orchestration via Flow Orchestration or Apex retains transactional control but introduces coupling. Platform Events are NOT a native event sourcing store — 72-hour default replay ceiling makes event sourcing without external durable store (Data Cloud, Kafka, custom Event_Log__c) architecturally unsound. Distinct from integration/event-driven-architecture-patterns (mechanism selection); this skill covers architectural style decisions. Gotcha: LLMs conflate event sourcing with Platform Events replay — 72-hour window does not support state reconstruction from event log without external durable store. |
| DONE | integration-security-architecture | Integration security: mTLS, OAuth patterns, API gateway, IP whitelisting, certificate management strategy. NOT for basic Connected App setup. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [Salesforce Integration Patterns — Security Considerations (architect.salesforce.com); Preferred Alternatives to IP Allowlisting on Hyperforce (help.salesforce.com)]. Key: mTLS is Salesforce's preferred alternative to IP allowlisting on Hyperforce — Hyperforce IPs are ephemeral and not stable. mTLS works alongside OAuth 2.0 (not in place of it); OAuth signing cert and mTLS client cert are separate and configured differently. Hard limit: 50 certificates per org. Port 8443 must be explicitly specified in Named Credential URL for mTLS. Salesforce Private Connect eliminates public network attack surface. Distinct architecture decision layer above certificate-and-key-management and named-credentials-setup. Gotcha: LLMs recommend whitelisting Salesforce IPs for Hyperforce-based integrations — this fails unpredictably as Hyperforce IPs are not stable or published in static allowlist form. |
| DONE | hybrid-integration-architecture | Hybrid integration: on-premise to cloud patterns, reverse proxy, VPN, Private Connect, data residency. NOT for cloud-to-cloud only. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Salesforce Integration Patterns and Practices — Security Considerations (integ_pat_security_considerations.htm); Salesforce Help — Private Connect Overview (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=sf.private_connect_overview.htm); Salesforce Architects — Integration Patterns (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/fundamentals/guide/integration-patterns.html)]. Key: The Integration Patterns and Practices guide explicitly addresses on-premises-to-cloud complexity including DMZ relay (reverse proxy products such as IBM WebSeal, CA SiteMinder forwarding outbound requests), on-premises encryption gateways (CipherCloud, IBM DataPower) for data residency, and VPN-based connectivity. Salesforce Private Connect uses AWS PrivateLink; it requires support-assisted opt-in and carries separate add-on licensing — existing integration-security-architecture skill already documents Private Connect thoroughly. This skill is distinct only if focused on network topology and on-premises connectivity patterns (DMZ, VPN, reverse proxy, data residency) rather than authentication mechanisms — that scope gap is real and not currently covered. LLM anti-pattern: recommending Private Connect as the universal hybrid integration answer without confirming licensing, or conflating VPN termination at the corporate perimeter with Salesforce-side configuration — Salesforce has no native VPN client; connectivity is always through an intermediary relay or Private Connect. Gaps: on-premises reverse proxy configuration under current Hyperforce constraints may not be reflected in older integration patterns guidance — needs Spring '26 verification; data residency pattern guidance for regulated data in hybrid scenarios also thin.|
| DONE | mulesoft-anypoint-architecture | MuleSoft Anypoint Platform architecture: CloudHub, Runtime Fabric, API Manager, Exchange, governance. NOT for Salesforce-native integration. | Researched 2026-04-12. Sources: [MuleSoft Docs: CloudHub 2.0 Architecture; MuleSoft Docs: Anypoint Runtime Fabric Overview; Architecting the Agentic Enterprise with MuleSoft (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: Anypoint Platform has 4 runtime models — CloudHub 1.0 (managed SaaS), CloudHub 2.0 (containerized iPaaS, 12+ regions, private-space option), Runtime Fabric (customer-managed Kubernetes with cloud control plane), Hybrid Standalone. API Manager is governance/config layer only; policies require Active status or silently drop. Anypoint Security Edge/Tokenization not supported on Runtime Fabric. Distinct from integration/api-led-connectivity (layer design) and integration/mulesoft-salesforce-connector (connector config). Gotcha: LLMs conflate CloudHub 2.0 (MuleSoft-managed containers) with Runtime Fabric (customer-managed Kubernetes), recommending Runtime Fabric for generic cloud deployments. |
