## Phase 16 — DevOps (Cloud-Specific Deployment Patterns)

### DevOps × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `devops`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | cpq-deployment-administration | CPQ metadata deployment: product rules, pricing rules, quote templates, deployment ordering for CPQ components. NOT for standard change sets. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [CPQ Product Rule Guidelines (help.salesforce.com id=sales.cpq_product_rule_guidelines.htm); CPQ Price Rules Intro (id=sf.cpq_price_rules_intro.htm); CPQ Quote Templates (id=sales.cpq_quote_templates.htm)]. Key: CPQ configuration (SBQQ__ProductRule__c, SBQQ__PriceRule__c, Price Actions, Price Conditions, Quote Templates SBQQ__QuoteTemplate__c) is stored as data records not metadata and cannot be deployed via Change Sets or Metadata API; deployment requires specialized tools (Prodly, Copado, Salto) or external-ID-based data loading with strict parent-before-child ordering (Price Rules before Price Actions; Products and Pricebooks before Option Constraints). Gotcha: CPQ uses API names as plain-text strings inside configuration records so renaming a custom field silently breaks rules at runtime with no deployment-time error. Gaps: official CPQ deployment ordering checklist article; CPQ Custom Settings (SBQQ__CustomClass__c) behavior during deployment; Quote Template content attachment handling across environments. |
| DUPLICATE | omnistudio-deployment-admin | OmniStudio DataPack management: export, import, version control, environment-specific data in DataPacks. NOT for standard deployment. | Covered by skills/omnistudio/omnistudio-deployment-datapacks |
| DONE | experience-cloud-deployment-admin | Experience Cloud site deployment: publishing, template versioning, content migration between environments. NOT for standard deployment. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [ExperienceBundle for Experience Builder Sites (communities_dev_migrate_expbundle.htm); Deploy Experience Cloud Site with Change Sets (networks_migrate_changesets.htm); Metadata API Developer Guide: ExperienceBundle (api_meta/meta_experiencebundle.htm)]. Key: Deploying an Experience Cloud site requires strict metadata order: Apex/classes first, then Network, then CustomSite, then ExperienceBundle; deploying ExperienceBundle without Network and CustomSite already present fails. The deployed version remains unpublished until an admin manually triggers Publish in Experience Builder or via Connect REST API; Enable Experience Bundle Metadata API checkbox must be activated in both source and target orgs. Gotcha: never include the SiteDotCom blob in ExperienceBundle deployment package as it causes failures even when all other metadata is valid. Gaps: partial/incremental ExperienceBundle deployment behavior; CMS Content migration via Managed Content REST API; scratch org definition flags for Digital Experiences. |
| TODO | managed-package-installation | Installing and upgrading managed packages: pre-install checks, post-install configuration, version management. NOT for building packages. | |
| DONE | deployment-monitoring | Deployment monitoring: status tracking, component errors, test failures, deployment history, troubleshooting. NOT for Apex debugging. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Metadata API Developer Guide v66.0 (api_meta/meta_intro.htm); Salesforce CLI Reference (sfdx_cli_reference)]. Key: Primary programmatic monitoring is checkDeployStatus(ID id, boolean includeDetails) via SOAP or GET services/data/vXX.0/metadata/deployRequest/{id}?includeDetails=true via REST; DeployResult exposes numberComponentsDeployed, numberComponentsTotal, numberComponentErrors, status enum (Pending/InProgress/Succeeded/Failed/Canceled), and nested componentFailures and runTestResults arrays. Only one deployment runs at a time; additional submissions queue as Pending Deployments not guaranteed to execute in submission order. Deployment Status page retains history for exactly 30 days. Gotcha: deployRecentValidation returns a brand-new deployment ID distinct from the validation ID; monitoring the original validation ID after quick deploy shows old result not live status. Gaps: REST polling interval best practices; sf project deploy resume behavior on dropped connection; Tooling API DeployRequest object as alternative history query surface. |

### DevOps × BA Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | deployment-risk-assessment | Deployment risk assessment: change impact analysis, rollback planning, user communication, go-live checklist. NOT for deployment execution. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Well-Architected Reliable (architect.salesforce.com/well-architected/trusted/reliable); Salesforce Well-Architected Resilient (architect.salesforce.com/well-architected/adaptable/resilient); Metadata API Developer Guide (api_meta)]. Key: Well-Architected frames deployment risk across three failure domains (people, process, technology) and ranks release mechanisms by stability -- unlocked packages offer the most rollback-friendly path through versioning while org-based deploys have no native undo and require a pre-retrieve backup as the only fast rollback option. Changes should be classified high/medium/low risk before the deployment window opens with rollback decision authority and trigger conditions documented in advance not decided under pressure. Gotcha: LLMs frequently suggest a native rollback or undo deployment button in Setup -- no such mechanism exists; rollback is always a re-deploy of the prior version. Gaps: Change Risk Assessment for IT Services article (id=service.it_srvcs_chng_mgmt_risk_assmnt.htm) returned 403 during research -- needs direct access to confirm scoring rubric applicability. |
| DONE | devops-process-documentation | DevOps process documentation: runbook creation, deployment guides, environment matrix, onboarding docs. NOT for release planning. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce DevOps Center Developer Guide Spring 26 (devops_center_dev_overview.htm); Salesforce Well-Architected Automated (architect.salesforce.com/well-architected/easy/automated); Salesforce Well-Architected Resilient (architect.salesforce.com/well-architected/adaptable/resilient)]. Key: Salesforce has no native runbook feature; runbooks are practitioner-authored execution checklists for metadata types not fully covered by Metadata API. Well-Architected treats documentation as Operational Excellence under Automated and Resilient pillars; teams maintain an environment matrix (env name, type, purpose, branch alignment, refresh cadence, data policy) and deployment guides covering pre/post-deploy validation, rollback procedures, and Named Credentials credential-entry steps. Gotcha: runbook creation is often conflated with release planning -- a runbook is purely an execution checklist for a single deployment event not a release plan or project schedule. Gaps: no dedicated runbook authoring guide in official docs; best practice lives in Well-Architected Automated/Resilient pages; cross-reference skills/devops/environment-strategy for environment matrix template. |
| DONE | change-advisory-board-process | Change advisory board process: change request classification, approval workflows, change calendar, risk assessment. NOT for Salesforce approval processes. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Well-Architected Intentional Governance (architect.salesforce.com/well-architected/easy/intentional); DevOps Center Overview (platform.devops_center_overview.htm); Getting Started: Governance: Change Management (id=000388899)]. Key: Salesforce does not ship a native CAB feature; CAB is an ITIL-derived governance layer where changes are classified as standard (pre-authorized, no CAB), normal (full CAB review), or emergency (ECAB expedited); high-risk metadata types (permissions, sharing, flows, integrations) require explicit multi-person sign-off. Change calendar must account for Salesforce seasonal release upgrade windows because sandbox preview opens 4-6 weeks before production and deployments staged near that window may encounter platform-behavior drift. Gotcha: LLMs commonly recommend Salesforce native Approval Processes to implement CAB approvals -- Approval Processes govern record-level business approvals with no pipeline awareness; real CAB runs outside the platform (Jira, ServiceNow) and gates the deployment toolchain. Gaps: official Salesforce-specific CAB guidance is sparse; consider Salesforce Governance Whitepaper PDF; regulated-industry CAB (GovCloud, HIPAA) warrants targeted search. |

### DevOps × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `devops`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | cpq-deployment-patterns | CPQ deployment ordering: product rules, pricing rules, quote templates, billing config, dependency sequence in CI/CD. NOT for generic SFDX deployment. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce Help CPQ Quote Calculation Sequence; Salesforce Help Integrating Salesforce CPQ and Salesforce Billing]. Key: CPQ configuration lives primarily as data records not metadata requiring dependency-ordered deployment Price Books and Discount Categories first (no dependencies) then Products and Price Book Entries then Price Rules then Product Rules (which reference Products) then Quote Templates last; objects with self-referential lookups require multi-pass strategy (insert base records then update reference fields) with External IDs as cross-org matching key; LLM anti-pattern is treating CPQ deployment like standard metadata deployment via SFDX since CPQ config data cannot be deployed with change sets or Metadata API alone requiring a separate data deployment step; no existing skill covers CPQ-specific deployment ordering. |
| DONE | health-cloud-deployment-patterns | Health Cloud deployment: care plan templates, clinical metadata, HIPAA-specific deployment ordering. NOT for generic deployment. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Health Cloud Administration: Install Health Cloud Packages (admin_install_package.htm); Create a Care Plan Template (admin_care_template_config.htm); Assign Permission Sets (admin_permissionset_licenses_assign.htm); Health Cloud Custom Metadata Types (hc_mdt_overview.htm); Health Cloud Managed Package Data Model (hc_managed_package_data_model.htm)]. Key: Strict deployment ordering required -- HealthCloudGA managed package installed first, then Permission Set Licenses assigned, then care plan template creation, then CarePlanProcessorCallback class manually registered in Setup > Health Cloud Setup > Care Plan Settings as a post-deploy step not captured in any deployable metadata artifact. Care plan templates (CarePlanTemplate__c) live in the HealthCloudGA namespace and can only be created through invocable actions not direct DML. HIPAA: signed BAA required before any PHI is stored; Shield Platform Encryption should be configured on clinical fields; debug logging must be gated to prevent PHI exposure. Gaps: full ordered deployment checklist specific to Health Cloud; Salesforce-published reference for change-set vs scratch-org vs unlocked-package tradeoffs for HealthCloudGA-namespace components. |
| DONE | fsc-deployment-patterns | FSC deployment: compliant data sharing config, household model metadata, industry-specific deployment ordering. NOT for generic deployment. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [FSC Admin Guide: Compliant Data Sharing Considerations (ind.fsc_admin_cds_considerations.htm); IndustriesSettings Metadata API Reference (api_meta/meta_industriessettings.htm); FSC Developer Guide: Custom Metadata Types (fsc_api_custom_metadata_usage.htm); Salesforce Architects: Compliant Data Sharing in FSC (medium.com/salesforce-architects)]. Key: FSC deployment has strict sequential dependency -- Person Accounts must be enabled before household record-type metadata can be deployed (this is irreversible and cannot be done via Metadata API); then Account record types and CDS object enablement before Participant Role custom metadata; CDS requires OWDs for target objects (Account, Opportunity, Financial Deal) set to Private or Public Read-Only before share-table entries are meaningful. Managed-package FSC model (FinServ__ namespace) requires namespaced API names in metadata artifacts while platform-native Core FSC orgs (Winter 23+) treat FSC objects as standard objects with no namespace -- making metadata deployment artifacts incompatible between the two models. Gaps: exact Metadata API field names inside IndustriesSettings for CDS activation flag (docs page returned JavaScript shell); SharingSettings metadata interaction with CDS share-table recalculation needs verification. |
| DONE | experience-cloud-deployment-dev | Experience Cloud deployment scripting: site metadata retrieval, CMS content deployment, LWR template deployment. NOT for standard SFDX. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [ExperienceBundle for Experience Builder Sites (communities_dev/communities_dev_migrate_expbundle.htm); Deploy Experience Cloud Site with Metadata API (communities_dev/networks_migrating_from_sandbox.htm); Metadata API Developer Guide: ExperienceBundle (api_meta/meta_experiencebundle.htm); DigitalExperienceBundle (api_meta/meta_digitalexperiencebundle.htm)]. Key: Critical split by runtime -- Aura-based sites use ExperienceBundle (enabled via ExperienceBundleSettings) while enhanced LWR sites use DigitalExperienceBundle; using the wrong type silently retrieves nothing or deploys to wrong structure. CMS managed content from CMS workspaces is NOT included in either metadata type and cannot be promoted via sf CLI deploy; a deploy omitting CMS content succeeds with exit code 0 but content will not appear in target org -- requires separate CMS export/import or Managed Content REST API scripting. Post-deployment manual steps (domain config, SSO, CDN URL bindings) are not captured in any metadata type. Gaps: ContentTypeBundle deployment (api_meta/meta_contenttypebundle.htm); Network metadata interaction with ExperienceBundle ordering; scratch org support gaps for DigitalExperienceBundle. |
| DONE | managed-package-development | Building managed packages: namespace, versioned components, subscriber org patterns, package upgrade scripts, ISV patterns. NOT for unlocked packages. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [First-Generation Managed Packaging Developer Guide v66.0 (pkg1_dev/sharing_apps.htm); Run Apex on Package Install/Upgrade (pkg1_dev/apex_post_install_script.htm); ISVforce Guide v66.0 (salesforce_packaging_guide.pdf); local corpus knowledge/imports/pkg1-dev.md]. Key: 1GP managed packages require a dedicated packaging org per package and separate patch org per patch release; a unique namespace per package registered in a Developer Edition org; upload via Setup UI or Tooling API -- none CLI-driven like 2GP. The PostInstall/UninstallHandler upgrade script implements InstallHandler Apex interface and the class name is locked after initial assignment (only body can change in subsequent patches). Flows uploaded to a released or beta 1GP managed package cannot be deleted from the packaging org -- only individual flow versions can be removed. Gotcha: agents frequently advise using sf package version create CLI for 1GP which uses Setup UI upload not CLI-based version creation. Gaps: push upgrade scheduling limits; subscriber org governor limit behavior during PostInstall script execution; LMA license-gated feature patterns in 1GP. |
| DONE | cross-cloud-deployment-patterns | Cross-cloud deployment: handling dependencies across Sales/Service/Experience Cloud metadata, deployment sequencing. NOT for single-cloud deployment. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Deploy Experience Metadata: B2B Commerce Developer Guide (b2b-d2c-comm-deploy-experience-metadata.html); Master Metadata API Deployments Best Practices (developer.salesforce.com/blogs/2025/10/master-metadata-api-deployments-with-best-practices); ExperienceBundle for Experience Builder Sites (communities_dev/communities_dev_migrate_expbundle.htm)]. Key: Cross-cloud deployment requires foundation-first sequence: custom objects, Apex classes, permission sets, and profiles first; then Network and CustomSite metadata; then ExperienceBundle or DigitalExperienceBundle -- deploying the Experience layer before its dependencies produces cascading reference errors such as 'no Network named X found'. The SiteDotCom blob embedded inside ExperienceBundle must always be excluded from deployments because including it causes failures even when all other metadata is valid. Target org cannot be on an older API version than source when Experience Cloud features are in scope because certain metadata types are not backward-compatible. Gaps: no single canonical Salesforce cross-cloud sequencing guide covering Sales/Service/Experience Cloud together; supplementary search for DevOps Center cross-cloud pipeline ordering and DX project structure multi-cloud package dependencies recommended. |

### DevOps × Data Role

> Domain folder: `data`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DUPLICATE | test-data-management-devops | Test data management: factory patterns, data setup scripts, anonymization, data generation, fixture files. NOT for production data migration. | Covered by skills/devops/data-seeding-for-testing |
| DONE | deployment-data-dependencies | Managing data dependencies in deployments: record type IDs, custom metadata records, environment-specific values. NOT for metadata deployment. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Metadata API Developer Guide — RecordType (api_meta/meta_recordtype.htm); Custom Metadata Types Help (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=platform.custommetadatatypes_overview.htm); Salesforce Developers Blog — Master Metadata API Deployments with Best Practices (developer.salesforce.com/blogs/2025/10/master-metadata-api-deployments-with-best-practices)]. Key: Record type IDs are org-specific — they differ between every org (sandbox vs. production) because Salesforce assigns new 18-character IDs per org; the only safe cross-org reference is RecordType.DeveloperName resolved dynamically at insert time via Schema.SObjectType.Account.getRecordTypeInfosByDeveloperName() in Apex, or RecordType.Name as external ID binding in SFDMU/Bulk API jobs. The canonical deployment data error is INVALID_CROSS_REFERENCE_KEY: Record Type ID when a hardcoded ID from source org is used as a lookup field value in target org — this is a data record deployment error, not a metadata deployment error. Custom Settings are org-specific data and do not deploy with releases — the only path is a post-deploy script or SandboxPostCopy to seed them. Distinct from environment-specific-value-injection (Named Credential and CMT config values) and fsc-deployment-patterns (FSC-specific sequencing) — neither covers data record deployment where RecordTypeId, queue IDs, or user IDs must be remapped across orgs. LLM anti-pattern: recommending hardcoded source org record type IDs in CSV/data plan files — produces silent INVALID_CROSS_REFERENCE_KEY failures at load time. Gaps: Prodly/Copado Data Deploy dependency graph resolution for complex CPQ/FSC relational data sets thin in official docs; sf data import tree @sf_reference_id mechanism needs contrasting with external ID-based approaches.|
| DONE | sandbox-refresh-data-strategies | Managing data during sandbox refresh: post-copy automation, data selection, reference data seeding, cleanup. NOT for sandbox admin setup. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Salesforce Help — Refresh Your Sandbox (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=platform.data_sandbox_refresh.htm); Apex Reference Guide — SandboxPostCopy Interface (apexref/apex_interface_System_SandboxPostCopy.htm); Trailhead — Get Started with Seeding (trailhead.salesforce.com/content/learn/modules/seeding-basics/get-started-with-seeding); Trailhead — Best Practices for Test Data Management and Seeding (trailhead.salesforce.com/content/learn/modules/seeding-basics/apply-seeding-best-practices); Salesforce DX Developer Guide — Work with Data (sfdx_dev/sfdx_dev_test_data.htm)]. Key: Existing sandbox-refresh-and-templates skill covers SandboxPostCopy mechanics, refresh intervals, and PII masking — but NOT the data selection and seeding strategy layer: how to decide which reference data must be re-seeded after every refresh, how to use Salesforce's native Data Seeding feature (supports Nodes/Levels/Generate template types, incremental seeding, automation-disable during seed, record type/picklist validation before insert), and stale data cleanup between sprints. Native Data Seeding does NOT support Big Objects, calculated fields, Chatter objects, Files/ContentDocument, external objects, or AgentWork. SandboxPostCopy runs as Automated Process user with DML restrictions — large data seeding must be handed off via a Queueable or triggered from post-copy script that enqueues a job; recommending SandboxPostCopy directly for large data seeding is the primary LLM anti-pattern. Distinct from sandbox-refresh-and-templates (refresh mechanics) and data-seeding-for-testing (scratch org/CI seeding); fills gap of post-refresh data strategy inside persistent sandbox. Gaps: Salesforce native Data Seeding feature GA date and license availability need confirmation; Backup and Restore integration for seeding from backup needs deeper research during build.|

### DevOps × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | ci-cd-pipeline-architecture | CI/CD pipeline architecture for Salesforce: stages, quality gates, deployment automation, monitoring strategy. NOT for individual CI tool setup. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce DX Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com); Salesforce DevOps Center Help Plan Your Pipeline (help.salesforce.com); Salesforce Well-Architected Overview (architect.salesforce.com)]. Key: A Salesforce CI/CD pipeline defines the stage sequence (feature branch to CI validation to QA sandbox to staging to production) and quality gates (Apex test thresholds PMD/Code Analyzer static analysis validation-only deployments) accounting for platform limits such as 10-minute Apex test timeouts and inability to natively roll back declarative metadata; DevOps Center supports up to 15 pipeline stages per pipeline but does NOT provide custom quality gates code scanning or test threshold enforcement those must be layered via external CI tooling; LLM anti-pattern is conflating pipeline architecture (stages gates promotion strategy) with CI tool setup covered by existing devops/github-actions-for-salesforce and devops/devops-center-pipeline skills. |
| TODO | cloud-specific-deployment-architecture | Cloud-specific deployment architecture: deployment ordering across clouds, cross-cloud metadata dependencies. NOT for generic deployment. | |
| DONE | package-development-strategy | Package development strategy: unmanaged vs unlocked vs managed, namespace decisions, ISV considerations. NOT for individual package creation. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Salesforce DX Developer Guide: Unlocked Packages (sfdx_dev/sfdx_dev_unlocked_pkg_intro.htm); Comparison of First- and Second-Generation Managed Packages (pkg2_dev/sfdx_dev_dev2gp_comparison.htm); First-Generation Managed Packaging Developer Guide (pkg1_dev/sharing_apps.htm)]. Key: Four package types (unmanaged, unlocked, 1GP managed, 2GP managed) span a spectrum of control vs. mutability -- unmanaged is one-time install with no upgrade path; unlocked supports source-driven upgrades but no AppExchange IP protection; 1GP managed provides IP protection and AppExchange distribution but is org-centric and being superseded; 2GP managed is Salesforce-recommended for all new ISV apps with multiple packages per namespace and full CLI automation. Hardest constraint: namespace choice is permanent -- a namespace-less unlocked package cannot be retroactively namespaced and a namespace linked to a Dev Hub cannot be transferred or reused. Gotcha: agents frequently recommend unlocked packages for AppExchange distribution or ISV IP protection -- unlocked packages have no code obfuscation and cannot be listed on AppExchange as a protected managed app; only 2GP or 1GP managed packages provide those guarantees. Gaps: official package-type selection decision matrix; 1GP-to-2GP migration timeline and deprecation status; org edition restrictions on installable package types. |

## Phase 17 — Data Cloud

### Data Cloud × Admin Role

> Domain folder: `admin`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | data-cloud-provisioning | Data Cloud provisioning and setup: data spaces, data streams, ingestion API, activation targets, licensing. NOT for CRM Analytics. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Turn On Data 360 (data.c360_a_setup_provision.htm); Create a Data Space (sf.c360_a_data_spaces_create.htm); Assign a Data Space Permission Set (sf.c360_a_assign_permission_set.htm)]. Key: The hardest architectural decision at provisioning time is Dedicated Home Org vs. existing org -- most Salesforce-native Data Cloud features are available only in the Dedicated Home Org model and this choice cannot be changed post-provisioning. Six standard permission sets govern access (Data Cloud Admin, Data Cloud Marketing Admin, Data Cloud User, Data Cloud Data Aware Specialist, Data Cloud Marketing Manager, Data Cloud Marketing Specialist); only Marketing Admin or Marketing Manager can create Activation Targets. Ingestion API setup requires creating a Connected App with cdp_ingest_api OAuth scope before the API source can be registered. Gotcha: LLMs commonly conflate Data Cloud provisioning with CRM Analytics setup and incorrectly advise teams they can switch from non-dedicated to dedicated org model post-provisioning. Gaps: exact per-org data space count limit (id=sf.c360_a_limits.htm); credit consumption model for Spring 25/Summer 25 licensing. |
| DONE | data-cloud-identity-resolution | Identity resolution rulesets: matching rules, reconciliation rules, unified profiles, cross-device identity. NOT for duplicate management in CRM. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Identity Resolution Rulesets (id=sf.c360_a_identity_resolution_ruleset.htm); Identity Resolution Match Rules (id=sf.c360_a_match_rules.htm); Building a Complete View with Data Cloud and Identity Resolution (developer.salesforce.com/blogs/2024/10/data-cloud-and-identity-resolution)]. Key: Hard org limit is 2 identity resolution rulesets total (counting auto-created Starter Data Bundle rulesets) and a ruleset's 4-character ID cannot be changed after creation; match rules support Exact, Fuzzy (first name only), Normalized (phone/email/address), and Compound types across Individual, Contact Point, Device, and Party Identification DMOs. Changing a reconciliation rule requires a full identity resolution re-run not incremental to update existing clusters. In real-time contexts only Exact and Exact Normalized match methods are evaluated -- fuzzy is batch-only. Gaps: cross-device identity specifics (Device DMO field mappings); manual run frequency limit (4 per 24 hours per ruleset -- confirm in id=sf.c360_a_data_cloud_limits.htm); cluster size monitoring and remediation; data space scoping of rulesets in multi-data-space orgs. |
| DONE | data-cloud-calculated-insights | Calculated insights creation: metrics, dimensions, streaming insights, scheduled refresh, insight configuration. NOT for standard formula fields. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Calculated Insights (id=sf.c360_a_calculated_insights.htm); Create a Calculated Insight Using SQL (id=sf.c360_a_get_started_with_calculated_insights.htm); Calculated Insights Processing and Retention Times (id=sf.c360_a_processing_calculated_insights.htm); Streaming Insights and Limits (id=sf.c360_a_streaming_insight_data_action_limits.htm); How Are Calculated, Streaming, and Real-Time Insights Different (id=sf.c360_a_differences_between_calculated_streaming_insights.htm)]. Key: Calculated Insights use ANSI SQL (131,021-character limit) with GROUP BY for dimensions and aggregation functions for measures; orgs support up to 300 total insights with max 10 dimensions and 50 measures per insight, 2-hour execution timeout, and scheduling only at 6/12/24-hour intervals. Measure API names, data types, rollup behavior, and dimension names are immutable after creation -- only additive changes allowed, making pre-build design critical. Streaming Insights capped at 20 per org, support only Mobile/Web SDK and Marketing Cloud Personalization sources, cannot join Unified Profiles, and cannot produce lifetime metrics -- for real-time triggers only not segmentation. Gaps: credit consumption rates per CI execution; nested insights behavior in complex multi-DMO joins; Spring 25 or Summer 25 changes to scheduling granularity. |
| DONE | data-cloud-segmentation | Segmentation in Data Cloud: segment creation, filters, activation, audience publishing, segment refresh. NOT for Marketing Cloud segments. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Publish a Segment in Data Cloud (id=sf.c360_a_publish_segment.htm); Create a Data Cloud Activation for a Segment (id=sf.c360_a_create_data_cloud_activation.htm); Learn to Navigate Data 360 Segmentation Effectively (trailhead.salesforce.com/content/learn/modules/customer-360-audiences-segmentation)]. Key: Data Cloud supports five segment types (Standard, Real-Time, Waterfall, Dynamic, Data Kit) with a hard org limit of 9,950 segments; refresh options are Standard (every 12-24 hours), Rapid Publish (every 1-4 hours on last 7 days of data, limited to 20 per org), and Incremental; activation field mapping caps at 20 related attributes per activation and 100 total activations with related attributes; segments with 10M+ population cannot use related attributes. Critical hard limit: Rapid Publish cap of 20 per org combined with 7-day data lookback restriction. Gotcha: LLMs conflate segment publishing schedule with activation refresh type -- they are configured independently and frequent segment refresh does not accelerate activation delivery; Data Cloud can activate contacts with null email addresses so segment filters must explicitly exclude nulls. Gaps: help article bodies for c360_a_segments.htm returned 403; Real-Time Segment and Dynamic Segment behavior under activation needs direct doc confirmation. |
| DONE | data-cloud-data-model-objects | Data Model Objects (DMOs): mapping, relationships, data transforms, data lake objects, schema management. NOT for standard CRM objects. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Model Data in Data Cloud — Data 360 DMO and Mapping Guide (developer.salesforce.com/docs/data/data-cloud-dmo-mapping/guide/c360dm-model-data.html); Standard Data Model Objects — Data 360 DMO and Mapping Guide (developer.salesforce.com/docs/data/data-cloud-dmo-mapping/guide/c360dm-datamodelobjects.html)]. Key: DMOs are logical groupings (physical and virtual views) of data stored in Data Lake Objects (DLOs), organized into subject areas within the Customer 360 Data Model; five DMOs are mandatory for identity resolution — Individual, Party Identification, Contact Point Email, Contact Point Phone, and Contact Point Address — and data streams omitting these cannot participate in identity resolution; streaming transforms are restricted to a single DLO (no joins), while batch transforms support cross-DLO joins and aggregations; only one data relationship is permitted per field-pair between two mapped DMOs. Gaps: hard limits on max custom DMOs per org, max fields per DMO, and max DMO relationships need confirmation from Data Cloud Limits and Guidelines (c360_a_limits_guidelines.htm); overlap boundary with existing data-cloud-data-streams skill (which covers DLO-to-DMO field mapping during ingestion) — new skill must scope to DMO schema design, subject area governance, relationship management, and data transforms rather than ingestion mechanics. LLM anti-pattern: confusing DMO fields with standard CRM object fields and attempting SOQL queries against DMO objects — DMOs do not support SOQL and require the Data Cloud Query API. |

### Data Cloud × Dev Role

> Domain folder: `apex` or `integration`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | data-cloud-ingestion-api | Data Cloud Ingestion API: streaming and bulk ingestion, connector development, schema management, error handling. NOT for standard Bulk API. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Ingestion API Overview — Data 360 Integration Guide (data-cloud-int/guide/c360-a-ingestion-api); Bulk Ingestion API Reference (data-cloud-int/references/data-cloud-ingestionapi-ref/c360-a-api-bulk-ingestion); Streaming Ingestion API Reference (data-cloud-int/references/data-cloud-ingestionapi-ref/c360-a-api-streaming-ingestion); Ingestion API Schema Requirements (data-cloud-int/guide/c360-a-ingestion-api-schema-req)]. Key: The Ingestion API exposes two distinct interaction patterns — streaming (fire-and-forget micro-batches processed asynchronously approximately every 3 minutes, synchronous validation endpoint available for dev-mode pre-flight) and bulk (CSV only, 150 MB max per file, 100 files max per job, UTF-8/comma-delimited per RFC 4180, full-replace semantics — patch/partial update not supported); schema is OpenAPI 3.0.x YAML and schema changes are largely irreversible after deployment (no field removal, no type change, no object deletion); a required DateTime field is mandatory for engagement-category objects. Gaps: explicit streaming payload size cap and per-minute rate limits not clearly documented — Data Cloud Limits and Guidelines reference doc should be fetched during build for hard streaming throughput numbers; confirm whether bulk delete support interacts differently with existing data-cloud-data-streams skill (that skill covers streaming upsert only; this skill covers full API surface including bulk and connector setup). |
| DONE | data-cloud-query-api | Data Cloud SQL queries: query profile data, calculated insights, data lake objects, query optimization. NOT for SOQL. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Data 360 Query Guide — Query Data in Data 360 (data-cloud-query-guide/guide/query-guide-get-started); API Limits for Profile, Query, and Calculated Insights (c360a_api/c360a_api_limits); Request Data With Query V2 (data-cloud-query-guide/references/c360a-api-query-v2)]. Key: The Data Cloud Query API uses ANSI-standard SQL (not SOQL) against unified profile objects, calculated insights, and data lake objects; authentication requires a Data Cloud-specific access token from /services/a360/token (not /services/oauth2/token) and uses dcInstanceUrl from the token response as the base URL, not the standard Salesforce instance URL; Query V2 is the current standard (synchronous, cursor-paginated via nextBatchId, full result set must be fetched within 1 hour, inter-batch gap must not exceed 3 minutes); the newer Query Connect API removes row-count limits and extends result availability to 24 hours. No overlap with existing skills — this fills a distinct gap from data-cloud-vector-search-dev (semantic search only) and rest-api-patterns (SOQL-based). Gaps: hard row-limit per batch for V2 needs verification against c360a_api_limits; Query Connect API GA status and whether it fully supersedes V2 needs confirmation. |
| DONE | data-cloud-activation-development | Data Cloud activation targets: custom activation, webhook triggers, CRM actions, Marketing Cloud push, Flow triggers. NOT for admin activation. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Activation Targets in Data Cloud (c360_a_activation_targets.htm); Data Action Targets in Data Cloud (c360_a_data_action_target_in_customer_data_platform.htm); Webhook Data Action Targets in Data 360 (data-cloud-int/references/webhook-data-action-targets)]. Key: Data Cloud exposes two distinct extensibility surfaces — Activation Targets (segment-level, for publishing unified profile segments to channels: Marketing Cloud Engagement, SFTP/S3/GCS, ad platforms Meta/Google/LinkedIn, CRM) and Data Action Targets (event-level, near-real-time: Salesforce Platform Event, Webhook, or Marketing Cloud); developer work lives primarily in Data Action Targets and Data Cloud-Triggered Flows (fire on DMO row insertion, not updates); for webhook targets, a HMAC-SHA256 secret key is mandatory — omitting it silently causes the target to receive no payload — and after key regeneration there is up to 15-minute propagation delay; events are retained for only 4 days with no automatic retry. Flow-triggered automations operate on DMO inserts only, not updates, so practitioners updating existing unified profiles will not get flow triggers without an explicit re-insert pattern. Gaps: explicit payload size limits per data action target type (check c360_a_limits_and_guidelines.htm); whether Flow trigger counts against standard Flow governor limits or has a Data Cloud-specific allocation (verify from c360_a_streaming_insight_data_action_limits.htm). |
| DUPLICATE | data-cloud-vector-search | Vector search in Data Cloud: embedding configuration, search indexes, RAG integration, semantic search, similarity. NOT for SOSL. | Covered by skills/agentforce/data-cloud-vector-search-dev (embedding config, Query API token flow, RAG/Agentforce grounding) AND skills/data/vector-database-management (chunking strategy selection, index refresh, PII exclusion, rebuild workflows). Together these two skills cover the full scope. |

### Data Cloud × Architect Role

> Domain folder: `architect`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DUPLICATE | data-cloud-architecture-patterns | Data Cloud architecture: ingestion strategy, identity resolution design, activation workflow, data model planning. NOT for individual feature setup. | Covered by skills/architect/data-cloud-architecture — that skill covers DSO/DLO/DMO/Unified Individual layer design, identity resolution match and reconciliation rule design, activation target pre-flight, and batch vs streaming segmentation strategy. |
| DONE | data-cloud-integration-strategy | Data Cloud integration: connecting source systems, streaming vs batch, lakehouse patterns, data pipeline design. NOT for standard integration. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Data 360 Integration Guide — Ingestion API (developer.salesforce.com/docs/data/data-cloud-int/guide/c360-a-ingestion-api); Data Cloud: Connectors and Integrations (help.salesforce.com — c360_a_sources_targets); Data Cloud Architecture Strategy (architect.salesforce.com — data-cloud-architecture-strategy)]. Key: Data Cloud Ingestion API supports two mutually exclusive patterns on a single connector — streaming (fire-and-forget micro-batches ~every 3 minutes, hard 200 KB per request limit) and bulk (CSV files up to 150 MB, max 100 files per job); streaming is NOT real-time but near-real-time async with no sub-3-minute latency guarantee. Connector types span built-in (CRM Connector, CRM Connector Streaming, cloud storage S3/GCS/Azure), Ingestion API (custom source systems), and MuleSoft Direct (unstructured sources like SharePoint, Confluence); each connector writes to a DSO then flows DSO → DLO → DMO, and pipeline design must account for this multi-hop lag before data is available for segmentation or activation. No direct overlap with existing data-cloud-architecture skill (that skill explicitly excludes individual data stream ingestion setup). Gaps: hard connector-specific daily row quotas and MuleSoft Direct volume limits need verification against Data 360 Limits and Guidelines help article (access blocked during research). LLM anti-pattern: conflating streaming ingestion (~3 min async) with true real-time streaming (sub-second) — no connector type offers a sub-minute ingestion SLA. |
| RESEARCHED | data-cloud-vs-analytics-decision | Data Cloud vs CRM Analytics: when to use each, complementary patterns, data flow design, overlapping capabilities. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Data 360 Architecture (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/fundamentals/guide/data-360-architecture); Data 360 Integration Patterns (architect.salesforce.com/docs/architect/fundamentals/guide/data360_integration_patterns_and_practices); Unlock CRM Analytics Insights on Data Cloud (sf.bi_direct_data_for_cdp.htm)]. Key: Data Cloud (Data 360) is the foundational unification and identity resolution layer — it ingests, harmonizes, and profiles cross-source data using a lakehouse + real-time NVMe architecture, with identity resolution running as frequently as every 15 minutes; CRM Analytics is an analytics/visualization consumer that connects to Data Cloud via the native Direct Data connector, querying Data Model Objects (DMOs) rather than raw Salesforce objects, making them complementary rather than competing platforms. The primary decision dimension is which analytics layer to use ON TOP of Data Cloud — CRM Analytics, Tableau (JDBC/Direct Query), or direct API access (Data Graph API) — not whether to use Data Cloud OR CRM Analytics. Hard limits: Data Cloud batch ingestion caps at 100M rows or 50 GB per object; zero-copy federation available to Snowflake/Databricks/BigQuery/Redshift. No overlap with existing crm-analytics-vs-tableau-decision skill (that skill covers CRM Analytics vs Tableau only). Gaps: help.salesforce.com Analyze Data from Data 360 page (c360_a_business_intelligence_analytics.htm) returned 403 — fetch during build; confirm whether Data Cloud license is required to use Direct Data connector from CRM Analytics. LLM anti-pattern: conflating Data Cloud as an analytics tool with CRM Analytics — Data Cloud produces no dashboards; also watch for Tableau CRM (deprecated name for CRM Analytics) vs Tableau name confusion. |
| DONE | data-cloud-consent-and-privacy | Data Cloud consent: consent framework, data subject requests, privacy compliance, data retention, GDPR/CCPA. NOT for general GDPR. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Consent Management for Data Cloud (consent_management_c360_audiences); Contact Point Consent DMO — Data 360 DMO and Mapping Guide (c360dm-contact-point-consent-dmo); Data Subject Rights — Data Cloud (xcloud.data_subject_rights); Use the Consent API with Data 360 (resources_consent_cdp_params); Data Retention Policies (xcloud.data_retention_policies)]. Key: Data Cloud consent is modeled through the ssot__ContactPointConsent__dlm DMO, which links Individual/Party to contact points via a Data Use Purpose — consent-aware segmentation and activation must filter on this DMO explicitly, as consent is NOT automatically enforced by the platform at query time (a common LLM anti-pattern is assuming opt-out blocks segment membership without an explicit filter rule). Deletion requests (Right to Be Forgotten) must be submitted via Privacy Center or the Data Deletion API and are processed within 90 days; erasure propagates across the unified profile but does NOT automatically cascade to downstream activations or external systems already seeded with that data. Data retention policies are configured per Data Lake Object in day-based increments with no platform-enforced minimum or maximum retention window. Gaps: consent write propagation latency confirmation; exact interaction between Privacy Center DSARs and identity resolution graph (whether all resolved profile nodes are deleted or just matched identifiers); whether CCPA Do Not Sell maps to a specific Data Use Purpose value out-of-box; overlap boundary with existing security/gdpr-data-privacy skill (that skill covers CRM-layer ContactPointTypeConsent objects, not Data Cloud DMO layer — distinction must be explicit). |

## Phase 18 — Slack Integration

> Domain folder: `integration`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | slack-salesforce-integration-setup | Slack app for Salesforce setup: connected org, channel linking, record sharing, notifications, search. NOT for custom Slack apps. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Connect Salesforce and Slack (slack.com/help/articles/30754346665747); Configure Salesforce for use with Slack (slack.com/help/articles/360044038514); Connect the Salesforce for Slack App to a Salesforce Org (id=sf.slack_apps_digital_hq_setup.htm); Permission Scopes for the Salesforce for Slack App (id=sf.slack_apps_digital_hq_scopes.htm)]. Key: The connected-org setup is a three-party handshake requiring a Slack Workspace Owner/Admin to initiate, a Salesforce System Admin to approve in Setup under Platform Tools > Slack > Manage Slack Connection, and a Slack Owner/Admin to activate -- a single admin cannot complete all three steps alone. Hard limits: 20 Salesforce orgs per Slack workspace; Government Cloud orgs cannot be connected at all. Record previews shared into Slack channels are visible to all channel members regardless of their individual Salesforce object permissions -- this is the primary data-exposure gotcha. Gaps: exact OAuth scopes granted to Platform Integration User (article returned 403); behavior when linked Salesforce record is deleted or sharing rules change; whether Slack Standard User permission set is still required with current Salesforce-managed app. |
| RESEARCHED | slack-workflow-builder | Slack Workflow Builder with Salesforce: triggers, steps, data actions, automated notifications, approval flows. NOT for Salesforce Flow. | Researched 2026-04-13. Sources: [Guide to Slack Workflow Builder (slack.com/help/articles/360035692513); Build No-Code Slack and Salesforce Automations With Flow (admin.salesforce.com/blog/2025); Slack Flow Core Actions (id=sf.flow_ref_elements_actions_slack.htm)]. Key: Slack Workflow Builder connects to Salesforce via the Salesforce connector step Run a Flow which can ONLY invoke active autolaunched Flows not record-triggered or screen Flows; record-triggered Flows can push Slack messages via Send a Slack Message action but only in asynchronous paths. Hard async limit of 250,000 calls per 24-hour period and configurable trigger record limit to prevent bulk notification floods. Gotcha: LLMs commonly confuse Slack Workflow Builder (Slack-native, invokes autolaunched Flows from Slack) with Salesforce Flow (Salesforce-native, can post to Slack as side-effect) -- separate authoring surfaces with different owners, trigger models, and failure modes; no declarative way to look up a user's Slack ID from Salesforce without a custom field, which LLMs routinely omit. Gaps: approval flow patterns within Slack Workflow Builder (buttons-based pause-and-resume); Slack Workflow Builder admin governance controls; behavior when Salesforce connector step auth user lacks field-level access. |
| DONE | flow-for-slack | Flow actions for Slack: send Slack messages from Flow, create channels, post to Slack from automation, templates. NOT for Slack Workflow Builder. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Slack Flow Core Actions (flow_ref_elements_actions_slack); Use Flows with Slack (flow_build_use_flows_with_slack); Flow Core Actions for Slack: Send Slack Message (flow_ref_elements_actions_slack_send_message); Flow Core Actions for Slack: Create Slack Channel (flow_ref_elements_actions_slack_create_channel)]. Key: Flow Core Actions for Slack went GA in Summer '22 and require the Salesforce for Slack app (free, from Slack App Directory + AppExchange managed package) with a connected workspace and either a Sales Cloud for Slack or Slack Service User permission set assigned to the running user — actions silently fault or are invisible in Flow Builder if the workspace OAuth token is revoked or the permission set is absent. The full action catalog includes Send Slack Message, Send Message to Launch Flow, Create Channel, Archive Channel, Add Users to Channel, Check if User is Connected, and Get Conversation Info; screen-flow-in-Slack launch via shortcuts/views was Beta and may be discontinued. Partial overlap with flow/flow-email-and-notifications (covers Send Slack Message as one of several notification channels) — new skill should cover the full action suite (channel lifecycle, user management, flow-launch messages). LLM anti-pattern: presenting Flow Slack actions as universally available without flagging the required managed package, workspace OAuth connection, and permission set — builders hit action-not-found or runtime faults when prerequisites are missing. Gaps: exact behavior of Send Message to Launch Flow (required fields, token scopes, response handling); confirmation on Enterprise Grid additional setup requirements; whether screen flow launch via Slack shortcuts is now GA or discontinued. |
| DONE | slack-connect-patterns | Slack Connect for cross-org communication: channel sharing, data security, compliance, external collaboration. NOT for Salesforce-to-Salesforce integration. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Slack Connect guide: Work with external organizations (slack-connect-guide-work-with-external-organizations); How data management features apply to Slack Connect (how-data-management-features-apply-to-slack-connect); Slack data loss prevention (slack-data-loss-prevention)]. Key: Slack Connect allows up to 250 external organizations to share a single channel; both sides must be on a paid Slack plan and each org's admin must explicitly accept the connection request before collaboration begins. DLP, eDiscovery, and retention policies all apply to Slack Connect channels, but native Slack DLP (PCRE-based rules) and EKM are Enterprise Grid / Enterprise+ features only — orgs on Pro/Business+ plans must rely on third-party DLP integrations. Data sovereignty is split-ownership: each organization retains its own messages under its own retention policy, meaning a message deleted by one org may persist in the other org's export. No overlap with existing skills (flow/flow-email-and-notifications covers internal Slack notifications; agentforce/agent-channel-deployment covers agent deployment, not cross-org governance). LLM anti-pattern: conflating Slack Connect (cross-org channel sharing between independent Slack workspaces) with Salesforce-to-Salesforce integration or the Salesforce for Slack app (internal workspace connector). Gaps: hard limits on Slack Connect DM behavior vs channel behavior; behavior when one party downgrades from Enterprise Grid mid-connection; how Salesforce Shield/Event Monitoring surfaces Slack Connect activity. |
| DONE | agentforce-in-slack | Agentforce deployment in Slack: agent channel configuration, Slack-specific actions, user experience, permissions. NOT for core Agentforce setup. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Connect an Agent to Slack (ai.agent_deploy_emp_slack); Customizing Agentforce Agents with Custom Slack Actions (docs.slack.dev/ai/customizing-agentforce-agents-with-custom-slack-actions); Set Up and Manage Agentforce in Slack (slack.com/help/36218109305875)]. Key: Agentforce deploys to Slack via a Salesforce-managed app (not a custom Slack app); the General Slack Actions topic must be explicitly added to the agent in Agent Builder to unlock Slack-native actions including Create Canvas, Search Message History, Send DM, and Look Up User — canvas creation is unavailable on the Slack Free plan; Slack enforces a public/private action distinction where private actions require Salesforce-to-Slack user identity mapping via a proxy layer, meaning agents will never surface data the Slack user lacks Salesforce permission to see. Overlap: existing agentforce/agent-channel-deployment skill already covers Slack OAuth setup, managed app installation, DM vs. channel-mention mode config, and required OAuth scopes — new skill must scope exclusively to Slack-native actions, user identity/permission mapping, and Slack UX patterns. Gaps: exact list of all available Slack-specific action names and API contracts; Winter 26 release changes to Slack action set; whether Slack-native actions require a separate Agentforce for Slack license add-on; Block Kit vs plain text formatting in agent responses. |

## Phase 19 — Additional Industry Clouds

> Domain folder: varies by topic

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |

| DONE | loyalty-management-setup | Loyalty Management: program creation, tier rules, point accrual, redemption rules, partner loyalty, member portal. NOT for Marketing Cloud engagement. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Loyalty Management Basics: Set Up a Loyalty Program (trailhead/loyalty-management-basics/set-up-loyalty-program); Tier Processing and Points Expiration (trailhead/loyalty-rules-management-and-processing/review-the-tier-processing-and-points-expiration-processes); Loyalty Management Standard Invocable Actions (developer.salesforce.com/docs/atlas.en-us.loyalty.meta/loyalty/loyalty_mgt_actions_parent.htm)]. Key: Loyalty Management separates currency into two distinct types — non-qualifying (redeemable points) and qualifying (tier points measuring engagement against a tier group) — and a qualifying currency can be associated with only one tier group at a time, a hard structural constraint that shapes program design; tier assessment is driven by DPE batch jobs (Reset Qualifying Points, Aggregate/Expire Fixed Non-Qualifying Points) that must be explicitly activated and scheduled, not automatic. Partner loyalty requires a separate Create Partner Ledgers and Update Partner Balance DPE definition to be activated or no partner balance tracking occurs, with conversion factors (accrual factor, redemption factor) agreed per partner; the member portal uses a Loyalty Member Portal Experience Cloud template and only one loyalty program can be associated with a given Experience Cloud site. Gaps: official hard limits page (loyalty_limits_process.htm) returned 403 — exact numeric limits (max tiers per tier group, max currencies per program, max promotion rules, Batch Management record cap) need direct doc review during build; Agentforce/Einstein integration with Loyalty Management if any also unconfirmed; confirm whether partner loyalty requires a separate add-on license. |
| RESEARCHED | loyalty-program-architecture | Loyalty Management architecture: tier design, point economy, partner integration, fraud prevention, scaling. NOT for implementation. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [Loyalty Management Solution Architecture (architect.salesforce.com/diagrams/template-gallery/loyalty-management-solution-architecture); Loyalty Management Capability Map (architect.salesforce.com/diagrams/reference-architectures/loyalty-management-capability-map); Loyalty Programs Data Model (architect.salesforce.com/diagrams/data-models/loyalty-cloud/loyalty-programs); Loyalty Management Data Model Developer Guide (developer.salesforce.com/docs/atlas.en-us.loyalty.meta/loyalty/loyalty_management_data_model.htm); LoyaltyMemberCurrency object (loyalty/sforce_api_objects_loyaltymembercurrency.htm); LoyaltyProgramPartner object (loyalty/sforce_api_objects_loyaltyprogrampartner.htm)]. Key: The canonical two-currency architecture is qualifying points (determine tier eligibility, LoyaltyMemberCurrency, API v51.0+) vs. non-qualifying points (redeemable for products/services) — conflating the two in point economy design is the single most common architecture mistake. Escrow points are the native fraud-prevention mechanism: points earned on a purchase are held in escrow until the return window closes, preventing redemption on subsequently returned items — a first-class data model concept, not a custom workaround. Partner integration uses LoyaltyProgramPartner with LoyaltyPgmPartnerCurrency junction (API v55.0+); architecture runs on three interoperable platforms (Salesforce Platform, Commerce, Marketing). Distinct from loyalty-management-setup (implementation mechanics, not yet built as a skill); this skill targets architect-level decisions (tier economy design rationale, partner integration topology, fraud strategy, scaling choices). LLM anti-pattern: conflating qualifying and non-qualifying points — they serve different functions and using non-qualifying for tier assessment breaks the tier calculation engine. Gaps: no official concurrency/throughput limits for Loyalty Business APIs or batch tier-processing jobs found in search results; developer guide deep-dive needed during build.|
| RESEARCHED | net-zero-cloud-setup | Net Zero Cloud (Sustainability Cloud): carbon accounting, emission factors, sustainability reporting, targets. NOT for standard reporting. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Net Zero Cloud Developer Guide v66.0 Spring '26 (netzero_cloud_dev_guide); Net Zero Cloud Data Model Overview (net-zero-cloud-overview); Configure a Net Zero Cloud Org — Trailhead (configure-a-net-zero-cloud-org); Emissions Factor Records Developer Guide (netzero_calc_emissions_factor_records); Net Zero Cloud IndustriesSettings API Reference (salesforce-industries-dev-guide)]. Key: Net Zero Cloud is a separately licensed Industry Cloud (Starter ~$48k/org/year; Growth ~$210k/org/year) requiring a dedicated permission set model — Net Zero Cloud Admin, Manager, and Auditor — plus Data Pipelines Base User and Use Data Processing Engine permission sets assigned in the correct order before any feature toggle is touched; skipping Data Pipelines setup before enabling carbon accounting features breaks automation silently. Feature enablement is granular: each capability (Carbon Accounting, Building Energy Intensity, Data Gaps, Scope 3 Hub, Target Setting, Waste, Water, Supplier Data, Carbon Credit Allocation) is a separate boolean toggle in SustainabilitySettings metadata (API v54.0+), and several features — Scope 3 Hub, Waste Management Category 5/12, Extended Organizational Boundaries — are Growth-license-only. Emission factors are versioned reference datasets (EPA, BEIS, IPCC sources preconfigured; custom fuel types supported) that must be loaded before carbon footprint auto-creation will calculate correctly; both Assign Carbon Footprint to Energy Use Records AND Auto-Create Carbon Footprints must be enabled — enabling one without the other leaves records uncalculated with no error. The data model exceeds 200 objects covering scope 1/2/3, stationary assets, vehicles, travel, procurement, waste, water, and ESG/materiality. Gaps: per-feature API version minimum table and CSRD/ESRS reporting output configuration need deeper doc review; Scope 3 Hub spend-based matching algorithm limits need confirmation. LLM anti-pattern: do not conflate Net Zero Cloud with standard Salesforce Reports — carbon footprint records are auto-generated by Data Processing Engine flows, not written directly by users or Apex. |
| RESEARCHED | sustainability-reporting | Sustainability reporting: ESG metrics, carbon footprint tracking, compliance reporting, disclosure frameworks. NOT for CRM Analytics. | Researched 2026-04-15. Sources: [ESRS Standards — Net Zero Cloud Developer Guide (netzero_cloud_dev_guide/netzero_esrs_report.htm); Create ESRS Disclosures Report (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=ind.netzero_manager_generate_esrs_report.htm); CSRD Guide for Companies (salesforce.com/net-zero/csrd-reporting/); Net Zero Cloud Emissions Tracking — Trailhead (net-zero-cloud-basics/track-emissions-with-net-zero-cloud); Sustainability Scorecard Developer Guide (netzero_cloud_dev_guide/netzero_calc_sustainability_scorecard.htm)]. Key: Net Zero Cloud has native report builders for CSRD, SASB, GRI, and CDP frameworks; CSRD compliance specifically requires a double materiality assessment (impact on business + business impact on society) as a discrete prerequisite step before report generation — skipping it produces non-compliant CSRD output even if the report builder runs. ESRS reports are authored via the MSESRSMainDataraptor Data Mapper in Microsoft Word/OmniScript format; emissions data tracked across three Scope categories using typed source objects (stationary assets, vehicle assets, Scope 3 procurement items) with Energy Use Records as unit of measure input. Distinct from net-zero-cloud-setup (feature configuration and emissions source setup — not yet built); this skill targets the reporting/disclosure output layer (which frameworks to use, double materiality, what stakeholders receive, compliance readiness). LLM anti-pattern: confusing Net Zero Cloud's built-in ESRS/CSRD Report Builder (outputs Word/OmniScript disclosures for regulators) with CRM Analytics dashboards — they are entirely separate surfaces. Gaps: GRI and SASB report builder coverage was thin in official sources; SASB sector-specific applicability and CDP submission workflow may need supplemental Trailhead/blog research during build.|
| RESEARCHED | automotive-cloud-setup | Automotive Cloud: vehicle lifecycle, dealer management, lead distribution, inventory management, test drives. NOT for standard Sales Cloud. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Automotive Cloud Developer Guide v66.0 Spring '26 (developer.salesforce.com/docs/atlas.en-us.automotive_cloud); Automotive Cloud Standard Objects (help.salesforce.com — ind.auto_cloud.htm); Set Up Vehicle Inventory Search (ind.auto_search_configure_parent.htm); Automotive Cloud Integrations API — Vehicle Inventory Resource Mapping (industries/automotive/guide/vehicle-inventory-resource-mapping.html)]. Key: Automotive Cloud is available only in Enterprise, Unlimited, and Developer Editions and requires an Industries Automotive permission set license per user — without it, core objects (Vehicle, VehicleDefinition, LeadLineItem, LeadPreferredSeller, DealerVehDefSearchableField, Fleet, Appraisal, WarrantyTerm) are inaccessible even on eligible orgs. The data model spans 100+ domain-specific objects covering vehicle lifecycle, dealer group and OEM management, lead distribution via LeadPreferredSeller, inventory search via VehicleSearchableField, test drive scheduling, financial accounts, appraisals, claims, and telematics — all Lightning Experience only. A hard boundary exists with Manufacturing Cloud: sales agreements, advanced account forecasting, and program-based business are NOT in Automotive Cloud. MuleSoft Direct integration assets are provided for vehicle inventory BOD flows and require separate MuleSoft licensing; Name is the only mandatory field across most vehicle inventory resource mappings. Gaps: permission set license details, test drive scheduler config, vehicle inventory search setup steps return 403 from help.salesforce.com — needs Salesforce docs browser session during build; pricing tiers and Automotive Cloud Data Kit basic settings also need direct Salesforce Help access. |

| RESEARCHED | salesforce-backup-and-restore | Salesforce Backup & Restore: native backup service, Odaseva/OwnBackup, metadata backup, recovery procedures, retention policies, compliance. Key: Native Salesforce Backup and Restore is a separately purchased add-on (not included in any edition by default) that provides daily full-org snapshots with record-level selective restore by object, time range, and relationship — maximum native RPO is 24 hours; the native service does NOT cover Big Objects (append-only, no restore path via any backup tool), metadata (must use Git/source control), or file/attachment content (ContentDocument/Attachment coverage requires third-party tools such as Own Company, Veeam Backup for Salesforce, or Odaseva, which also offer sub-daily scheduling, cross-org restore, and compliance-grade audit logging for GDPR/HIPAA). ### 20a — Revenue Cloud (New — distinct from CPQ Phase 6)

> Domain folder: varies by topic

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | revenue-lifecycle-management | Revenue Cloud: revenue lifecycle, contract amendments, order decomposition, billing schedule, revenue recognition rules. NOT for CPQ quoting (use cpq-* skills). | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Revenue Lifecycle Management Overview (sf.revenue_lifecycle_management.htm); Dynamic Revenue Orchestrator — Trailhead (dynamic-revenue-orchestrator-foundations/meet-dynamic-revenue-orchestrator); Revenue Cloud Developer Guide — Get Started (revenue_lifecycle_management_dev_guide/rlm_get_started); Manage Orders in Revenue Cloud — Trailhead (revenue-cloud-design/manage-orders)]. Key: Salesforce Revenue Lifecycle Management (RLM) is a native Revenue Cloud product (distinct from CPQ + Salesforce Billing managed package) covering the full order-to-cash lifecycle — order decomposition via Dynamic Revenue Orchestrator (DRO) splits commercial orders into technical fulfillment orders routed across swimlanes (billing, provisioning, shipping) using auto-tasks, callouts, manual tasks, milestones, and pauses; billing schedules are created via Connect API POST after order activation and do NOT auto-update when an asset amendment order is activated — each amendment produces a net-new billing schedule record requiring manual reconciliation for correct revenue reporting. Critical overlap risk: existing billing-schedule-setup and revenue-recognition-requirements skills cover the Salesforce Billing managed-package (blng__*) objects in depth — this skill must be scoped strictly to the native RLM/Revenue Cloud product model (Asset Lifecycle Management, DRO, Invoice Management) and must explicitly call out it does NOT apply to the legacy Billing managed package or CPQ quoting. Gaps: hard limits on DRO fulfillment step count per plan, max concurrent orchestration plans, and billing schedule API batch size need targeted doc research during build (developer.salesforce.com RLM dev guide pages returned 403). LLM anti-pattern: conflating Salesforce Billing (managed package, blng__* objects) with native Revenue Cloud RLM — they are separate products with separate object models, separate activation flows, and separate amendment behavior. |
| TODO | usage-based-pricing-setup | Usage-based pricing in Revenue Cloud: metered billing, usage records, rating, tiering, consumption schedules. NOT for CPQ pricing rules. | admin |
| RESEARCHED | revenue-cloud-architecture | Revenue Cloud architecture: order-to-cash flow, contract lifecycle, billing integration, ERP handoff, multi-entity. NOT for CPQ architecture. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [ERP Integration Architectural Considerations for Lead to Cash (blng_erp_arch_consid_ltc); Transaction Management: Order Data Model (revenue-cloud-transaction-mgmt-order-data-model); Revenue Cloud Billing Data Model — Legal Entities (rev-cloud-billing); Plan Your Revenue Cloud Implementation (plan_your_revenue_cloud_implementation)]. Key: Revenue Cloud (Revenue Lifecycle Management) models order-to-cash across five composable domains — Product Catalog & Pricing, Transaction Management, Contract Lifecycle Management, Order-to-Cash, and Billing — connected through a shared canonical data model with objects Order, OrderItem, Contract, BillingSchedule, Invoice, LegalEntity, and AccountingPeriod; multi-entity scenarios are handled via the LegalEntity object, which scopes invoices, accounting periods, and payment terms per entity within a single org, making entity proliferation a key design risk. The primary ERP handoff pattern is Change Data Capture on Opportunity/Order records consumed via CometD or MuleSoft, or outbound Apex callouts (must be @future/@queueable — synchronous callouts from triggers are blocked); architect-recommended pattern is event-driven via Platform Events or CDC, not point-to-point trigger callouts. Overlap risk with existing cpq-architecture-patterns and cpq-integration-with-erp skills — this skill must stay scoped to Revenue Cloud (RLM) architecture, not CPQ managed-package flows. Gaps: hard per-transaction and per-org limits for Transaction Management (verify qocal_limits page); multi-entity tax jurisdiction routing specifics; LLMs frequently conflate Salesforce Billing (blng__ namespace) with native Revenue Cloud RLM — explicit disambiguation required in this skill. |
| DONE | revenue-cloud-data-model | Revenue Cloud data model: OrderItem, BillingSchedule, BillingScheduleGroup, Invoice, Payment, FinanceTransaction relationships. NOT for CPQ data model. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Revenue Cloud Data Model Gallery (revenue-cloud-category); Billing Invoice Data Model (billing-invoice); Payments Data Model (payments); Transaction Management: Order (transaction-mgmt-order); BillingSchedule Object Reference (sforce_api_objects_billingschedule)]. Key: Revenue Cloud (native, non-managed-package) exposes standard objects — BillingSchedule, BillingScheduleGroup, Invoice, InvoiceLine, Payment, PaymentLineInvoice, and FinanceTransaction — distinct from the managed-package blng__ namespace objects used by legacy Salesforce Billing; BillingSchedule (available from API v55.0+) is a child of OrderItem and rolls up into a BillingScheduleGroup, which drives Invoice generation, while FinanceTransaction represents the accounting journal entry created when an Invoice is posted or a Payment is received (read-only ledger record sitting downstream of both). Confirmed no overlap with existing data/billing-data-reconciliation skill (covers only blng__ managed-package reconciliation chain). Gaps: FinanceTransaction field-level schema and write restrictions (whether fully read-only or supports upsert via API) need direct Object Reference confirmation; BillingScheduleGroup aggregation logic (which fields drive grouping) requires verification against Spring '26 release notes or billing-invoice diagram. LLM anti-pattern: conflating native Revenue Cloud objects (BillingSchedule, Invoice, Payment — standard API names) with legacy Salesforce Billing managed-package objects (blng__BillingSchedule__c, blng__Invoice__c, blng__Payment__c) — SOQL patterns, field names, and governor limits differ entirely between the two. |

### 20b — Pub/Sub API & Modern Integration

> Domain folder: `integration`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | pub-sub-api-patterns | Pub/Sub API: gRPC streaming, subscribe/publish, event replay, managed subscriptions, auth flow, language clients. NOT for legacy PushTopic or Streaming API. | Researched 2026-04-14. Sources: [Pub/Sub API Developer Guide — Get Started (pub-sub-api/guide/intro.html); Pub/Sub API Allocations (pub-sub-api/guide/allocations.html); Pub/Sub API Authentication (pub-sub-api/guide/supported-auth.html); Managed Event Subscriptions Beta (pub-sub-api/guide/managed-sub.html)]. Key: Pub/Sub API is a gRPC/HTTP2 API (GA since Summer '22) exposing Subscribe, ManagedSubscribe, and Publish/PublishStream RPC methods; event bus retains events for 3 days with replay via Earliest/Latest/Custom replay-ID presets, capped at 100 events per FetchRequest and 1,000 concurrent gRPC streams per HTTP/2 connection; Managed Subscriptions (Summer '24 Open Beta) offload replay-ID tracking to server-side ManagedEventSubscription metadata records, with a hard org limit of 200 managed subscriptions; publish requests capped at 1 MB per event, 3 MB recommended / 4 MB hard limit per batch, max 200 events per publish request; auth requires accesstoken + instanceurl + tenantid headers using OAuth or session ID, with a default 2-hour session timeout that does NOT drop active Subscribe streams but does close idle PublishStream connections. Overlap confirmed with change-data-capture-integration and platform-events-integration (both cover gRPC subscription mechanics as supporting detail) — this skill must scope tightly to the transport/protocol layer (gRPC method contracts, auth flow, flow control, managed subscription lifecycle). Gaps: Managed Subscriptions GA date and changes from Beta need verification at build time; language client library maturity and official sample repo status; interaction between org-level Platform Event delivery allocations and Pub/Sub API stream limits needs cross-referencing with Limits cheatsheet. LLM anti-pattern: recommending CometD/EMP Connector for new external subscriptions when Pub/Sub API gRPC is now the preferred path; also conflating the 100-event-per-fetch cap with a throughput ceiling (it is a per-request fetch size, not a rate limit). |
| DONE | bulk-api-2-patterns | Bulk API 2.0: ingest/query jobs, CSV streaming, job monitoring, retry on partial failure, multipart upload. NOT for Bulk API 1.0 or REST API (use rest-api-patterns). | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Bulk API 2.0 Developer Guide (bulk_api_2/api_asynch); Bulk API 2.0 Limits and Allocations]. Key: Bulk API 2.0 supports ingest (insert/update/upsert/delete/hardDelete) and query jobs via REST+OAuth; ingest jobs follow Open->UploadComplete->InProgress->JobComplete/Failed/Aborted state machine — PATCH {state:UploadComplete} is mandatory or job stays Open indefinitely. Hard daily limit: 150M records per org per 24 hrs; each upload PUT must stay under 150 MB after base64 encoding; query results paginate via Sforce-Locator header which returns literal string 'null' on last page. Overlaps with data/bulk-api-patterns and data/bulk-api-and-large-data-loads — scope this skill to integration-tier retry/streaming patterns. LLM anti-pattern: generating concurrencyMode:Serial which is a v1-only field and no-op in v2.0. Gaps: confirm queryAll support in v2.0; verify 100K multipart cap in API v63+. |
| RESEARCHED | heroku-salesforce-integration | Heroku integration: Heroku Connect, Heroku Postgres sync, add-on architecture, Salesforce Canvas, SSO. NOT for generic PaaS or AWS. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Heroku Connect - Heroku Dev Center (devcenter.heroku.com/articles/heroku-connect); Integrating Heroku and Salesforce Overview (devcenter.heroku.com/articles/integrating-heroku-and-salesforce); Canvas App Authentication - Canvas Developer Guide (platform_connect/canvas_app_authentication.htm)]. Key: Heroku Connect syncs via OAuth token per add-on; demo plan caps at 10,000 synced rows; polling minimum every 10 seconds (pg_notify-triggered) or 2 minutes otherwise; co-locating Connect + Postgres + Salesforce org region is primary latency lever; Salesforce Canvas: Signed Request (default POST-based, no consent screen) vs OAuth 2.0 web server flow - LLMs commonly conflate these or recommend OAuth where Signed Request is correct for embedded iFrame use; Heroku SSO via Salesforce Identity uses SAML restricted to Heroku Teams/Enterprise. Gaps: Heroku Connect paid plan row counts (not publicly listed); Salesforce Data Cloud direct Postgres connector (newer path at devcenter.heroku.com/articles/connecting-heroku-postgres-to-salesforce-data-cloud); Shield Connect HIPAA compliance requirements. |
| TODO | aws-salesforce-patterns | AWS integration with Salesforce: Amazon AppFlow, EventBridge, Lambda callouts, S3 file integration, Amazon Connect CTI. NOT for MuleSoft. | integration |
| TODO | azure-salesforce-patterns | Azure integration: Azure Functions callouts, Azure Service Bus, Power Platform connectors, Azure AD SSO, Azure Blob storage. NOT for MuleSoft. | integration |
