### 20c — Security Hardening

> Domain folder: `security`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | mfa-enforcement-strategy | MFA enforcement: Salesforce Authenticator, TOTP apps, security keys, SSO MFA delegation, exemptions, rollout strategy, compliance deadlines. NOT for login flow customization (use ip-range-and-login-flow-strategy). | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Salesforce MFA FAQ (id=000396727); MFA Enforcement Roadmap (id=000389313); Enable MFA for Your Entire Org (xcloud.security_mfa_org_wide_setting.htm); Exclude Exempt Users from MFA (xcloud.security_mfa_exclude_exempt_users.htm)]. Key: MFA became a contractual requirement Feb 1 2022 and is auto-enabled for all new production orgs — no future deadline, requirement already in effect. Four verification methods: Salesforce Authenticator (push), TOTP apps (Google/Microsoft Authenticator), FIDO2/WebAuthn security keys (YubiKey), built-in authenticators (Windows Hello, Touch ID). SSO satisfies MFA ONLY when: IdP enforces MFA AND all users access via SAML/OIDC SSO AND direct login is fully disabled. API-only users must use API Only profile or JWT bearer OAuth flow + Waive MFA permission set. Distinct from ip-range-and-login-flow-strategy (which covers login flow customization). LLM anti-pattern: claiming SSO alone satisfies MFA requirement or that Trusted IP Ranges exempt users from MFA (they do not since enforcement). Gaps: MFA waiver permission set exact API name; Spring '25+ interaction with My Domain authentication policies. |
| RESEARCHED | private-connect-setup | Private Connect: AWS PrivateLink for Salesforce, inbound/outbound connections, VPC endpoint setup, DNS config. NOT for standard Named Credentials. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Secure Cross-Cloud Integrations with Private Connect (sf.private_connect_overview.htm); Considerations for Private Connect with AWS (sf.private_connect_considerations.htm); Establish Inbound/Outbound Connections with AWS (sf.private_connect_inbound_aws.htm; sf.private_connect_outbound_aws.htm)]. Key: Private Connect is add-on licensed (one license per AWS region = one inbound + one outbound connection + 5 GB/day data transfer); inbound = AWS-to-Salesforce via PrivateLink VPC endpoint with customer-managed DNS; outbound = Salesforce Apex/Flow/External Services calling into customer VPC via NLB-backed endpoint service; hard 56.48 GB/hour traffic limit; only Full Copy and Partial Copy sandboxes supported (Developer/Developer Pro excluded); requires Hyperforce in target region; NOT supported for Tableau, Marketing Cloud, Commerce Cloud, or Apex Continuations. Gaps: Azure Private Link equivalent; Government Cloud Plus constraints; External Services integration pattern with outbound Private Connect. |
| TODO | zero-trust-salesforce-patterns | Zero-trust patterns: continuous verification, device trust, conditional access policies, session-level controls, event monitoring integration. NOT for basic login security. | security |
| TODO | salesforce-shield-architecture | Shield architecture: Platform Encryption + Event Monitoring + Field Audit Trail as unified compliance strategy, key management strategy, BYOK, cost planning. NOT for individual Shield feature setup. | architect |
| RESEARCHED | oauth-token-management | OAuth token lifecycle: refresh token rotation, token revocation, connected app policies, session management, token introspection. NOT for OAuth flow selection (use oauth-flows-and-connected-apps). | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Manage OAuth Access Policies for a Connected App (xcloud.connected_app_manage_oauth.htm); Revoke OAuth Tokens Programmatically (xcloud.remoteaccess_revoke_token.htm); OAuth 2.0 Refresh Token Flow (xcloud.remoteaccess_oauth_refresh_token_flow.htm); Rotate Refresh Tokens (rn_security_refresh_token_rotation.htm release=248); OpenID Connect Token Introspection (xcloud.remoteaccess_oidc_token_introspection_endpoint.htm)]. Key: Access token lifetime = min(Connected App Session Timeout, org-wide Session Settings timeout) ranging 15 min to 24 hrs; revoking access token via POST /services/oauth2/revoke terminates that session only; revoking refresh token simultaneously invalidates all outstanding access tokens issued against it. Refresh token rotation (release=248/Winter '24, enabled per Connected App) issues a new refresh token on every use and immediately invalidates consumed token — bug fix landed in release 250. Refresh token policy options: valid until revoked, valid for N days, expires after N days of inactivity (configured under App Manager > OAuth Policies). Distinct from oauth-flows-and-connected-apps (which covers flow selection, not token lifecycle). Gaps: retry semantics when client fails to receive new refresh token during rotation; whether introspection requires specific OAuth scope; refreshTokenPolicy=zero metadata value behavior. |
| DONE | security-incident-response | Security incident response in Salesforce: event monitoring alerts, transaction security actions, login anomaly detection, forensic investigation, containment steps. NOT for general security setup. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [A Primer on Forensic Investigation of Salesforce Security Incidents (salesforce.com/blog); Login Anomaly — Salesforce Help (xcloud.real_time_em_threat_detection_login_anomaly.htm); Transaction Security Benefits and Use Cases — Trailhead; Real-Time Event and Transaction Security Monitoring — Trailhead]. Key: Event Monitoring (Shield add-on required for full 30-day retention and 70+ event types; free tier: 5 types, 1-day retention) is the primary forensic visibility layer — investigators query EventLogFile via SOQL+REST and LoginHistory (free, 6-month retention including source IP, country, MFA outcome, login type). Transaction Security Policies provide real-time containment: enforcement actions are Block, MFA/2FA challenge, Notification (email to admin), and End Session — configured via Enhanced Condition Builder (no Apex needed, Spring '21+) or legacy Apex PolicyCondition interface. LoginAnomaly is a native ML-flagged threat-detection event type (distinct from manual LoginHistory querying). Containment sequence: preserve evidence -> freeze/lock account -> revoke active sessions (Setup > Session Management or delete AuthSession) -> rotate credentials -> remove unauthorized OAuth tokens/connected apps -> eradicate backdoors -> restore data integrity. Gaps: LoginAnomaly object field schema; Salesforce-documented incident response SLA; org-freeze/read-only containment options. |

### 20d — Flow Gaps

> Domain folder: `flow`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| DONE | process-builder-to-flow-migration | Process Builder to Flow migration: conversion tool, pattern mapping, order-of-execution changes, testing migrated flows, bulk behavior differences. NOT for building new flows. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Move Processes and Workflows to Flow Builder with the Migrate to Flow Tool (platform.flow_migrate_to_flow.htm); Migrate to Flow Tool Considerations (platform.migrate_to_flow_tool_considerations.htm); Transition to Flow Retirement (id=000389396); Workflow Rules Retirement (id=001096524)]. Key: Salesforce provides a native 'Migrate to Flow' tool (Setup > Migrate to Flow) converting Process Builder processes to inactive record-triggered flows for review before activation; cannot handle invocable actions, scheduled actions requiring async paths, or external callout actions. Process Builder end-of-support: December 31 2025; new creation blocked Spring '25. Order-of-execution change: Process Builder ran in process creation order; flows use Flow Trigger Explorer priority integers. Bulk behavior improves: before-save Fast Field Updates ~10x faster than Process Builder; after-save flows ~50% faster. LLM anti-pattern: assuming migration is safe 1:1 automated conversion; mixing active Process Builder and Flow on same object creates unpredictable execution order. Gaps: none — official docs are thorough. |
| DONE | workflow-rule-to-flow-migration | Workflow Rule to Flow migration: field update mapping, email alert migration, outbound message alternatives, time-based workflow replacement. NOT for Process Builder migration. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Transition to Flow Retirement (id=000389396); Workflow Rules Retirement (id=001096524); Migrate to Flow Tool Considerations (sf.migrate_to_flow_tool_considerations.htm); Send an Outbound Message from Record-Triggered Flow (rn_automate_flow_builder_outbound_message.htm release=234)]. Key: Workflow Rules share Process Builder retirement — new creation blocked Spring '25, end of support December 31 2025 (existing rules continue executing but no bug fixes). Migrate to Flow tool converts field updates, email alerts, and outbound messages as Action elements; cannot handle task creation, ISCHANGED()/ISNEW() formula criteria, global variables, record-type-based criteria, or related-record field updates. Outbound messages are called as Core Actions in Flow referencing existing Outbound Message definitions (definition must exist before building the flow). Distinct from process-builder-to-flow-migration skill. Gaps: behavior of pending time-based actions in flight at cutover (release=246 note); whether outbound message core actions support same WSDL/acknowledgment semantics as legacy type. |
| RESEARCHED | flow-large-data-volume-patterns | Flow patterns for large data volumes: collection variable limits, loop optimization, Get Records performance, batch-like patterns, async invocable. NOT for Batch Apex. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [General Flow Limits (sf.flow_considerations_limit.htm); Flow Considerations (platform.flow_considerations.htm); Spring '25 release note: Enhance Flow Performance Controlling Number of Records Retrieved (release=254)]. Key: Hard SOQL governor limit for Flow is 50,000 rows per transaction — unbounded Get Records throws 'Too many query rows: 50001' in production while sandbox tests with small data pass. Spring '25 added 'All records, up to a specified limit' option on Get Records element to cap retrieval safely. Classic loop+DML anti-pattern consumes shared transaction budget — correct design: query outside loop into collection, accumulate mutations in Assignment inside loop, commit single Update Records after loop. DML cap: 150 statements and 10,000 rows modified; CPU: 10 seconds; all shared across automation in one transaction. For workloads exceeding safe Flow scope, use @InvocableMethod wrapping Queueable/Batch Apex or use record-triggered flow's async path. Gaps: Spring '25 cap behavior when underlying SOQL exceeds 50K; async path budget vs Queueable; whether 2,000-record community cap is platform-enforced or recommended only. |
| RESEARCHED | flow-dynamic-choices | Dynamic choice sets in flows: picklist sources, record choice sets, dependent choices, multi-select patterns, choice performance. NOT for screen flow design. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Flow Resource: Record Choice Set (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView - flow_ref_resources_recordchoice.htm); Picklist Choice Set Resource (flow_ref_resources_picklistchoice.htm)]. Key: Four distinct choice resource types - Static Choice, Picklist Choice Set, Record Choice Set, Collection Choice Set; Record Choice Set caps at 200 choices (first 200 records returned) and consumes one SOQL query per instance; Collection Choice Set bypasses both the 200-record cap and the database query by reusing a pre-fetched collection; Picklist Choice Set auto-updates with picklist metadata but cannot filter by record type or respect picklist dependencies. Gaps: dependent choice patterns beyond what Picklist Choice Set natively supports; multi-select picklist field behavior in non-screen flow contexts; Spring 26 updates to choice set filtering or record-type awareness. |
| RESEARCHED | flow-action-framework | Flow action framework: standard actions, custom Apex actions, external service actions, action packs, Invocable variables. NOT for Invocable Methods in Apex. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [InvocableMethod Annotation — Apex Developer Guide (apexcode/apex_classes_annotation_InvocableMethod.htm); InvocableVariable Annotation (apexcode/apex_classes_annotation_InvocableVariable.htm); Provided Flow Core Actions (platform.flow_ref_elements_actions_list.htm); Flow Element: Apex Action (sf.flow_ref_elements_apex_invocable.htm); Making Callouts from Invocable Actions (apexcode/apex_forcecom_flow_invocable_action_callout.htm)]. Key: Five action categories in Flow Builder: standard/core platform actions (Send Email, Post to Chatter, Submit for Approval), custom Apex (@InvocableMethod — input must be List<T>, output must be List<T> of same size), External Service actions (OpenAPI 2.0/3.0 via Named Credentials), subflows, and local actions (LWC). @InvocableVariable supports Apex primitives, sObjects, and List/List<List> of those types — NOT Object, Map, Set, static/final fields. For callouts from Apex actions in screen flows, callout=true modifier required on @InvocableMethod. LLM anti-pattern: generating @InvocableMethod processing a single record instead of List<T> — Flow batches records and throws runtime mismatch if output list size != input list size. Gaps: full standard core actions enumeration; action pack versioning for managed packages; callout=true behavior in auto-launched vs record-triggered flows. |
| DUPLICATE | flow-interview-debugging | Flow interview debugging: debug log analysis, flow interview records, fault email interpretation, flow version troubleshooting. NOT for Flow Builder debug mode. | Covered by skills/flow/flow-debugging — near-complete duplicate (fault email interpretation, Interview Log analysis, debug log review, flow version troubleshooting all covered v1.0.0 2026-04-04). Only delta is Apex-log-to-flow correlation when flow is invoked from Apex and Event Monitoring fallback when Interview Log entries are purged after 7 days. |

| RESEARCHED | lwc-internationalization | LWC internationalization: @salesforce/i18n, locale-aware formatting, custom labels, translation management, RTL support, number/date/currency formatting. NOT for Translation Workbench admin. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Internationalization — LWC Developer Guide (create-i18n); Labels — LWC Developer Guide (create-labels); @salesforce Modules Reference (reference-salesforce-modules)]. Key: @salesforce/i18n provides ~30 read-only locale-context properties (lang, dir, locale, timeZone, currency, number/dateTime format strings) reflecting running user's org settings — does NOT provide translated strings; @salesforce/label/namespace.labelName is the separate mechanism for translated strings via Translation Workbench. RTL: read @salesforce/i18n/dir (returns 'rtl' or 'ltr') and apply directional CSS manually — no automatic layout flip. Use JavaScript Intl.NumberFormat/Intl.DateTimeFormat with @salesforce/i18n values or delegate to base components (lightning-formatted-number, lightning-formatted-date-time) which auto-adapt. LLM anti-pattern: hardcoding locale strings like new Intl.NumberFormat('en-US') which breaks for non-US users. Gaps: LWR-specific i18n limitations (@salesforce/i18n currency/number.currencySymbol unsupported on LWR sites); local dev server hardcodes @salesforce/i18n values to en-US masking locale bugs in Jest and local dev. |
| RESEARCHED | lwc-drag-and-drop | Drag-and-drop patterns in LWC: HTML5 drag API, sortable lists, kanban boards, file drop zones, cross-component drag. NOT for Lightning App Builder drag-and-drop. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [LWC Developer Guide - Shadow DOM (create-dom.html); LWC Developer Guide - DOM Access Containment (locker-dom.html); LWC Developer Guide - Event Propagation (events-propagation.html)]. Key: HTML5 drag events work in LWC within single component shadow root but cross-component drag hits shadow DOM event re-targeting - event.target resolves to host element; use event.composedPath() to walk real path; Lightning Web Security (default Spring 22+) enforces DOM containment so document.querySelector is blocked - use this.template.querySelector; DataTransfer string payloads are safest cross-boundary channel; file drop zones via lightning-input type='file' cap at 3.5 MB per file. Gaps: touch-drag support on mobile - HTML5 drag API does not fire on touch; pointer-events polyfill needed for Salesforce Mobile App and Experience Cloud mobile. |
| RESEARCHED | lwc-virtualized-lists | Virtualized/windowed lists in LWC: rendering large datasets, lazy loading, infinite scroll, virtual DOM patterns, dataset pagination. NOT for standard lightning-datatable. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Improve Datatable Performance - LWC Guide (data-table-performance.html); LWC Performance Best Practices - developer.salesforce.com/blogs]. Key: No first-party virtual-windowing API in LWC - must hand-build: track render window of N items in JS state, use IntersectionObserver or scroll sentinel to shift window, recycle DOM nodes (official guidance: 'don't support creation of infinite list items'); items need stable unique key; for SOQL-backed lazy loading use LIMIT/OFFSET or GraphQL cursor pagination capped at 50 rows per page; 1000 rows/5 columns is benchmark before datatable performance degrades; lightning-datatable enable-infinite-loading is out of scope for this skill. Gaps: IntersectionObserver nuances inside Lightning shadow DOM; whether any first-party virtual-list base component added in recent releases. |

### 20f — Tableau / Analytics Connectors

> Domain folder: varies

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| TODO | tableau-salesforce-connector | Tableau Desktop/Cloud connector to Salesforce: data source setup, live vs extract, join patterns, custom SQL, incremental refresh. NOT for CRM Analytics. | integration |
| TODO | tableau-embedding-in-lightning | Embedding Tableau dashboards in Lightning: Tableau Viz LWC, Connected App auth, URL parameters, SSO, cross-filtering. NOT for CRM Analytics dashboards. | lwc |
| RESEARCHED | crm-analytics-security-predicates | CRM Analytics security predicates: row-level security, predicate syntax, multi-level predicates, team-based access, performance impact. NOT for standard sharing rules. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Analytics Security Implementation Guide Spring '26 (sf.bi_security_implementation_guide.htm); Add Row-Level Security with a Security Predicate (analytics.bi_security_datasets_predicate_considerations.htm); Predicate Expression Syntax for Datasets (analytics.bi_security_datasets_predicate_syntax.htm); Sample Predicate Expressions (analytics.bi_security_datasets_predicate_sampleexpressions.htm); Values in a Predicate Expression (sf.bi_security_datasets_predicate_values.htm)]. Key: Security predicates are SAQL filter strings stored at dataset level (NOT dashboard/lens level) using syntax 'DatasetColumn' operator value with comparison operators (==, !=, <, <=, >, >=), logical operators (&& ||), and matches (regex-style); built-in $User.* variables (Id, UserRoleId, ProfileId, Name, any custom User field) resolve to running user at query time and cannot be overridden. Predicate is invisibly appended to EVERY query against the dataset across all consuming lenses, dashboards, and REST API — only system permission View All Data bypasses predicates. Multi-level/team-based predicates require embedding an entitlement or role-expansion dataset via Flatten+Augment step in dataflow/recipe at build time — predicates CANNOT join to another dataset at query time; predicate character limit is 5,000 characters. Complex predicates with many branches add measurable query latency as filter evaluates server-side against every row. LLM anti-pattern: assuming predicates can reference other datasets at query time (they cannot — expansion must happen at ETL/recipe time). Gaps: performance benchmarks at scale; getSecurityCoverageDatasetVersion REST API audit endpoint; Opportunity Team-specific predicate syntax. |

| RESEARCHED | devops-center-advanced | DevOps Center advanced: work items, change tracking, pipeline stages, conflict resolution, org comparison, vs SFDX tradeoffs. Sources: [DevOps Center - Conflict Detection and Resolution (sf.devops_center_promotion_conflict_detection.htm); Merge Conflict Prevention Tools (platform.devops_center_mcp_intro.htm); DevOps Center for Hybrid Teams blog (developer.salesforce.com)]. Key: ~70% overlap with existing devops/devops-center-pipeline skill (work items, pipeline stages, bundle promotion, conflict resolution); distinct uncovered scope: org comparison/environment diff (comparing two orgs for drift outside promotion context) and Merge Conflict Prevention (MCP) tooling; DevOps Center uses Metadata API internally (not sf deploy), surfaces no CLI deploy logs, does not support unlocked packages or namespace-scoped metadata, cannot be mixed with CLI deployments without diverging source tracking state. Gaps: org compare/environment diff feature ('Salesforce DevOps Center org compare'); MCP tools feature set via 'Salesforce DevOps Center merge conflict prevention site:help.salesforce.com'. |
| DONE | salesforce-cli-automation | Salesforce CLI (sf/sfdx) automation: scripting patterns, CI/CD commands, data export/import, org management, plugin ecosystem. NOT for VS Code extensions. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Salesforce CLI Command Reference — sf unified (sfdx_cli_reference/cli_reference_unified.htm); sf v2 Is Here blog (developer.salesforce.com/blogs/2023/07/salesforce-cli-sf-v2-is-here); Migrate sfdx-Style Commands to sf Equivalents (cli_reference_migrate.htm); data Commands Reference (cli_reference_data_commands_unified.htm)]. Key: sf (v2) is the unified actively-developed CLI superseding sfdx — all new features ship exclusively in sf; sfdx receives only security patches. CI/CD pipelines must install sf only (installing both causes failure). Core commands: sf project deploy start (replaces sfdx force:source:deploy), sf apex run test, sf data tree export/import (small-batch relational), sf data bulk (large dataset moves between orgs), sf org login jwt (non-interactive auth). All scripting must use --json and parse only stdout — human-readable output is not deprecation-protected. LLM anti-pattern: using sfdx-style commands in new CI/CD scripts (deprecated, no new capabilities); parsing human-readable CLI text via sed/awk (breaks across CLI version updates). Gaps: plugin ecosystem depth (@salesforce/plugin-packaging, community plugin authoring). |
| DONE | code-review-checklist-salesforce | Salesforce code review checklist: governor limits, CRUD/FLS, injection, bulk patterns, test coverage, naming conventions, architectural compliance. NOT for security-only review. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide — Trigger and Bulk Request Best Practices (apexcode/apex_triggers_bestpract.htm); Running Apex within Governor Execution Limits (apexcode/apex_limits_tips.htm); Naming Conventions (apexcode/apex_classes_naming_conventions.htm); Code Coverage Best Practices (apexcode/apex_code_coverage_best_pract.htm)]. Key: Seven review categories: (1) governor limit compliance — no SOQL/DML in loops, 100 SOQL/150 DML sync limits; (2) bulk pattern correctness — triggers must handle 200 records without per-record queries; (3) CRUD/FLS enforcement — WITH USER_MODE or Security.stripInaccessible() on every query/DML; (4) test quality — 75% minimum/90%+ target, real assertions not coverage inflation, @testSetup factory, System.runAs() for sharing tests; (5) naming conventions per Apex Developer Guide; (6) sharing keyword intentionality — every class/trigger must explicitly declare with sharing/without sharing/inherited sharing; (7) architectural compliance — single-trigger-per-object handler, no logic in trigger body. Overlaps with secure-coding-review-checklist on CRUD/FLS only; distinct on governor limits, bulk, naming, architecture. Related skills: devops/salesforce-code-analyzer (automated enforcement), apex/trigger-framework (architectural compliance). LLM anti-pattern: reviewing trigger code for injection without checking if it processes Trigger.new as a 200-record collection — misses SOQL-in-loop that hits 100-query limit under bulk load. Gaps: Well-Architected explicit Apex review rubric beyond Trusted pillar. |

### 20h — Admin & Architect Gaps

> Domain folder: varies

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| RESEARCHED | large-data-volume-architecture | Large data volume (LDV) architecture: skinny tables, custom indexes, query optimization, archival strategy, sharing performance at scale. NOT for individual SOQL tuning. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Salesforce Large Data Volumes Best Practices (ldv_deployments_introduction.htm); LDV Best Practices: Indexes (ldv_deployments_infrastructure_indexes.htm)]. Key: LDV issues begin at 100K+ records (non-selective query risk on tables >200K in Apex triggers); standard indexed fields used when filters match <30% of first million records (<=15% for additional records, capped at 1M rows); custom indexed fields require <10% of total records or <=333,333 rows absolute ceiling. Skinny tables are read-only physical column subsets (max 200 columns) eliminating join overhead on wide objects — must be requested via Salesforce Support case, available on Account/Contact/Opportunity/Lead/Case and custom objects, not applicable to formula/roll-up/encrypted fields, only copied to Full sandboxes. Sharing recalculation is non-incremental — any ownership reassignment triggers full recalculation across all records owned by affected users; ownership skew (>10K records per owner) is the primary performance lever. Related skill high-volume-sales-data-architecture covers Account/Opportunity specifically — this skill is broader (any object/domain). Gaps: archival via External Objects/Salesforce Connect; Data Cloud vs Big Objects at extreme scale; Async SOQL batch limits; Divisions feature (>1M records, >35 licenses). |
| DUPLICATE | event-driven-salesforce-architecture | Event-driven architecture in Salesforce: Platform Events, CDC, Pub/Sub API, event bus patterns, eventual consistency, saga pattern. NOT for individual event implementation. | Covered by skills/architect/event-driven-architecture AND skills/integration/event-driven-architecture-patterns. Together these cover Platform Events vs CDC vs Pub/Sub API use cases, event bus pattern selection (Pub/Sub/Fanout/Passed Messages/Streaming/Queuing), choreography vs orchestration decision, and eventual consistency tradeoffs. Saga pattern gap (no official Salesforce doc) can be added to existing skills. |
| RESEARCHED | migration-architecture-patterns | Org migration architecture: org merge, org split, data migration strategy, metadata migration, cutover planning, coexistence patterns. NOT for go-live cutover. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Enterprise Architecture: Multi-org Strategy (developer.salesforce.com/blogs); How to Prepare for a Salesforce Org Migration (help.salesforce.com/s/articleView?id=000386897); Data 360 Provisioning Decision Guide (architect.salesforce.com/decision-guides)]. Key: Org merge requires pre-migration metadata audit (objects/fields/picklists/validation rules/automation) before any data movement - skipping this is the most common LLM anti-pattern (also in skills/architect/multi-org-strategy llm-anti-patterns.md Anti-Pattern 5); org split must distinguish 'why' (regulatory isolation, M&A, limits relief) from 'how' (metadata fork point, data partitioning, coexistence via Salesforce Connect External Objects or Platform Events); coexistence requires identity/SSO continuity, duplicate detection, and rollback-safe metadata deployment windows; distinct from skills/architect/multi-org-strategy (decision only). Gaps: official architect.salesforce.com guide for CRM org merge/split execution lifecycle; cutover sequencing patterns (freeze window, parallel-run, hard-cutover); record ID remapping when external systems reference org-specific 15/18-digit IDs; Hyperforce region constraints. |
| TODO | tenant-isolation-patterns | Multi-tenant isolation: custom metadata per-tenant, permission-based feature gating, data partitioning, namespace isolation, ISV patterns. NOT for multi-org strategy. | architect |
| TODO | composable-commerce-architecture | Composable commerce on Salesforce: headless API layer, micro-frontends, BFF pattern, CDN strategy, third-party composability. NOT for standard storefront. | architect |
| TODO | nonprofit-cloud-vs-npsp-migration | Nonprofit Cloud (NPC) vs NPSP decision and migration: feature comparison, data model differences, migration path, timeline, coexistence. NOT for NPSP admin. | architect |
| DONE | data-loader-and-tools | Data Loader, Workbench, Salesforce Inspector, and third-party tools: when to use each, configuration, common pitfalls, limits. NOT for Bulk API development. | Researched 2026-04-16. Sources: [Data Loader Guide v66.0 Spring '26 (local knowledge/imports); When to Use Data Loader (sf.loader_when_to_use.htm); Configure Data Loader/Enable Bulk API (sf.loader_configuring_bulk_api.htm); Replacement Tools for Workbench (platform.replacement_workbench_tools.htm)]. Key: Data Loader (v66.0, Spring '26) is a desktop application (macOS+Windows) supporting up to 150M records via Bulk API 2.0; SOAP API import batch max 200 records, Bulk API v1 max 10,000 per batch, Bulk API 2.0 manages batch size automatically. Data Import Wizard (browser-based, native) preferred for loads under 50,000 records on supported objects. Workbench (workbench.developerforce.com) is a Salesforce-hosted browser-based web tool for REST/SOAP Explorer, SOQL/SOSL, and small-scale DML — official replacement guidance points to Code Builder, VS Code Extensions, and Salesforce CLI REST Explorer (Workbench is in sunset trajectory). Salesforce Inspector and Salesforce Inspector Reloaded are open-source Chrome extensions (NOT official Salesforce products) for record inspection and small exports only. 'Bulk API Hard Delete' permission required separately for hard-delete operations regardless of API mode. Gaps: exact Workbench retirement date; official stance on Inspector Reloaded; Data Import Wizard object list and field count limits. |
| DUPLICATE | formula-field-performance | Formula field performance at scale: compiled size limits, cross-object references, SOQL context, caching behavior, alternatives for complex logic. NOT for formula syntax. | Covered by skills/apex/formula-field-performance-and-limits. Compiled size limits (5,000 compiled characters), cross-object spanning (max 10 unique relationships per object, never indexable), SOQL indexability (formula fields require Support case for custom index on deterministic formulas), LDV full table scan behavior, and materialization pattern already covered. Admin-framing content can be added to existing skill's well-architected.md. |
| RESEARCHED | report-type-strategy | Custom report types: object relationships, cross-filter design, bucketing, matrix reports, joined reports, analytics snapshots. NOT for dashboard design. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Custom Report Types (sf.reports_report_type_setup); Joined Report Limits (analytics.reports_unavailable_with_joined_reports); Cross Filter Considerations (sf.reports_cross_filters_overview); Reporting Snapshots (analytics.data_about_analytic_snap)]. Key: Joined reports cap at 5 blocks and 2000 rows per block and cannot be used directly in dashboards - LLMs ignore these limits; custom report types support up to 4 object levels and 1000 fields per CRT; analytics snapshots run on scheduled job mapping source summary/matrix report to target custom object - snapshot does NOT run in real time, fails silently if field mappings break after schema changes. NOTE: overlap with existing admin/reports-and-dashboards skills - scope strictly to CRT object-relationship modeling and analytics snapshot operational setup. Gaps: none on core topics. |
| RESEARCHED | email-deliverability-monitoring | Email deliverability monitoring: bounce management, SPF/DKIM/DMARC, compliance BCC, Salesforce email logs, relay configuration. NOT for email template design. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Enable Email Bounce Handling (sales.emailadmin_bounce_enable); Compliance BCC Emails (sales.admin_compliancebcc); Set Up Email Relay (sales.email_relay); Salesforce SPF and DKIM FAQ (000389240); Deliverability Settings Guidelines (sales.emailadmin_deliverability)]. Key: Distinct from existing email-deliverability-strategy skill (Marketing Cloud only) - this covers Salesforce Core org monitoring; bounce management is opt-in and populates EmailBouncedDate/EmailBouncedReason on Lead/Contact but does NOT auto-suppress records (orgs must build flow/list filter automation); email log files at Setup > Email > Email Log Files have 30-day retention and 7-day max per request; SPF requires adding include:_spf.salesforce.com to DNS TXT record; DKIM keys generated at Setup > Email > DKIM Keys (2048-bit recommended); relay requires TLS Required-Verifying + bounce management disabled to avoid Return-Path conflicts. Gaps: Compliance BCC for Flow/Apex-sent emails; relay interaction with DMARC alignment; whether Summer 25/Spring 26 changed the 30-day log retention cap. |
| TODO | flow-orchestration-admin | Flow Orchestration admin: stage configuration, step assignment, background steps, interactive steps, evaluation flows, work items. NOT for Flow Orchestration development. | admin |

Key: Finalizer runs in separate Apex transaction with full governor limits after parent Queueable completes; only one Finalizer per Queueable via System.attachFinalizer(); FinalizerContext provides getJobId(), getResult() (SUCCESS or UNHANDLED_EXCEPTION), getException(); Finalizer may enqueue exactly one additional Queueable. NOTE: ~60-70% overlap with existing apex/apex-queueable-patterns - scope this skill to advanced Finalizer-only patterns not there: multi-hop recovery, governor edge cases, error message taxonomy (apex_transaction_finalizers_error_messages.htm). Gaps: Finalizer chaining across multi-hop recovery; error message taxonomy verification. |

## Phase 21 — LLM-Frequent: Patterns, Migrations, Tooling, Tribal Knowledge

> Skills targeting the most common questions LLMs receive from Salesforce practitioners.
> These are the "I ask ChatGPT/Claude this every week" topics with zero repo coverage.

### 21a — Apex Patterns LLMs Get Asked Daily

> Domain folder: `apex`

| Status | Skill Name | Description | Notes |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------|
| RESEARCHED | apex-collections-patterns | Map<Id, List<SObject>> construction, nested maps, Set intersection, collection-based trigger patterns, Map.containsKey guard patterns. NOT for basic Apex syntax. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide - Collections (langCon_apex_collections); Apex Reference Guide - Map Class (apex_methods_system_map)]. Key: Collections are heap-allocated against 6 MB heap limit; nesting Map<Id, List<SObject>> is idiomatic for bulkified triggers but inner List allocations add to heap - LLMs frequently generate unbounded accumulation in Database.Stateful batch classes; Map.get() returns null (not exception) so Map.containsKey() guard is required; Set intersection via retainAll() mutates receiver - a common LLM anti-pattern is building new Set in a loop instead of calling retainAll(). Gaps: putAll(List<SObject>) Id-keying semantics; custom sort via Comparator interface (Spring 24+) well-architected guidance. |
| RESEARCHED | apex-json-serialization | JSON.serialize, JSON.deserialize, JSON.deserializeUntyped, JSON.createParser, wrapper class DTO patterns, API response mapping. NOT for callout patterns (use callouts-and-http-integrations). | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Apex Developer Guide: JSON Support (apexcode/apex_methods_system_json_overview.htm); Apex Reference Guide: JSON Class (apexref/apex_class_System_Json.htm)]. Key: JSON.serialize(obj, suppressApexObjectNulls) omits null fields when second arg is true - LLMs routinely omit this flag and produce bloated payloads; JSON.deserialize throws TypeException if JSON shape doesn't match Apex type (extra fields tolerated but wrong type on matching field is fatal); JSON.deserializeUntyped returns Object requiring manual casting at every level - typed wrapper DTOs strongly preferred. Gaps: heap consumption for payloads >1 MB and createParser streaming API limits; whether suppressApexObjectNulls applies to nested objects/collections. |
| TODO | apex-string-and-regex | String methods (substringBefore, split, replaceAll), Pattern/Matcher regex, text parsing, template rendering, safe null handling. NOT for formula functions. | apex |
| RESEARCHED | apex-dml-patterns | Database.insert(records, false) partial success, SaveResult/UpsertResult handling, allOrNone patterns, Database.merge, convertLead. NOT for trigger framework. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [DML Statements vs. Database Class Methods - Apex Developer Guide (langCon_apex_dml_database); SaveResult/UpsertResult Classes - Apex Reference Guide (apexref)]. Key: Database.insert/update/delete/upsert accept allOrNone Boolean (default true); false enables partial success requiring per-row SaveResult.isSuccess()/getErrors() - failure on one row does NOT roll back the batch; Database.merge (Account/Contact/Lead only) returns MergeResult; Database.convertLead has no allOrNone variant and throws on failure; DML counts against 150-statement and 10000-row limits regardless of keyword vs Database method form. LLM anti-pattern: naked DML keywords in bulk contexts instead of Database.insert(records, false) with error inspection. Gaps: Database.merge under different OWD; convertLead with duplicate rules; DMLOptions.DuplicateRuleHeader with allOrNone=false. |
| RESEARCHED | apex-soql-relationship-queries | Parent-to-child subqueries, child-to-parent dot notation, polymorphic SOQL (TYPEOF), multi-level relationships, relationship naming conventions. NOT for SOQL fundamentals (use soql-fundamentals). | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [SOQL Reference - Using Relationship Queries (sforce_api_calls_soql_relationships_query_using); Understanding Relationship Query Limitations (sforce_api_calls_soql_relationships); Apex Developer Guide - Polymorphic Relationships (langCon_apex_SOQL_polymorphic_relationships)]. Key: Child-to-parent dot notation caps at 5 levels deep and max 55 relationships per query; parent-to-child subqueries limited to 20 per query (API v58.0+ only, not Bulk API or external objects); TYPEOF counts each WHEN branch as a separate relationship against the 55-limit; dot notation inside a subquery SELECT list is invalid - a frequent LLM error. Gaps: TYPEOF with dynamic SOQL and WITH USER_MODE enforcement; multi-level parent-to-child in Bulk API 2.0. |
| RESEARCHED | apex-aggregate-queries | GROUP BY, HAVING, AggregateResult handling, COUNT(), SUM(), AVG(), rollup patterns with aggregate SOQL, aggregate limitations. NOT for roll-up summary fields. | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Aggregate Functions - SOQL and SOSL Reference (sforce_api_calls_soql_select_agg_functions); Working with SOQL Aggregate Functions - Apex Developer Guide (langCon_apex_SOQL_agg_fns); GROUP BY Considerations (sforce_api_calls_soql_select_group_by_considerations)]. Key: AggregateResult fields must be accessed via get('alias') not typed getters; aggregate queries cap at 2000 rows; GROUP BY cannot be used in inner queries and is incompatible with WITH DATA CATEGORY; COUNT() without argument cannot coexist with other SELECT fields; non-aggregated SELECT fields must appear in GROUP BY. LLM anti-pattern: SELECT Name, COUNT(Id) total FROM Account GROUP BY Name fails - COUNT() without arg cannot coexist with other fields. Gaps: GROUP BY ROLLUP/CUBE syntax; AVG() with Currency in multi-currency orgs; dynamic SOQL AggregateResult type coercion. |
| TODO | apex-schema-describe | Schema.SObjectType, Schema.DescribeFieldResult, dynamic field describe, RecordType ID retrieval, picklist values, field-level metadata at runtime. NOT for Metadata API. | apex |
| TODO | apex-enum-patterns | Enum definition and usage, enum-based dispatch, ordinal values, enum in Custom Metadata, global enums for packages, enum limitations. NOT for picklist fields. | apex |
| RESEARCHED | apex-batch-chaining | Batch job chaining via finish(), Queueable chains, hybrid batch-queueable orchestration, chain depth limits, monitoring chained jobs. NOT for single batch patterns (use batch-apex-patterns). | Researched 2026-04-17. Sources: [Using Batch Apex - Apex Developer Guide (apexcode/apex_batch_interface.htm); Queueable Apex - Apex Developer Guide (apexcode/apex_queueing_jobs.htm); FlexQueue Class - Apex Reference Guide (apexref/apex_class_System_FlexQueue.htm)]. Key: Batch chaining via finish() supported from API v26.0; Flex Queue removed old 5-concurrent-batch ceiling but chaining without FlexQueue capacity check risks silent job-queue saturation; Queueable chains have no enforced depth limit in production (Developer/Trial orgs cap at 5); AsyncOptions.MaximumQueueableStackDepth sets explicit depth guard; batch finish() can enqueue Queueable but counts against 250,000 async executions per 24h limit. LLM anti-pattern: unbounded chain loops with no depth counter or FlexQueue capacity check. Gaps: FlexQueue.moveBeforeJob reordering semantics; AsyncOptions behavior from batch finish() context. |
| TODO | apex-limits-monitoring | Limits class methods (Limits.getQueries(), getHeapSize()), transaction budget tracking, proactive limit avoidance, limit-safe patterns. NOT for governor limits concepts (use governor-limits). | apex |
| TODO | apex-jwt-bearer-flow | JWT bearer token flow: certificate-based auth, server-to-server integration, Connected App JWT setup, token exchange, headless auth. NOT for OAuth interactive flows. | apex |
| TODO | apex-wrapper-class-patterns | Wrapper/DTO classes: SelectOption replacement, display wrappers, API response wrappers, inner class patterns, Comparable implementation. NOT for JSON serialization (use apex-json-serialization). | apex |

## Phase 22 — LLM-Frequent II: Dev Primitives, Admin Workflows, Debugging

> The "every developer asks this weekly" and "every admin Googles this monthly" layer.
> These are the atomic building blocks that LLMs need to answer correctly before they can compose higher-level guidance.

---

## Anti-Patterns (Do Not Do These)

- Do not create a skill for a Cloud × Role cell before verifying no duplicate exists.
- Do not write content from memory. Every factual claim needs an official source.
- Do not create overlapping skills. Always run search_knowledge.py first.
- Do not hand-edit registry/, vector_index/, or docs/SKILLS.md.
- Do not mark DONE until validate_repo.py exits 0.
- Do not skip the query fixture step. Skills with no fixture produce a WARN that fails CI.
